If the afflicted receive the rites of the Three Caverns’ Dharma Masters, these ghosts shall be seized by the heavenly beings and taken away. Should they refuse to depart, the celestial enforcers of the Three Heavens shall surely behead them.

The Dao speaks: Within the Three Realms, the Great Demon King commands thirty-six lesser kings, each ruling forty-eight billion lesser kings, who in turn command countless great soldiers. They roam the world under Our oath: to govern the common folk justly, never to wrongfully harm the innocent, nor bring misfortune through malevolent haunting. From this day forth, wherever there is urgent illness, official peril, or distress, you shall attend to them, lend your power to their fortune, resolve disputes, and ensure that rulers, ministers, and all evil ghosts are made joyful. Let illness be cured, official matters resolved, clans harmonious, the realm at peace, the Five Grains abundant, rulers and people rejoicing, demonic soldiers subdued, and all free from sickness and pain, with every wish fulfilled.

Should you achieve this, the ghost-kings shall ascend, and all heavenly beings shall rejoice. But if you allow untimely winds and rains, failed harvests, unrest among the people, tyranny from rulers, unresolved disputes, or unhealed illness, then you, the Great Demon Kings and their consorts, along with the hundred billion ghost-kings, shall all be beheaded.

Thus concludes *Scroll Seven of the Most High’s Cavernous Abyss Divine Incantations Sutra*.
*Scroll Eight of the Most High’s Cavernous Abyss Divine Incantations Sutra* begins.

**Summoning Ghosts Chapter**

The Dao spoke: Within the Three Realms, those who believe in the sutras are rare indeed. Thus, worthy persons are not born, and many evil people gather and multiply. When there are those who believe in the Dharma and uphold the sutras, they come from Heaven above. The calamity of *jiashen* brings Heaven’s welcome to the Daoists. It does not welcome sinners, for sinners do not believe in the Dharma and are thus not received.

In the years *renwu* and *gengchen*, plague ghosts and weapons will slaughter people, leaving few alive in the world. During times of illness, if a Master of the Three Caverns performs the turning of sutras and the Daoist rites, the Heavenly Worthy will summon the great deities of the ten directions, causing sickness to be cured and official matters to resolve themselves. Should they disobey this command, the ghost-kings shall be the first to be punished.

The Dao spoke: In the year *xinsi*, there will be a ghost named *Duluna*, standing three *zhang* tall, with eyes slanting and mouth askew, ears six *cun* long, wielding an iron staff. It will roam among people, striking down the wicked. Plagues, epidemics, and official troubles will be accompanied by sixty-nine thousand ghosts. Some will take the form of great crows; where these crows pass, people will all fall ill and die, beyond cure. By the year *renchen*, the people will be greatly afflicted, and by *jiashen*, they will perish entirely. If the kingdom’s Dharma Masters can govern this, performing the turning of sutras and Daoist rites, the great armies of the Three Heavens will come to protect them, sparing them from harm.

Daoists transform people, causing them to receive the Three Caverns’ sutras. The Dao spoke: As *jiashen* approaches, ghostly soldiers will slaughter people, and forty-nine thousand *Wuxuan* warriors will traverse the realm. Wherever a Master of the Three Caverns turns the sutras and practices the rites of the Three and Five, each will be guarded, preventing evil ghosts from drawing near. Evil ghosts will flee far away, aiding the Daoist in enlightening the foolish. If kings, emperors, regional lords, officials of two thousand *shi*, magistrates, nobles, or common folk uphold the Three Caverns, they shall later obtain great blessings, their fortune extending to their descendants for generations without end. They will be born among heavenly beings and humans, always encountering sages, never becoming the poor, and never forsaken by emperors, ever assisting the sovereign.

The Dao spoke: In the world’s wicked places, good people are not born. If there are now noble and virtuous people, they come from Heaven above. Why is this? Evil people do not believe in the Great Dharma, nor do they understand the sutras’ words. Though they may have been born human, their past lives held little fortune, and now, though they are nobles with wealth, they do not recognize the Dharma’s canon, having no affinity with it. These are sinners indeed. I know this well: worldly official glory is like morning dew—when the sun rises, it dries up. Glory does not last long; in an instant, one dies. It is better to study immortality, which stands firm for ten thousand kalpas.

The Dao spoke: Daoists transform people, causing them to uphold the Three Caverns, and soon they will ascend. If there are illnesses or official troubles, turning the sutras brings great fortune. Wherever this is done, plague ghosts will die of themselves. Exert yourselves to encourage one another.

The Dao spoke: Since the year *wuyin*, there has been a great ghost with a red nose, named *Fuzi*, nine *chi* tall, with three faces and one eye. There is also a ghost with two heads and one body, three *chi* tall, each with red eyes. Another ghost, named *Daye*, has three heads and one body, seven *chi* tall. Countless in number, they wield white blades, roaming the world to seize children. They travel among the clouds, their bloated forms emitting red *qi*, causing people to suffer chills and fever, vomiting blood, heart distension, and broken *qi* in the ribs. At such times, if a Master of the Three Caverns comes to turn the sutras, the sick will recover, and official matters will resolve themselves. If they do not recover, the ghost-kings shall be the first to be punished.

The Dao spoke: From now until the year *gengchen*, there will be thirty-six thousand evil ghosts named *Tianchi*, accompanied by thirty thousand followers, roaming the world and wrongfully killing the good. By the year *renwu*, another three thousand nine hundred red-headed ghosts, named *Datou*, will descend to slaughter people. Weapons will clash throughout the world—it cannot be endured for long. Disasters and rebellions will arise in all directions, and the Six Barbarians will perish entirely. The Daoist Dharma will flourish, while the secular world will decline. In the year *jiashen*, the people will die out.

To know how to survive these calamities, only those who uphold the Three Caverns, revere their masters, and honor the sutras will be protected by heavenly deities and thus ascend to Heaven, where heavenly beings will welcome them.

The Dao spoke: By the year *renwu*, the world will be in turmoil. The common people will suffer hardship, and the Six Barbarians will invade one another. The people will be restless, and men and women will flee in chaos. The lands of Shu and Han will be vast, and the people will suddenly perish. Daoists will enter the mountains to cultivate the Three Caverns and meet the Perfected Lords. The Perfected Lords are not far off—this will occur between *renchen* and *renwu*.

From now on, Heaven will slay the foolish, but Daoists will save them, preserving their lives. The Dao spoke: In the year *renwu*, there will be eighty thousand lowly ghosts named *Dadan*, each three *chi* and six *cun* tall, accompanied by thirty-nine billion companions. They will wield red staffs, roaming among people to kill the wicked. There will also be white crows, as large as cartwheels, flying in the millions. They will enter people’s homes and kill their children. If people see them, or if large fish die in the water and people eat them, they will die. If deer die in the wilderness and people eat them, they too will die. Daoists who uphold this sutra and teach others will prevent heavenly beings from violating these prohibitions.

The Dao spoke: The world’s fate is nearing its end, and the waters will soon rise. Men and women will all perish, except for those who uphold the Three Caverns—they alone will be preserved. From now on, wherever Daoists save people from official troubles and illnesses, four hundred thousand heavenly maidens will descend to assist, sparing them from misfortune. Daoists, diligently transform the people.

The Dao spoke: The great kalpa is approaching, and the people are mostly foolish, unaware of the coming disasters. Daoists who first see this text must urgently transform the people, causing them to enter the Three Caverns.

The followers of the Three Caverns will be welcomed by heavenly beings—this sacred teaching does not speak in vain.

The Dao spoke: The great kalpa draws near, and the people will undergo transformation. Heaven and earth were established, and Daoists transform the people. Those who do not believe differ not from the six livestock. The Most High pities you, moved by compassion. Alas, alas! Sentient beings, deluded and attached, do not seek liberation on their own; clinging to ignorance until death, what can be done for them? Summon the great deities of the ten directions and the Daoists of the Three Caverns to transform the foolish, that they may know the scriptural Dharma—such merit is boundless.

If Daoists enter the mountains to still their minds but do not transform others, this is without merit. The Dao spoke: If Daoists wish to deliver themselves, they should enter the renowned mountains. Those who wish to deliver all people should remain among the foolish, that they may be liberated. If Daoists enter the mountains, the mountain paths are profoundly remote, and worldly people will not see them, left without refuge. Though their original intention remains, there is no means to deliver others. Thus, wise Daoists need not remain in the mountains.

The Dao spoke: Unless one is a Dharma Master of the Three Caverns, one must not recklessly recite this sutra. Why is this so?

Here follows the translation:

Within this sutra are recorded the names of all great demon kings who slay ghosts and govern the people. Those who receive this scriptural Dharma shall themselves attain deliverance, each storing it in a single casket. Should any suffer official disputes, imprisonment, grave illness, or prolonged affliction, perform a one-day-and-night purification rite, and I shall summon the hundred ghosts to interrogate them, that the sick may recover before they are released.

You Daoists, diligently transform the myriad people. Wherever a Daoist who has received the scriptures treats illness, the great demon kings and lesser ghost kings shall assist in healing. When the sick recover, you shall ascend in rank, and I shall never fail my word. From this day forward, I make this covenant with you, the great demon kings.

The Dao spoke: From this jiǎchén year onward, three hundred sixty thousand black ghosts shall spread dysentery and bloody flux, and ghostly children shall come by night to slay men. The ghosts of the Six Barbarians, numbering in the millions, often take the forms of women or elders, entering homes to seize infants and causing livestock to die suddenly. The state neglects its people, and the populace scatters. High ministers and petty officials wrongfully take lives. In such times, ghostly soldiers bring chaos and disease.

You Daoists, simply perform the rites and recite the scriptures for one day and one night. I shall dispatch three hundred sixty thousand celestial soldiers from the Three Heavens to summon the ghosts of the ten directions and question them. Which ghosts afflict the people? Each shall be examined, and good and evil separated. The celestial soldiers shall execute them, exterminating their kindred, and show no mercy.

Swiftly, swiftly, in accordance with the oral command of the Most High.

The Dao spoke: The mountain and forest ghosts, named Xuánzǐdū, command twenty-nine million ghosts. They commonly cause sudden death, slaying infants and elders, entering homes to frighten chickens, dogs, and children. There are also thirty-nine thousand red-turbaned ghosts who enter homes to seize livestock. Further, eighty thousand green insect ghosts—each three feet six inches tall—constantly wield heavenly fire to burn homes, bringing official disputes and slander upon the inhabitants. There are also the great moving green ghosts, forty-nine thousand in number, each three *zhàng* tall, who wield red staffs to bludgeon the people to death.

Those who are virtuous and faithful to the Dharma shall not be harmed. But the wicked—those who lack righteousness, kill living beings, defy the Dao, neglect their parents, deceive Daoists, or revile masters and disciples—shall be executed without mercy and consigned to hell. Some shall suffer incurable illness, myriad calamities converging upon them, their agony beyond words. If Daoists do not intervene, their aid shall be of no avail.

The Dao spoke: These wicked ones disrespect their masters, defy the Dharma, slander Daoists, seclude themselves to revile their teachers, and utter their masters’ names. Their sins are grave; they shall be dragged into the Red Sand Hell, where they shall remain for ten thousand kalpas. Upon release, they shall become field-protecting crows, ever dwelling in water to guard ten thousand *qǐng* of fields. Or, before death, they shall suffer illness and torment, pain clinging to their bodies, their fields and silkworms failing, their endeavors unfulfilled, and all shall mock them. These afflictions are the retribution for their past lives’ revilement of masters and disciples.

From this day forward, should such people exist, the great demon kings shall swiftly punish them. Those who disrespect masters and disciples or do not uphold the Three Caverns shall be bound and executed without mercy by the great demon kings and lesser ghost kings.

The Dao spoke: You Daoists, in serving your masters, must be single-minded. If your hearts remain unchanged, you bring suffering upon yourselves. To slight or revile your masters is to commit the five rebellions and be unfilial, to slander the common folk, forcibly seize their wealth, teach others to do evil, or incite litigation and murder. Such people shall be seized by the great demon kings and lesser ghost kings of the Three Caverns’ scriptures and bound in the Three Heavenly Prisons. Their three *hún* and seven *pò* shall be tormented—women’s fourteen *pò* likewise—so they endure every suffering, desiring death yet unable to attain it.

You Daoists, both men and women, must deeply guard yourselves.

The Dao spoke: In the jiǎyín decade, thirty-nine thousand people shall be executed in the great purge for disrespecting their masters, wrongfully taking lives, slandering Daoists, or pointing out their masters’ names. Such people shall fall into the great purgation of blade, flood, and fire.

You Daoists and all worldly people must wholeheartedly honor masters and disciples, receive the Three Caverns’ scriptures, transform all beings, and heal the afflicted. In households where illness persists, recite the scriptures to treat them. I shall summon the great ghosts of the ten directions and all deities to question them. If they remain defiant, causing households to suffer incurable illness, unresolved official disputes, or death, the great demon kings and lesser ghost kings shall hack your bodies into ten thousand pieces without mercy.

Swiftly, swiftly, in accordance with the oral command of the Most High.

The Dao spoke: Daoists serving their masters must revere them as heaven, visiting at the four seasons and eight solar terms to inquire after their well-being. When worldly people face matters, they must act in accordance with the Dharma. If they no longer follow their masters, and their masters no longer attend them, the spirits shall not abide with them. Among people, none are greater than masters; masters are supreme and must be honored as parents. Those who slight them shall be punished by heaven and men, and the demon kings shall not save such sinners.

Swiftly, swiftly, in accordance with the oral command of the Most High.

The Dao spoke: Daoists who defy their masters shall be examined by celestial soldiers, and their descendants shall likewise fall among the ranks of common ghosts. In the gēngshēn and rénwǔ years, Daoists who slight their masters shall be executed by three hundred sixty thousand ghostly soldiers. Further, in the yǐsì year, forty-nine thousand red-nosed ghosts shall slay three hundred ninety thousand wicked people across the land. By the guǐsì year and rényín epoch, those who do not believe in the Dao or receive its scriptures shall fall into the eighteen purgations.

The wrongfully dead number thirty-nine thousand each day, yet the Most High distinguishes their fates accordingly. Should pestilence strike the land in any given year, Daoists who heal the afflicted shall see them recover. If they do not recover, the demon kings Nalü and their ilk shall rend such Daoists limb from limb, showing no mercy.

The Dao spoke: From this day forth, male and female Daoists must diligently convert the foolish of the world, urging them to receive the great scriptures of the Three Caverns. Let every person receive talismans and registers, wear their name-contracts upon their bodies, and be recorded in the Jade Calendar. Masters and disciples shall transmit the teachings in succession, allowing no disrespect. Should any violate this covenant, celestial soldiers shall execute them, annihilating their households and consigning them to plague and pestilence, where regret shall come too late.

I now dispatch thirty-six thousand crimson riders, each wielding an iron staff, to traverse the land and seize the unrighteous and the five-fold traitors. If the sick are treated by Daoists, the ghost kings shall pardon them. Should they refuse, these ghost kings shall be demoted and punished without leniency.

The Dao spoke: In the rénxū and guǐhài years, eight thousand punishing ghosts shall slay those who fail to honor the Great Dao. By the guǐwèi and jiǎchén years, one hundred twenty thousand red ghosts shall slaughter with blades and warfare—half for mocking those who receive the Dao, disturbing the hearts of others, assaulting Daoists, denying the power of the Dao, speaking falsely while harboring deceit, and slandering masters and disciples. Such sinners shall be cast into the Boiling Ash Hell, the Knife Mountain and Sword Tree, with no hope of release.

The Dao spoke: In the jǐmǎo, bǐngyín, and dīnghài years, eight thousand shall die unjustly. This befalls those who disobey the Dao’s laws, withhold celestial taxes, break vows without repayment, make empty promises, deceive ghosts and spirits to seize others’ wealth, perform no meritorious deeds, and neglect fasting and purification. Though they be Daoists, they kindle no incense, attend no rites, ignore others’ distress, and act greedily without aid. When preparing meals for their masters, they offer impure or inadequate food, or withhold it entirely. Such people shall be cast into the Great Purgation’s Water Prison, trapped for ten thousand kalpas. Even if reborn, their six senses shall be incomplete, repelling others, reduced to the level of livestock. The Great Purgation shall execute them, and the demon kings shall offer no salvation.

The Dao spoke: Great Patriarchal Masters traverse the world, witnessing the multitude’s ignorance, and thus expound the great scriptures of Samādhi. These scriptures comprise twenty scrolls, transmitted by the Most High. Those who receive them shall behold the Most High face-to-face. Without receiving the divine incantations, none may enter the mountains, nor be called true Daoists, nor heal the sick.

From this day forth, masters must first receive these scriptures, for they subdue all great demon kings, lesser ghost kings, and their wives and descendants—all aiding Daoists in converting people and healing the sick. Why? Because all demon kings, too, assist the Most High in transforming the myriad families. Let the wise and virtuous ponder my words.

The Dao spoke: You people of later generations, failing to honor the Great Dao, instead follow vulgar masters who beat drums to sacrifice to spirits, slaughtering pigs, dogs, and chickens, offering the three pure animals and grass upon the waters, summoning a hundred ghosts, and worshipping wild deities. Such practices breed chaos and evil; the spirits shall not protect you. Your kin shall be struck down, condemned by the Three Officials, subjected to myriad tortures. The dead shall not rest, returning to claim the living, causing deaths great and small, and ultimately annihilating your households. Do not blame the Dao.

The Dao spoke: Households that honor the Dao must do so with wholehearted devotion. In all endeavors, direct your thoughts single-mindedly toward the Dao. Conduct rites, burn incense, and perform the ten thousand offerings, guided by your master’s fasting and understanding. Do not invite vulgar masters or those who practice heterodox sacrifices into your homes, lest chaos arise, household spirits grow restless, and the living be punished. Such people shall grow wicked, and their families shall be destroyed. This, too, is the Dao’s teaching, awakening those who comprehend.

The Dao spoke: The world is filled with fools who see no good, recognize no law, and thus perish in great numbers. From this day forth, when someone embraces the Dao and falls gravely ill, summon these Patriarchal Masters and all Daoists to perform rites, set up altars, make offerings, and heal the afflicted. In cases of legal disputes, heaven shall dispatch celestial warriors, the Jade Maidens of the Three Heavens, and the great immortals of the ten directions to assist the Daoists, swiftly curing the sick, resolving legal matters, and fulfilling the host’s every desire. Those who act thus shall be elevated through countless ranks, and my golden words shall not be in vain.

Should the sick not recover, the Daoists’ efforts shall be in vain, and the host shall invite disaster, drawing misfortune upon themselves. The demon kings, their wives, children, and descendants, along with the ghost kings, shall execute without mercy all who fail to heal the afflicted.

The Dao spoke: All demon kings and those afflicted in this world—where Daoists heal them—shall turn and convert the host’s kin, their great ancestors, and all thirty-six generations of forebears, delivering them all. Let the host’s illness be cured, legal troubles dissolved, and every wish fulfilled. I shall summon the hundred ghosts to interrogate the spirits afflicting the sick. Each shall be reported, questioned by the Three Officials, and persuaded to relent. If they do not, they shall be seized and executed without mercy.

"Proclaim this with utmost urgency, as the oral command of the Most High, by law and decree.

The Dao spoke: From this day forward, for all who suffer illness, dispatch the Great Halberd General to lead thirty-nine hundred million red-armored cavalry, each wielding a crimson staff, to patrol the mortal realm, lying in wait for the petty ghosts of pestilence—those who falsely claim the titles of the Three Dukes and Five Emperors—and slay them on sight. Should any petty ghost refuse to depart, the Demon Kings of the Three Heavens and their descendants shall be executed without mercy.

From this day forward, should any among you fail to heed my incantation, your heads shall shatter into seven pieces.

The Dao spoke: From this day forward, should any within the realm fall ill, it is the work of petty ghosts and minor malevolent spirits. You must swiftly withdraw your legions and disperse them, that the living may suffer no further harm—this is the command of the Demon Kings, a thousandfold and ten thousandfold. Should illness persist and the living perish, all great ghosts, both within and without, shall be slain without mercy.

The Great Demon King of the Pecked Head, the Great King Wu Yan, the Great King of the Long Nose, the Great King Zhong Xiang, the Great King of Small Eyes, the Great King of the White Face, the Great King of the Red Face, and their four hundred ninety thousand followers—each shall be interrogated, along with their descendants. Summon the petty ghosts at once and command them to cure the afflicted. If they do not, I shall have you and your petty ghosts executed without mercy.

The Dao spoke: From this day forward, should any within the realm suffer illness, or face legal disputes, slander, imprisonment, or bondage under the Three Officials, unable to find relief—it is because you, the great Demon Kings, have failed in your duty. From this day on, command the petty ghosts: do not harm my people. Swiftly recall your legions and issue the writs, that the sick may recover, legal troubles dissolve, and disputes cease. With utmost urgency, as the oral command of the Most High, by law and decree.

The Dao spoke: In the world, there are sixty-nine kinds of great ghostly afflictions, long-bearded and short-haired, mourning for the rivers and mountains. The rivers and mountains harbor evil ghosts, causing the people of the realm to fall ill and die. Now they come to wreak havoc upon the world, bringing sickness and stirring all manner of pestilential qi. The Yellow Slave and his seven sons conspire to kill. I have learned your names, petty ghosts—from this day forward, depart a thousand li. With utmost urgency, by law and decree.

The Dao spoke: From this day forward, the thirty-six Demon Kings of the Three Heavens above and the Three Heavens shall descend and kowtow seventy times, beseeching the capture of the lesser ghosts. Since the decree of the Most High was issued, no petty ghost shall dare return to the mortal realm to take the people. Should illness persist, the Demon Kings shall suffer ten thousand executions.

The Dao spoke: My good and peaceful people dwell within the realm, yet some do not believe in the Daoist teachings. Now, if even one person receives the Dao and wears the Three Caverns, and another falls ill, when the Dharma Master performs rituals for the afflicted, you Demon Kings must assist the Daoist and ensure their recovery—then you shall ascend. Should they not recover, I shall execute your petty ghosts without mercy.

As the Most High proclaimed this merit, all the great Demon Kings descended, each bowing their heads and declaring: From this day forward, we swear never again to indulge the petty ghosts. Should even one person in the world remain stricken with illness, our heads shall shatter into forty-nine pieces."

Here ends Scroll Eight of the *Most High Cavernous Abyss Divine Incantations Sutra*.
Here begins Scroll Nine of the *Most High Cavernous Abyss Divine Incantations Sutra*.

**Chapter on Slaying Ghosts**

The Dao spoke: In the years of *gengchen* and *renwu*, there shall come Great Thunder Ghosts, one named Nine Prosperities, leading eighty thousand lesser ghosts. Wielding crimson staves, they shall come to slay the wicked, inflicting thirty-six kinds of illness to kill evildoers. There shall also be thirty-nine million Sorrow-Simple Ghosts, spreading red swellings. Eighty-six million nine hundred thousand ghosts shall bring dysentery. Twelve million Red-Eyed Ghosts shall cause vomiting and flux. Ninety million ghosts shall afflict the eyes with pain. Forty-nine million ghosts shall bring chills and fever, sickening and killing the wicked.

At such time, where a Dharma Master recites the sutras, these ghosts shall perish of themselves. Eighty million trillion Jade Maidens of the Three Heavens, together with thirty-nine thousand maidens of the Ten Directions, shall descend as one, bowing their heads to the Most High and declaring: From this day forward, if there be households troubled by illness or official misfortune, and they invite a Dharma Master to recite the sutras, should plague ghosts still linger, we swear to drive them away, banishing them ten thousand leagues, that the living may recover and official entanglements be resolved. Should they not depart, the Enforcers of the Nine Heavens shall slay them without mercy.

The Dao spoke: Many in the world do not believe in the Dao. If even one receives the scriptures, men and women mock them. A Daoist who feels no shame at the scorn of fools is no true Daoist—the Dao treasures even mockery. The great flood draws near; the year *jiashen* approaches. In *renwu* and *guiwei*, the Great Crows shall slay men. Heaven shall dispatch plague ghosts to spread *qi*, sickening and killing the wicked. Blades and weapons shall clash, and the people shall perish. Insects, snakes, tigers, wolves, water, fire, and poisonous *qi*—all shall be capable of killing men. Yet men remain ignorant, their hearts foolish, slandering the worthy, reviling Daoists, defaming scriptures, and measuring sacred texts. Such sinners shall die suddenly, choking on blood, their throats sealed, their bodies swollen, their voices lost. Heaven and its hosts shall punish them, and none shall be saved.

Daoists, discipline yourselves: guard your speech and restrain your hearts.

The Dao spoke: From this *renchen* year onward, the True Lord shall surely come—the True Lord is not far. Daoists who believe, take heed and study diligently, converting others to receive the scriptures, and immortals shall come to welcome you. In the *renwu* year, plague ghosts shall slaughter men, and the people shall perish utterly. The Most High, moved by compassion, shall dispatch Great Perfected Ones—Cheng Zao, Yan Ping, Wang Jinfang, She Zhou, Zhuang Xuan, Tang Jun, and others—to go among the world and convert men. Those with immortal bones from past lives shall encounter these Perfected Ones. All these Perfected Ones are men of the world, with descendants among the living, and thus the Most High sends them.

The Dao spoke: By the *renwu* year, great calamity shall come, with waters rising a thousand myriad fathoms. Daoists who enter the mountains shall escape this disaster. From the third to the ninth month of the *renwu* year, the people shall perish utterly. Thirty-seven thousand plague ghosts, heads bent on slaughter, shall come—those who do not believe shall be the first to perish. They shall inflict ninety kinds of illness to kill men. The True Lord shall soon appear, but the wicked shall not see him. Heaven shall send slaying ghosts to punish them, sweeping clean heaven and earth, remaking sun and moon, rearranging the stars, and altering the cosmic order. Divine beings shall govern the law, with immortals as their aides. For five directions and ten thousand kalpas, there shall be no death, no weapons of war. The earth shall be adorned with the seven treasures, clothing and food shall arise spontaneously, no six livestock shall remain, men and women shall all be sages, and the race of wicked men shall cease to exist.

The Dao spoke: As the great flood approaches, those who know should receive the Three Caverns. Men and women who believe in the Dharma and practice the Dao with single-minded devotion—I shall send one hundred thousand Jade Maidens of the Three Heavens to protect them. When a Daoist converts others to receive the scriptures, converting even one, the hosts of heaven shall proclaim their virtue. But if one’s heart is corrupted and they refuse conversion, the hosts of heaven shall punish them. You all have immortal destiny from past lives, and thus you encounter this sutra. This sutra is profound and wondrous, revered by the heavens above. Honor it, make offerings, and keep it in your homes—plague ghosts shall be driven away, and no evil ghosts shall dare approach.

The Dao spoke: From this day forward, if there be disputes, official troubles, imprisonment, illness, peril, or the uncertainty of life and death in the world, you must swiftly recite this *Divine Incantations Sutra*. The sutra commands thirty-nine billion great spirits, who shall come to save men, and plague ghosts shall depart of themselves. The Crimson Soldiers of the Ten Directions, the Four Heavenly Demon Kings, and the maidens shall all descend to aid you, ensuring no evil befalls. Where a Daoist recites the sutras, should plague ghosts not depart, the Enforcers of the Three Heavens shall slay them without mercy.

The Dao spoke: From the *renwu* year onward, the people shall suffer many illnesses, and ghostly soldiers shall roam in bands of thousands and ten thousands, seeking to kill the wicked. When illness strikes, if a Dharma Master comes to save them, I shall also dispatch forty-nine million trillion Good Spirits and Directors of Destiny to drive away the plague ghosts, banishing them ten thousand leagues. Should they not depart, they shall be slain without mercy.

The Dao spoke: In the *renwu* year, a hundred million Great Crows shall spread *qi*-borne illness, sickening and killing the wicked. The wicked do not believe—what can be done when they die? The Perfected Ones shall rise again, sweeping clean heaven and earth, and plague ghosts shall come to slaughter men. If the people wish to escape disaster, they may, in the ninth and tenth months, establish this fast, pay homage to the Five Emperors, hold a great assembly for one day and two nights, and make repentance. Bow nine times toward the east, three times toward the south, seven times toward the west, five times toward the north. Toward *qian*, *kun*, *gen*, and *xun*, bow twelve times each. Toward the upper direction, bow thirty-two times; toward the lower, twelve times. The heavenly hosts shall descend, record your merits, and inscribe your name in the Jade Register. Alternatively, face east and bow thirty-six times in single devotion—only sincerity matters, and the blessings shall be boundless.

By the *guiwei* year, plague ghosts shall spread seventy kinds of disease to slay men. Should one seek to live, let every household establish this fast, pay homage to the Five Emperors, and bow thirty times toward the south—then shall the plague ghosts flee ten thousand *li* away.

The Dao declares: In the years of *jiazi*, *jiaxu*, and *jiashen*, there shall be eight hundred thousand red-tailed ghosts, named *Duo’a*, each with one head and three tails, their bodies nine *chi* in length. In their hands they hold water, bringing chills and fever to men, spreading ninety kinds of disease to afflict and kill the wicked. Daoists must swiftly convert the people, establishing a quiet abode by the water’s edge beside the Way. Hold a great assembly for one day, offering rites to the Five Emperors and the Controller of Fate, and bow thirty-six times toward the west. The heavenly hosts shall surely descend, recording the names and households of your kin in the Jade Register, sparing them from the rolls of death. Their names shall be inscribed at the Gate of Heaven, their lifespans extended by the Controller of Fate, and they shall never suffer an untimely end.

The Dao declares: In the years of *jiawu* and *jiachen*, black *qi* shall bring disease to slay men. Eighty-nine myriad plague ghosts shall spread throat obstructions and dysentery to kill. Should Daoists convert the people, receiving the talismans of the Three Caverns, let them hold a great assembly upon the waters in the first, second, and third months—one day and two nights, five watches—gathering to offer rites to the Five Emperors and the Twelve Spirits. Bow twenty-five times toward the north, and the heavenly hosts shall naturally record their names.

The Dao declares: In the year of *jiayin*, there shall be great-eyed ghosts, three *cun* in length, gathering in the thousands and myriads, accompanied by a million red crows, descending into households to slay men. Those who know this must swiftly assemble, fast, and hold rites upon the waters for one day and two nights, five watches of repentance. Bow thirty-six times toward the east, and the heavenly hosts shall surely come to record your name. The plague ghosts shall flee of their own accord, daring not draw near to men. Daoists must swiftly convert the people.

The Dao declares: The reason for disasters in the *renwu* year is that the gates of the mountains shall close—three before and two behind. Thus, in the years of *xinsi*, *renwu*, and *guiwei*, there shall surely be floods, and the regional lords, the Three Dukes, and the two-thousand-*shi* officials must swiftly turn toward goodness. In this year, plague ghosts shall certainly spread, slaying and eliminating the wicked, and those who do not believe shall perish. Daoists need only convert the foolish, and the heavenly hosts shall record their sincerity.

The Dao declares: The people of the world do not believe in the Dao and its methods, so Heaven commands plague ghosts to punish them. From this time forth, those of discernment who believe and practice shall be regarded by the heavenly hosts, who shall never allow them to suffer wrong. Wise scholars must propagate this, establishing merit and virtue—take heed!

The Dao declares: From the *renwu* year onward, thirty-six kinds of plant ghosts shall slay men. When people gather herbs from the wild to eat, the roots, stems, and leaves of these hundred plants contain ghostly toxins, named *Shengru*. *Shengru* and his brothers, a hundred myriad strong, can spread *qi*-borne diseases. On the tenth day of the month, they enter the four limbs and hundred joints of men, turning their bodies yellow and red. These ghosts are three *cun* and seven *fen* in length. In the mountains, a female ghost named *Luoweng* has one consort and two daughters, leading twenty myriad female ghosts. They lurk in the mountains, forests, and waters, lying in wait for men. There is also a female ghost named *Jiangnü*, who once had boundless merit and was destined for immortality, but for her disrespect toward the Three Heavenly Worthies and her failure to honor the Three Masters. When she sees Daoists entering the mountains, her heart harbors no goodwill. Her form is most hideous: her body stands a *zhang* tall, her face black, her eyes vertical, her entire being a sickly yellow-red, her form filthy and foul. Men do not wish to see her; those who do flee far to avoid her. For her disrespect of the Three Matters, she is taught to receive the scriptures and revere her masters, forbidden to slander the Dharma-teachers, to serve with diligence, and not to engage in frivolous conduct or associate with common folk. Those who do not follow this shall be held accountable by the heavenly hosts and condemned to dwell in the mountains for three thousand nine hundred *yi* kalpas—thus she remains trapped. Daoists who receive the secret talismans of the Three Caverns, the true essentials of the Most High, lay the foundation for their future. Yet in an instant, all may be lost. How much better to study immortality and never die through ten thousand kalpas!

The Dao declares: When Daoists receive the scriptures and find an enlightened master, possessing the fullness of the Three Caverns, they are like the wealthy of the world. Why is this? The greatly wealthy possess vast fields and estates, thousands of servants and slaves, and wealth sufficient for all needs. The poor of the world all labor for them, their desires fulfilled without want or lack. When they go forth, they ride fine steeds, their retinues at ease. When they give alms or make offerings, all is as they wish, for they are greatly wealthy. The great Dharma-teachers of the Dao, inwardly and outwardly accomplished, understand all worldly documents and letters. They are versed in healing, medicine, acupuncture, and moxibustion, and as they move among the people, the myriad folk revere and love them. The great scriptures of the Three Caverns are all complete within them, and the people honor them as they would a Heavenly King or a man of great wealth.

The Dao declares: Wealth and poverty, nobility and lowliness—all are but human conditions. All receive but a single fate; what difference is there? Yet the distinctions between wealth and poverty, nobility and lowliness, arise from the causes of past lives. Some, having practiced the Dao in former lives, are born in the Central Kingdom with clothing and food naturally provided. Others, having established merit and virtue in past lives, now enjoy great wealth and nobility, their blessings flowing to their descendants. Some, destined for immortality in past lives but not yet ascending, now enjoy great wealth and nobility for that reason. Daoists who are poor yet delight in the Dao—this is because they have studied for long in past lives but failed to convert others, thus they are made greatly impoverished. Those who die without property or livestock have committed grave sins in past lives, failing to perform merit and virtue, disbelieving in the scriptures and the Dao. They come from among the six kinds of livestock, or from the ranks of servants and slaves. Noble Daoists all come from Heaven. Without accumulating goodness in past lives, one shall never become a noble Daoist.

The Dao declares: In this world, there are many wicked people who do not believe in the Dao. Some receive the scriptures, yet fools mock them, their laughter filling the roads. They slander the worthy, calling the Dao mad and deluded, asking, “What do they seek in the mountains?”

Some claim them to be demonic spirits, feigning virtuous conduct, yet knowing nothing of all things. Man cannot long preserve himself; wealth and honor are fleeting, and cannot be held forever. The young grow old, and the old must inevitably die—three thieves within the body drag one away, yet death comes unperceived. Worldly people know only to covet wealth and cherish wives and children, preferring to commit sins rather than receive the scriptures, seek the Dao of immortality, or attend to their own burdens. Their days pass idly, yet they would do better to study the Dao, for then they would never die through ten thousand kalpas, and might wander together with the heavenly immortals.

The Dao declares: In the year *renshen*, pestilential *qi* shall spread widely, bringing twenty-three kinds of disease to afflict and slay the wicked. Only those who have received the scriptures, revered the Three Masters, and healed all manner of illnesses shall be noted by the heavenly beings. When the land embraces the Dao and receives the Three Caverns, teaching and transforming the people, then the emperors and kings of the Middle Kingdom shall remain unaware of the myriad evils summoned by the common folk—evils that arise from below without cause or origin, as a hundred ghosts vie to descend. At that time, male and female Daoists must unite in their efforts to remedy this. I shall dispatch thirty-nine hundred million Great Expelling Generals from the ten directions to aid the Daoists in driving them away.

The Dao declares: Within the Three Realms, fools who do not believe in the Dao and its methods die and enter the ranks of evil ghosts. Thus, these men and women, with their countless ghostly soldiers, come to slay the wicked. From this time forward, when one, two, or three households fall ill with affliction and distress, invite a great Dharma Master of the Three Caverns to recite the scriptures for one day and two nights, performing the five watches, practicing the Way of Nine Ones and the *qi* of Three Fives, and invoking the positions of the ten directions. In every direction, ghosts shall be slain, and even the ghost kings shall not dare to resist. Now, I myself shall send four hundred thousand Red Bow Soldiers and thirty-nine thousand Strongmen of the Nine Provinces to assist the Daoists, driving away all great ghosts, mountain and forest demons, *qi* of the ten directions, and ghostly bandits—all shall be cut down.

The Great Demon King and lesser kings, following my teachings, shall command the lesser ghosts to aid the Daoists in curing the host’s illness and resolving urgent official matters. Should they fail to comply with the law, the Demon Kings *Weirui* and others shall be slain without mercy. The Dao declares: All Daoists come from Heaven. Though worldly people may be base, ugly, or lowly, if their hearts believe in the Three Caverns, they too come from Heaven. The good are not necessarily fair of form; each has their own karmic causes. Those of upright appearance come from thoughts of goodness. The greatly wealthy come from past lives of almsgiving to the poor. The greatly noble come from building merit and worshiping the Three Treasures. Daoist Dharma Masters come from accumulated study. Thus, those who yearn for the Great Vehicle do so on the foundation of past lives—it is not suddenly attained in this one. If a Daoist aspires to the mountains and marshes, renouncing official life and severing all ties to enter the mountains and cultivate the Dao, such a one is not far from immortality. When such Daoists wander the world, healing the sick, the Demon Kings shall aid them.

The Dao declares: The world is full of those who drift heedlessly, unaware of the day of their death—these are but walking corpses. Daoists who seek immortality, receiving the essentials of the Three Caverns, should exhort others to do the same. Whether dwelling in the mountains or among people, they transform all fools. Yet fools, bound by desire, refuse to accept the Dao. When floods come, they shall perish; when blades strike, they shall be slain, flowing with the mud, and only then will they regret in vain. When the great expulsion and annihilation occurs, ghostly soldiers shall rage unchecked, causing evil ghosts to slay people throughout the land. But where Daoists practice the scriptures and save others through their recitations, all the great and lesser Demon Kings, male and female heavenly beings, shall come together with the Daoists to heal the sick, resolve official matters, and grant all wishes as the heart desires. Should any defiant ghostly *qi* arise to harm the living, the Demon Kings *Yunzhou* and others shall shatter their heads into sixteen pieces—none shall be spared.

All is as decreed by the Most High. The Dao declares: From this time forward, evil ghosts shall slay people, including the ghost named Red Eyebrow *Wuran* and his forty-eight thousand followers, who shall rampage across the land to slay the wicked. When Daoists and female Daoist priests come to save a host, the lesser ghost kings shall swiftly report to the Great Demon King, who shall command the Strongmen to aid the Daoists in transforming people, dispelling illness and *qi*, and resolving all matters. On the day of no other recourse, we shall ascend a thousandfold, ten thousandfold, never betraying the Golden Mouth. Those who do not believe shall be hewn into ten thousand pieces by the Demon Kings and lesser ghost kings—none shall be spared.

Here ends Scroll Nine of *The Most High Scripture of the Wondrous Spells of the Cavern Abyss*.
Here begins Scroll Ten of *The Most High Scripture of the Wondrous Spells of the Cavern Abyss*.

**Chapter on Slaying Ghosts**

The Dao spoke: On Mount Xuandu, I expounded the *Great Scripture of Expulsion* to all demon kings. At that time, the Three Heavenly Princes sought the *Scriptures of the Upper, Middle, and Lower Primordials*. Ten Perfected Ones from the ten lands also requested the *Scripture of Samādhi, the Boundless Primal Essence*. Furthermore, immortals from the ten directions sought the *Scriptures of the Yellow Court’s Inner and Outer Two Sceneries of Daoic Transformation*. From the four quarters of Jambudvīpa, thirty thousand Perfected Ones gathered to hear the scripture.

Before the exposition was complete, they all descended from their seats and said: "The people of the world do not comprehend the Dao and its methods. Epidemic ghosts slay them, blades and violence oppress them, and the people suffer bitterly. Death fills every household, and none possess the Three Caverns to deliver themselves. We beseech this Dharma Master to disseminate these teachings throughout the world. May the Heavenly Worthy incline toward the transformation of the Dao."

The Most High replied: "Excellent, excellent! Now I shall dispatch thirty thousand Perfected Ones to carry the scriptures and propagate the Dao across the world." There was also the Perfected One Nihe, who led thirty-nine thousand followers, bearing the scriptures to spread the teachings throughout the land. The people of the Middle Kingdom all received them. For households afflicted by sudden illness or official troubles, they would transmit the scriptures. Practicing the Dao thrice a day and night, official matters would be resolved, and the sick would recover. Epidemic ghosts lingering without departure would be slain one by one—none would be spared.

The Dao spoke: "These Perfected Ones share profound karmic ties with the people of this land, and thus they are sent to transmit the scriptures. Those who receive the Three Cavern scriptures all possess prior blessings and karmic conditions, destined for transcendence, and only then do they encounter such teachers. From this day forward, if there are those who uphold and wear these scriptures, I and the heavenly beings shall protect them, and no evil shall befall them."

The Dao spoke: "In the *renwu* year, great calamities shall arise. The people will be restless, the six barbarian tribes unsettled, and epidemic ghosts will slay them. One may craft spirit talismans and, according to the method, place them within homes for peace. Three, five, ten, or a hundred households may gather by the water. On a single day, hold a grand assembly, constructing an earthen altar eight feet wide and six feet high. Facing east, perform thirty-six prostrations, paying homage to the Five Emperors. Submit a memorial to the heavenly beings, and they shall surely record your sincere devotion."

The Dao spoke: "In the sixth month of the *xinsi* year, the ninth month of the *renwu* year, and the seventh month of the *guiwei* year, eighty thousand epidemic ghosts shall descend to slay the people. The ghost named Wutu Lunna stands seventy *zhang* tall, and they gather in the thousands and tens of thousands. There shall also be great crimson crows, their forms like cartwheels, flying to devour people. If one upholds the Three Cavern scriptures and practices them among the people, these plague crows shall perish. Let the Daoists bear witness to this truth."

The Dao spoke: "The great kalpa draws near, and rulers grow greedy and cruel. They neglect the common folk, who fall into destitution. Corvée labor is unjust, and the people suffer hardship. Wails fill the roads, and corpses cover the fields. Men and women lose their proper seasons, forsaking the Dao and its methods, fleeing in panic. The six barbarian tribes stir in chaos, and great bandits run rampant. They contend with *qi*, fathers and sons grow suspicious of one another. Heaven sends epidemic ghosts to execute these sinners. Their crimes are grave, and they shall face the great flood. The waters shall come soon, yet they remain unaware. Daoist masters and priests, in households where transformation is underway, the Three Heavenly Kings, all immortals, and jade maidens from the ten directions shall come to assist. They shall strengthen the Daoists, and the households they save shall be protected by heavenly beings. Illness and official troubles shall swiftly be resolved, ghostly *qi* shall dissipate, and the sick shall recover. If even a single ghost lingers, it shall be slain—no mercy shall be granted."

The Dao spoke: "The Lords of the Ten Directions declare: 'In this degenerate age, people are mostly wicked, and few believe in the Dao. The world remains untransformed. In the *renwu* year, eighty million epidemic ghosts shall be dispatched, spreading seventy kinds of diseases to slay the people. Those who are aware should establish this fast in every household, bowing to the Five Emperors by the great waters. Face the northwest in prostration, and craft a great talisman to hang above the main gate. Epidemic ghosts shall not dare approach. For households without talismans or those that do not hang this charm, the epidemic ghosts shall harm them. This talisman is guarded by eighty million mighty warriors.'"

The Dao spoke: "By the *jiaxu* and *renwu* years, there shall be eight thousand nine hundred red-faced ghosts named Mingzhen. Each shall lead thirty-nine thousand lesser ghosts, all wielding crimson staves to bludgeon the wicked. The wicked are many, for they do not believe in the flood or the Dao and its methods, and thus they shall fall into the Three Wretched Realms and Five Tribulations. The Most High, in profound vision, pities all beings and thus delivers them."

The Dao spoke: "In the *renwu* year, for all who hold fasts and transmit the *Scripture of Boundless Samādhi*, epidemic ghosts shall not dare approach. Daoists who have received the Three Cavern teachings and propagate them shall be aided by the Heavenly Emperor and shall never fall into evil destinies."

The Dao spoke: "From the *guiwei* to the *jiashen* years, three hundred ninety thousand *qi*-crows shall fly over the central rivers, spreading poison into households and afflicting people with water-borne illnesses, which cannot be cured. If one wears talismans and scriptures, and five or ten households build a healing abode by the water, making offerings to the Three Treasures with morning and evening incense and lamps, performing repentance and prostrations, and paying homage to the Five Emperors for one, two, or seven days, the heavenly beings shall surely record your name, and it shall enter the Jade Register."

The Dao spoke: "The great calamity draws near, and the flood shall come soon. Foolish people remain oblivious, idly passing their days. One hundred twenty thousand celestial maidens shall descend to transform them, yet the people shall not perceive it. If in the *xinsi* year one encounters these maidens’ transformation, you shall attain transcendence."

If one suffers from illness, legal troubles, or slander, let the Dharma masters and Daoist priests perform rituals to transform their fate. The celestial maidens shall also come to assist you, ensuring the household avoids misfortune.

The Dao spoke: "By the *guiwei* year, the Dao’s qi shall flourish daily, and the Three Caverns shall spread across the four seas and nine provinces, where all shall believe and rejoice. If Daoist hearts remain upright, the ruler shall uphold the Way. Sweep and purify every palace hall, erecting scripture altars within. Light lamps morning and evening, burn incense, and perform prostrations. Plague demons shall flee, the sick shall recover, and legal troubles shall dissolve. The armies of the Three Heavens shall shield the Dharma masters; wherever they walk, ghosts and bandits shall be driven a thousand miles away, and heavenly beings shall descend to aid the Daoists."

The Dao spoke: "In the *jiashen* year, great dragons shall ascend to heaven in flocks of ninety thousand. Whoever witnesses this shall know the great flood draws near. Daoists who enter the mountains may preserve their lives. Yet worldly people, steeped in wickedness, indulge in lust, covet wealth, and kill without restraint. Their cruel hearts never change; they scorn the Great Dao, refuse to cultivate immortal practices, and when they see others receive the scriptures, they mock them instead. Such people shall enter the endless hells, where each day they endure seven deaths and seven rebirths before being revived again. This torment shall last forty-two kalpas before they are released. Even then, as humans, they shall be maimed—deaf, mute, or dumb, afflicted with goiters, missing limbs, blind, cleft-lipped, hunchbacked, or crippled, their faces like deer, their feet like roebucks, without hands or feet. No one shall wish to see them; those who do shall retch in disgust. Such is the retribution for their past deeds."

The Dao spoke: "Where the virtuous are born, they surpass others in wisdom, for this comes from past lives of study. Those born with deformities bear the weight of grave sins from former existences. If such a person remains untransformed, it is because they have never witnessed goodness. Daoists must still strive to convert them, for the heavenly beings shall record your resolve. To fail in this is to betray the sincere devotion of those who came before, and it is not the way of the Great Beings who deliver all beings."

The Dao spoke: "By the *renwu* year, thirty thousand white-headed ghosts shall appear, each named *Thousand Transformations*, their bodies thirty feet tall, their faces emanating qi, their heads white, gathering in the millions. They shall unleash thirty-nine thousand kinds of diseases to slay the wicked. Those who scorn the Dao and its teachings, slander Daoist priests, or criticize the scriptures—who argue over right and wrong, claim the scriptures lack power, and fail to grasp the Dao’s profound depth, as boundless as the heavens and as immeasurable as the sea—shall face their judgment."

Thus do the foolish-hearted expound the wondrous scriptures. They scorn Daoist priests, claiming the world holds no numinous power. Their minds waver between two paths, corrupting the true heart. Such sinners deserve ten thousand deaths, to be cast upside-down into the hells. There they shall stand inverted for thirty kalpas, and only when the kalpa ends shall they emerge—reborn as the six kinds of livestock.

The Dao spoke: "The people of the world are mostly foolish, and so Heaven commands the myriad spirits to slay them with baleful qi. The reason for their slaughter is their slander of Daoist priests and the murder of good people. Now, those who disbelieve in the Great Dao, disrespect the Three Treasures, and refuse to receive the scriptures—Heaven’s soldiers shall execute them. Today, three thousand and sixty kinds of diseases slay people; there are thirty thousand flesh-ghosts, one hundred thousand stone-ghosts, twenty thousand wood-ghosts, thirty-six million water-ghosts, six hundred thousand earth-ghosts, and one hundred sixty-six thousand insect-ghosts, all capable of killing. The reason they can kill is that the ghosts attach themselves to these things to slay people: entering water, one drowns; entering mountains, one is crushed by stones; felling trees, one is killed by wood; eating meat, one dies by its qi; digging earth, one is buried by soil; entering grass, one is harmed by insects—all these are the qi of unlawful forces.

From this day forward, Daoist priests must diligently convert the myriad families, teaching foolish men and women to all devote themselves to the Dao, so that ghosts will not draw near. If they refuse to believe, on the day of the great expulsion, I fear the ghostly soldiers will come to execute you."

The Dao spoke: "In the *renwu* year, the lord of the Six Barbarians shall all submit to the Great Dao, and the Three Caverns’ teachings shall spread far and wide. Those who enter the mountains shall be found everywhere. You who receive the dharma and uphold the scriptures—whether great or small, old or young, man or woman—only those with the heart to devote themselves shall have their lifespans extended by the heavenly beings, never meeting an untimely death, and naturally attaining the ranks of immortality."

The Dao spoke: "From this day forward, if there are Daoist priests, male or female officials, who diligently convert the myriad people, traveling through the lands to heal the hundred diseases, then you, demon kings, heavenly beings, and lesser ghost kings, must all assist the Daoist priests in treating illnesses, preventing the living from suffering misfortune, cutting short their lifespans, slaying ghosts, and pacifying people."

The Dao spoke: "From this day forward, I command all ghost kings to follow Daoist priests and pacify people, curing the myriad diseases so that none remain unhealed. If any disease is not cured, they shall be hacked into ten thousand pieces. Now I dispatch the divine generals of the five directions and the great soldiers of the nine heavens—thirty-nine million in all—to descend as one. They shall assist the households where Daoist priests treat illnesses, resolving all afflictions and official matters at once. Those who disobey shall be seized first by the ghost kings. All shall follow the oral decree of the Most High, without delay or violation of the statutes. Hasten, as the law commands!"

The Dao spoke: "The people of the world do not believe in the Dao, nor do they receive the scriptures. Born into worldly customs, they bring upon themselves the root of sin. Seeing others do good, they mock those who practice the Dao; they disrespect the Three Treasures, and the heavenly beings shall execute them. Suddenly they depart, and though they may regret it, what use is remorse? Now I dispatch thirty million vajra-warriors from the ten directions to descend as one and assist these Daoist priests wherever they go, pacifying people and severing evil. If any insult, curse, strike, scheme against, or steal from Daoist priests, their souls shall be seized one by one and handed over to the local hells for punishment, so they may know their guilt and understand Heaven’s decree. Ghost kings, take these words of mine and execute such evil people for these Daoist priests. If you do not slay them, the heavenly beings will be displeased, and the Great Dao will lose its numinous power."

All demon kings replied: "So be it! We shall each follow the command and now slay such people."

The Dao spoke: "From this day forward, wherever Daoist priests travel to convert others at the borders of foreign lands, seeking out the sick, they must perform rites and recite scriptures for each one. I shall dispatch eight hundred thousand great soldiers from the ten directions to assist you in your work. I command all great demon kings to ensure that no evil winds blow across the land, that rain does not fall in torrents, that people and ghosts live in harmony, that the common folk rejoice, and that kings believe in the Dao. If the common people receive the scriptures for seven days, they may enter the mountains and ascend as immortals. If this is not so, I shall no longer be called the Great Dao, nor shall I convert people again."

The Dao spoke: "When great dharma masters treat illnesses, they need only recite the oral talismans, not write them on paper, and cure them in silence. When reciting scriptures and performing the Dao, none shall remain uncured. If a patient is gravely ill, the oral talismans may also be recited aloud to repent past transgressions, untangle karmic nets, and absolve sins and retributions. Daoist masters of the Three Caverns need only enter a quiet chamber to commune with like-minded souls. When Daoist priests practice the qi of the Nine Ones or the qi of the Three Fives, all heavenly vajra-warriors and divine kings shall descend without fail. This is the art of the celestial perfected, the heavenly beings, and the divine maidens; all heavenly beings shall descend to assist your heart, and official matters and illnesses shall be cured without exception.

From this day forward, in the households where Daoist priests perform the Dao, great demon kings and lesser ghost kings shall all follow and assist, ensuring the sick are cured. If they are not cured, the lesser kings and the great demon kings, along with Wei Zhen, shall have their heads shattered into eighty pieces. All shall follow the oral decree of the Most High, and none shall be spared."

The Dao spoke: "Daoist priests who uphold the Three Caverns must not travel together with those who practice the Yellow and Red Ways. Daoist priests who uphold the scriptures and masters of the Three Caverns should enter the mountains to distance themselves from the impure world. If they remain among people, male and female Daoist priests of the Yellow and Red Ways must establish separate lodgings. If they wish to meet, they must choose auspicious days: *gengshen*, *jiazi*, *dingmao*, *jimao*, the 8th, 12th, 22nd, 9th, 1st, and 18th days—these are the proper days."

The Dao spoke: "All demon kings, from this day forward, wherever Daoist priests go to save people, ensure that the suffering of the living is cured and their official matters resolved."

"Should any person commit evil deeds, suppress them all—then a hundred blessings shall gather upon their body, bringing peace to people and slaying demons. If illness is cured, they shall ascend into the Great Dao. Should any fail to aid Daoist priests and cause the death of the living, you shall each rend them into ten thousand pieces, showing no mercy. Execute every command as if spoken by the Most High’s own lips—swiftly, as the law decrees.

The Dao spoke: Now there are eighty thousand black-bodied ghosts, each six inches tall, riding upon crows in flight to dwell in the waters. When wind and rain arise, they cling to human bodies, and those afflicted shall die. There are also thirty-nine thousand sand-dwelling Hu ghosts, each three inches tall, their forms red and white. When waters surge, they attach themselves to people. Further, there are eight hundred thousand great damp ghosts, named Heaven’s Head, whose masters delight in violence and chaos. Each commands thirty thousand ghostly brigands to enter human dwellings, causing fires that cannot be extinguished. Such ghosts, in the era of great floods, will incite rulers to cruel governance, leading to the slaughter of the people. Yet those Daoist priests who receive the scriptures and devote themselves to the mountains, refusing worldly office—such persons, along with the male and female practitioners of the Yellow and Red Ways—shall not be harmed.

The Dao spoke: From this day forth, there shall be a great ghost named Collapsing Zhou. Ten thousand great ghosts, named Li Zi, Shi Er, and Peach Ginger, shall in the *renwu* year each lead one hundred twenty thousand to slay the wicked—only true persons and Daoist priests shall they dare not offend. From this moment until the *jiaxu* year and beyond, ten million ghostly soldiers shall come to kill the evil. Should any foolish ones have Daoist priests recite scriptures and perform rites to save them, heaven’s people shall aid them, and the ghost kings shall take pity, coming to protect them.

The Dao spoke: From this day until the *renwu* year through the *renchen* year and the *zi* and *chou* years, great ghosts shall slay people. Of those who survive, barely three or four in ten shall remain—so numerous are the wicked. Thus heaven punishes them with blades, weapons, and drowning. Alas, alas! Only those who receive the scriptures as Daoist priests shall be welcomed by heaven’s people. As the great kalpa nears its end, they shall swiftly come. Ghosts shall rise in competition, and people shall die of pestilence. Should any have a master of the Three Caverns perform the Dao for them, all great ghost kings and demon kings shall protect and assist, curing their illnesses at once. They shall subdue the wayward ghosts of the world, both inner and outer, driving them a thousand feet into the earth. If the afflicted do not recover, death shall spread like carrion, official matters unresolved, fields and silkworms barren, careers stagnant, and all shall be as they wish it not. The officials and soldiers shall be the first to answer, and the great demon kings and lesser ghostlings shall rend them into a thousand pieces, showing no mercy. Proclaim every decree as if uttered by the Most High’s golden lips—swiftly, as the law decrees.

The Dao spoke: Now there are eighty-nine thousand black-faced great ghosts, named Red Beard, each seven *zhang* tall. In groups of four hundred ninety thousand, they falsely claim to be the Yellow Emperor, terrorizing the households of the living. Leading all manner of unregistered ghosts, the *wangliang* of the world, and the male and female *□*, they command Luo Ding Le Zhang, Nan Yang Ye Gong, Stone Mother’s Prince, Yun Zhong Li Zi Ao, and the ghosts of the Three Heavens Without Attachment—countless in number, they invade homes to seize infants, the elderly, men, and women, causing illness and death throughout the land, present in every place, death at every door. Ghostly soldiers shall gather, occupying the lanes and paths of the people, seizing their livestock and beasts, while birds and animals manifest omens of misfortune. People shall suffer official disputes, unjust imprisonment, and wrongful punishment; their fields and silkworms shall fail, and every endeavor shall bring misfortune. From this day forth, you demon kings, lesser ghosts, and all ghost kings must swiftly assist Daoist priests in aiding the living—resolving their official matters and curing their illnesses. Should you disobey, each of you demon kings shall be rent into ten thousand pieces. Execute every command as the Most High’s oral decree and the law demand."

**The Tenth Scroll of the *Supreme Scripture of the Wondrous Abyss and Divine Spells* concludes.**
**The Eleventh Scroll of the *Supreme Scripture of the Wondrous Abyss and Divine Spells* begins.**
**Chapter on the Samādhi King’s Summons of Ghosts and Spirits**

In the second year of the Highest August’s reign, during the *chen* month of the establishment of spring, at noon on the eighth day, within the Supreme Yang’s Upper Palace, the Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning expounded the *Scripture of the Wondrous Cavern, Numinous Treasure, Great Possession, Utmost Perfection, and Natural Wisdom of Pure Sincerity* to the Great Brahmā Heavenly Emperor of the Great Luo, the Lofty Perfected of the Four Poles, the Primordial Kings of the Nine Heavens, and the True August Ones of the Three Heavens. When the Dharma rites were complete, he further summoned the Heavenly Lords of the Three Qi, the Five Elder Thearchs, the Perfected Immortals of the Nine Palaces, the Thirty-Six Heavenly Emperors of the Four Boundless Directions, the Flying Heavenly Spirit Kings, the Earthly Sovereigns of the Nine Lands, and the officials of the Three Realms. Surrounded by the Great Demons of the Divine Empyrean, they soared through the vast sky, returning their chariots to descend upon the Azure Sea’s shore in the Wànlì Heaven, within the Jade Pool’s Chamber of the Wondrous Abyss. Seated upon a five-colored flying dragon lotus throne, he was about to expound the essential Dharma to save and deliver all sentient beings of the Three Realms and Five Paths. Radiating his majestic light, he illuminated the dragon palaces of the one hundred eighty seas in the ten directions, the courts of the Fengdu and Yánggǔ Water Assemblies, the palaces of the Earthly Sovereigns of the Nine Lands and Thirty-Six Earths in the Windy Marsh, the registries of the Perfected Immortals and Great Sages, and the Thirty-Six Grotto-Heavens—each possessing its own sun, moon, and stars, its officials, people, livestock, birds, beasts, insects, and fish, all deeming themselves secure and joyful. Those without divine Dao, the common folk—husbands and wives, men and women, old and young, high and low—all trace their lineages, bearing manifold names and forms. The Five Agents, yin and yang, fortune and misfortune, suffering and joy, poverty and wealth, nobility and baseness—all are as in this world, with no difference. There are also those who study the Dao and seek immortality, dwelling in mountains and valleys to realize the Dao and attain sagehood. Yet without cultivating the Six Penetrations and Six Awakenings, they cannot be called Daoist priests, but are termed other scholars, for they lack such matters—even unto the boundless worlds of the uppermost heavens.

All realms where sages and beings dwell, the karmic retribution of suffering and joy—pray, let the nine murky springs of the netherworld and the grotto-heavens of the Five Marchmounts be revealed, that all in the great assembly may witness the retribution of good and evil, life and death: the ceaseless toil through cycles of filth and flame, drifting through the Eight Gates, self-born and self-perishing, a sight most piteous and grievous.

Within the great assembly, among the ranks of heavenly beings and earthbound immortals, some possess minor knowledge and insight, soaring through the Five Marchmounts, practicing corpse-liberation, ingesting elixirs, and refining the body. Yet those who do not aspire to the vast wisdom-source of the Numinous Treasure, who have not attained the true quiescence and spontaneous nature of past lives, find their minds unsteady, deluded by falsehoods, swayed by the Six Passions. At times, clinging to their attachments, their four views drift and scatter, above in the heavens or below on earth, where, according to the weight of their evil, they receive their retribution. With no self-exhortation, they endure manifold torments, all filled with dread. Their five spirits mourn in dismay, yet they know not where to turn, each desiring to flee but unable to depart. Gazing at one another, they say: "Today we have encountered the Sacred Venerable—why must we witness such dire retribution?" Their bodies and minds tremble in terror, unable to find peace. They can only pray to the Heavenly Venerable, beseeching mercy and deliverance, to expound the primordial origin and restore their original minds.

Thereupon, from among the assembly, the Flying Heavenly King of the Nine Heavens, named Samādhi Majestic Virtue, arose from his seat. Radiant with wisdom and adorned with auspicious marks, he possessed the power to subdue all demons. Heavenly spirits, dragons, and ghosts all revered his luminous incantations and skillful expedient means, which brought timely benefit. Leading the perfected ones, the Radiant Net King, and the thirty-six lesser kings of the heavens, including King Gulou, they adjusted their robes and crowns, rose together, and prostrated themselves, knocking their heads to the ground in reverence. Kneeling, they bowed deeply and addressed the Dao Lord:

"We, having accumulated profound merit, have been graced by the presence of the Great Sage, following the perfected immortals and the lofty and mysterious adepts. Overwhelmed by undeserved favor, we hold our royal positions, each governing the various heavens, our joy and awe intermingled. Today, beholding your compassionate radiance, you have further opened the great amnesty. We have all come, having once received your teachings and decrees, traversing the Three Realms, the thirty-two heavens, and the lands of the ten directions—mountains, forests, sacred peaks, and the dragon palaces beneath the seas, as well as the grotto-heavens and blessed lands. At times we roam the world, at others we enter the human realm, adapting to the customs of the multitudes, sharing in their labors, experiencing the ranks of noble and base, rich and poor. Some dwell in secluded mountains, engaging in cultivation, while others endure the hardships of livestock, insects, water, and fire—there is nowhere we do not enter.

We have witnessed the common folk, whether learned or unlearned, heedless of past lives, disregarding scriptural teachings. Their judgments are confused, their four views deluded, their Six Passions stained, their minds uncentered. When committing evil, they feel no fear; at times, seized by terror, they cry out to gods and ghosts, seeking deliverance. Some invoke the Three Luminaries, their seven ancestors, or the departed as oaths, racing against one another without end. Families turn against one another, killing without principle. In times of war and famine, relying on brute force, they gather mobs to slaughter the innocent. All beings—humans, ghosts, birds, and beasts—when facing the end of life, cling to their homes, cherish their bodies, their hearts gripped by urgency and longing. Some harbor evil thoughts, others utter wicked vows. Following their original oaths, wherever they reside, wherever blood and flesh adhere, wherever qi is exhaled or eyes gaze, they generate evil karmic causes. Their ethereal souls become habituated, their retribution endless. Having not entered the natural precepts of the Numinous Treasure’s wisdom, how can they escape?

Some believe their refined spirits and subtle mind-and-form are stirred by light, sound, and qi, thus riding the qi of the Six Heavens, the Five Yous, the hundred spirits, the Nine Uglies, the Eight Winds, and the waxing and waning of the Five Agents. They attract calamities: pestilence, plagues, and a hundred diseases arise. Creditors and enemies, slander and defamation—many suffer such encounters. In cities and government dwellings, villages and mountain marshes, wails follow one another, malevolent spirits grow fiercer, and human hearts tremble with fear, giving rise to chills and fevers. From within, cold and heat arise; from without, illness is born. Some pray to shrines and temples, invoking the impure qi of old ghosts who seek blood offerings, falsely predicting fortune and misfortune. Unaware of the true Dao, ignorant of their return, blind to scriptural teachings, they fail to recognize their original nature. Entangled with the hundred spirits, they accumulate sins before the Three Officials, sinking into the Five Paths, self-born and self-perishing, forever without escape.

At times, the Five Dipper star-officials announce calamities and disasters: floods, droughts, winds, and rains that disrupt the four seasons; blades, wars, and epidemics that bring inauspicious qi. Rulers grow anxious, the people suffer in filth and flame, with no deliverance. Today, by the power of the Sacred Venerable, we have been entrusted as divine kings. Having witnessed all this, we pray for peace and nurturance, to repay your compassion. We shall lead our hosts—the thirty-six lesser kings of the heavens and eighty million beings—to traverse the ten directions, healing the sick, protecting nations, nurturing all life, and spreading the true Dharma. Is this not our shared duty?"

Thereupon, the perfected Radiant Net King led forty-nine billion perfected immortals and their retinues. With them were the Three Heavenly Perfected Kings; the thirty-six Great Demon Kings of the Nine Heavens, numbering thirty-six billion; the divine kings of great spiritual penetrations and wisdom, the Sentence-People and Divine Youths, totaling eight billion; the Heavenly Prohibition Great Executioners and their soldiers, four hundred thousand; the Heavenly Execution Great Soldiers, four hundred thousand; the Upper Three Heavenly Marshals of the Dark Blade, thirty thousand; the Great Soldiers of the Nine Heavens, ninety billion; the Thirty-Six Heavenly Demon Kings, including King Gupenzi, and seventy-two lesser kings; the Demon King Wulinzi and the Great Demon King Wuliuzi, totaling thirty-six million; the Three Heavenly Jade Maidens and the Great Brahma Maidens, eighty million; the Seven Heavenly Demon Kings, three hundred thousand; the Generals of Rampant Slaughter, eighty million; the Great Demon Kings of Azure Perfection—Zizhen, Konglun, Wuyanshuai, and Chongquan—and thirty-nine kings, including Wuchuan, Lianzi, Wenjixiu, and Fenglianzi, totaling three billion six hundred million; the Three Heavenly Valiant Soldiers, three hundred thousand; and the Great Execution Generals of the Ten Directions, three hundred thousand, who govern the plague demons, dispel disasters and mists, and sweep away defilements.
