Today, the fast and rites conclude,
Fortune descends like clouds and rain.

The Yellow Emperor of the Center,
Who governs the immortals of the ten directions.
True persons and jade maidens dwell in chambers,
The mysterious and responsive, distant and serene.
The darkest gloom is lit by the Three Lights,
Sun and moon shine bright and clear.
Majestic and resplendent, the Supreme Yang,
The Three Caverns spread their flow,
Bringing salvation to all quarters.
Men and women who cultivate with devotion,
Shall behold the Jade Emperor’s face.
Riding phoenixes, they wander in radiance,
Their bodies soaring in flight.
All the Perfected gather in clouds,
Maidens scatter blossoms in the air.
With sincere hearts, bow to the Center,
The afflicted find peace and health.

The Lord of Mystic Qi of the Northeast,
Supreme Sovereign of all heavens.
Divine consorts and true immortal maidens,
Step through clouds with flying strides.
Revere the master, receive the Three Caverns,
Generation after generation, descendants prosper.
Today, present this oral petition,
Slay ghosts and stir the demon kings.
Plague ghosts flee ten thousand leagues,
All evil is crushed and concealed.
Should any dare defy,
Their lives shall perish, vanish away.
The Great Sage transforms the multitudes,
The faithful enter the immortal realm.
Slander gives rise to strife,
Naturally meeting frost and wind.
Why not uphold the Great Dao,
Revere and ascend to Heaven’s halls?
Devoutly bow to the Northeast,
Illness fades, life is prolonged.

The Bright Emperor of the Southeast,
Wind gods stand tall and proud.
Mysterious maidens come to bow,
Nine dragons cross the Three Rivers.
A human life in this world,
Is like mistletoe clinging to a pine.
When the pine dies, the mistletoe withers,
How can human life be long?
The foolish fear they will not live,
The wise drift with the world’s flow.
Official posts do not long endure,
In but a moment, sighs arise.
Without great wisdom and sagacity,
How can one escape the world’s snares?
Plagues and illnesses arise in their time,
The body’s misfortunes are many.
Today, present this oral petition,
Heavenly beings command the great demons.
Demon kings, lesser ghosts,
Depart swiftly, tarry not.
All evil and every wickedness,
Slay them, let them be destroyed.
The master of rites bows to the Southeast,
Vital qi naturally prevails.

The Supreme Unity Lord of the Southwest,
The Heavenly Mother proclaims her divine might.
Disciples present petitions,
Establish fasts to seek long life.
All illnesses naturally heal,
Offices and courts find peace.
Family feuds are resolved,
Water and fire cease their strife.
Immortals come to protect,
Jade maidens and nine dragons welcome.
The Three Caverns dispel the world’s woes,
The faithful live through ten thousand kalpas.
The Flame Emperor of the Northwest,
The Three Lights stir the divine.
With whole heart, uphold the talismans,
True immortals descend to welcome.
Jade maidens by the thousands and millions,
Revere the master, cultivate long life.
Disasters vanish, great merit is achieved,
When complete, divine dragons welcome.
Those who do not believe, who slander the Dao,
Shall dwell in the Nine Dark Realms forever.
Rising or sitting, they slander others,
For ten thousand kalpas, they shall not be reborn.
Illness, official strife, and slander,
Bandits arise from past transgressions.
Today, sacrifice to the Five Emperors,
Present petitions to save the living and the dead.
Devoutly bow to the Northwest,
Hear my recitation and chant.
Above, the void stretches vast,
Heavenly beings all depend on it.
The Three Caverns transform the world’s deluded,
Those who wear them shall soar on clouds.
Petitions cure illness,
Plague ghosts naturally weaken.
Now, I pay homage to the Five Emperors,
Chanting these rare and subtle words.
Sweep away the miasmas of the home,
All demons yield in awe.
Devoutly wear the talismans,
Revere the masters who recite the scriptures.
Bow thirty times to the Above,
Ten thousand blessings naturally return.

The Lord of the World Below,
Miling, how lofty and grand!
The fate of a generation is but an evening,
Ten thousand years pass like a single dawn.
Yet among them are the deathless,
Who chant the Three Caverns’ hymns.
Establish fasts, recite divine incantations,
Present petitions to command demon kings.
Jade maidens by the hundreds of thousands,
Plague ghosts all hide away.
With utmost sincerity, sacrifice to the Five Emperors,
Seek life and deliver the departed.
To dispel illness and suffering,
Devoutly bow to the Below.

The Hymn of the Three Heavenly Lords:
Vast and boundless, the Great Beginning,
Towering and shrouded in mist.
Within it are the worthy,
Surrounded by immortal elders.
Mysterious maidens descend,
Ten thousand spirits in layers.
Spirits of the Five Peaks,
Come to assist in harmony.
Eighty thousand attendants,
Dark elders and azure youths.
Heal the world’s illnesses,
Slay ghosts and dispel misfortune.
Today, present this oral petition,
Ten thousand ghosts plunge into the flood.
Dare any defy,
They shall be slain without mercy.
With sincere hearts, bow thrice,
That you may forever prosper.

The Hymn of the Nine Heavenly Jade Maidens:
The Three Caverns spread their transformation,
Fiery qi brushes the heavens.

In this shallow age, the foolish fail to recognize worth.
They spurn the good, prolonging endless night.
The Dao speaks of goodness, yet the seven ancestors fade into oblivion.
Illness, official misfortune, and slanderous tongues swirl in chaos.
They wear talismans and receive registers, yet their hearts remain divided.
With forked tongues, they slander, then turn to blame others.
They sabotage others’ good deeds, break precepts, and indulge in lust.
Such beings defile the Dao’s gate with wickedness and shame.
In death, they descend into the Nine Dark Realms, bringing calamity upon their descendants.
They seek favor through crooked means, begging for mercy in the moment,
Unknowing of their grave sins, bound for ten thousand kalpas in entanglement.
Their past lives lacked fortune, and long illness stretches unbroken.
They refuse to bestow kindness, yet urgently demand it from others.
Never having accumulated goodness, what words of regret remain?

With sincere hearts, bow in reverence—
The Ten Thousand Saints shall grant their grace.

**The Hymn of the Fusang Great Emperor:**
Mysterious, the Three Heavens,
Above dwell the divine masters.
The Five Dipper stars gleam bright,
The Three Luminaries radiant.
Immortal sages descend,
Jade maidens play in delight.
The True Sovereign’s kalpa-endures,
Countless eons unfold.
Establish merit, practice the Dao,
Heal illness and private woes.
Evil cannot assail the upright,
Crooked and straight return to their source.
Today, present this oral petition,
Erect blessings vast and towering.
The Ghost King seizes poison,
All suffering and decline dispelled.
With devout hearts, bow to the Saints—
Ten thousand blessings come as aid.

**The Hymn of the Golden Heavenly True Mother:**
The world’s people swarm in chaos,
Creating their own tangled webs.
The Three Caverns spread their teachings,
Yet the foolish remain deaf.
They see the Dharma but do not cultivate,
Engendering evil and misfortune.
Greed harms the present,
Ten sorrows entangle them.
The Three Wretched Paths, Six Thieves,
Five Destinies, Eight Gates.
Rely on this oral petition,
Erect blessings and pray for grace.
May past transgressions be absolved,
Present afflictions find relief.
The whole household bows in worship,
Reverently gazing to the heavens above.
Heavenly maidens descend,
To dispel disaster and misfortune.

**The Hymn of the Heavenly True Sovereign:**
The Three Caverns flow and unfold,
Divine soldiers drive out evil.
The foolish do not believe,
Bringing calamity upon themselves.
The sages sigh in lament,
Mourning the world’s stubborn fools.
Wandering the Three Realms,
They linger at heaven’s crossroads.
Unknowing how to seek the Dao,
To ascend to the celestial kitchens.
Illness and suffering stretch endlessly,
Only then do they seek a master.
Their past lives lacked goodness,
In this life, they suffer further.
They blame themselves in word and heart,
Yet have nothing to offer in atonement.
Despising their bodies, they crave ease,
Entering the Dao to find solace.
With devout oral petitions,
They make their pleas heard in the Great Void.
Erecting fasts to pray for blessings,
All evils dissolve and vanish.
Azure youths and jade maidens,
Immortal sages descend in joy.
The Thirty-Six Heavens,
Heavenly maidens together.
Three, five, seven, nine,
The Twenty-Four Origins.
All practice the Dao at once,
Ten thousand evils vanish.
With sincere hearts, bow six times—
Good fortune and blessings overflow.

**The Hymn of the Thirty-Two Heavenly Jade Maidens:**
Heaven transforms the foolish and deluded,
Yet the world’s people remain unaware.
They kill and harm the innocent,
Causing gods and spirits to flee.
Uphold the Three Caverns’ talismans,
Heavenly maidens descend in harmony.
Today, present this oral petition,
Command the spirits to take heed.
The sick swiftly recover,
The Ghost King does not defy.
Each devoutly bows thrice,
Accumulating merit without flaw.
The Mysterious Maiden personally descends,
Bestowing blessings in equal measure.

**The Hymn of the Three Heavenly Jade Maidens:**
The Yellow, Red, and Purple Palaces,
Open the Dao’s scriptures.
Having received them, they do not practice,
Blocking the gates of ghosts.
The Three Caverns’ divine incantations,
The root of flying immortals.
Having received them, they do not uphold,
Seven ancestors languish in darkness.
Past lives bear sins,
Illness clings to the body.
Today, devote oneself to repentance,
Pouring out one’s heart in confession.
All debts from past lives,
Humbly beseech to be washed away.
As the honored decree commands,
Following the master’s scriptural words.
Kneel and bow twice,
Supplicating heavenly grace.

**The Hymn of the Ten Heavenly Perfected:**
The Three Heavenly Jade Maidens,
A host of immortals descend in play.
Following the master, upholding the Dao,
All illnesses naturally heal.
Water, fire, and kalpa-turning disasters,
The wise grieve in sorrow.
The foolish do not believe,
Flowing together for a thousand years.
Alas, the stubborn fools,
Die and enter the Nine Dark Realms.
Now, to heal illness,
Manifest and instruct the mortal realm.
Bow thrice with sincere hearts,
Heavenly maidens descend in throngs.

**The Hymn of the Five Peaks’ Immortals:**
The world’s people abound in evil,
Foolish and base, they gather and multiply.
They do not believe in the Three Caverns,
Nor the Forty-Nine Hidden Scriptures.
Thus, they fall ill,
Suffering clings and torments.
Past lives and present,
Their sins and punishments are not light.
Today, present this oral petition,
Erect fasts to seek life.
May they receive grace,
And behold great peace.
With sincere hearts, bow thrice—
Forever preserve health and tranquility.

**The Hymn of the Thirty-Six Heavenly Great Brahma Kings:**
I see the world’s foolish people,
Do not believe in the sacred and true.
They create karmic bonds of defilement,
Bringing calamity upon their seven ancestors.
Relying on the master, wearing talismans and registers,
They revert to being like ordinary folk.
The Three Caverns’ faith is not upheld,
Heavenly tributes are again demanded.
Yearly offerings dwindle,
Monthly provisions gradually fade.
Thus, great sins accumulate,
Sins amass, illness clings to the body.
To dispel past-life debts,
One must diligently cultivate blessings.
To repel the Five Pestilences,
Present an oral petition to the Three Heavens.
Supplicate facing north,
Decrees descend to dissolve past transgressions.

**The Hymn of the Thirty-Six Heavenly Devas:**
I see the world’s foolish people,
The foolish do not believe in the Dao.
Seeing others receive the Three Caverns’ teachings,
They slander them as deluded.
Unknowing of the divine incantations,
Flying immortals and earth gods created them.
Teaching others to receive the Yellow and Red,
Yet in doubt, they suffer punishment.
This life bears heavy sins,
All from past lives’ afflictions.
With reverence, bow to the Perfected,
Pray they come to dissolve suffering.
**The Hymn of the Ten Heavenly Great Spirits:**
I see the people of the world’s paths,
Foolish and wicked, they know not the true.
They call a lifetime a thousand years,
Unknowing of past lives.
They casually slander others,
Defame masters with threefold hearts.
They bring added punishment upon themselves,
Punishment scourges their bodies.
Illness stretches endlessly,
Whom can they blame for this?
Today, specially present this oral petition,
With sincere hearts, bow to the immortals.

**The Hymn of the Thirty-Six Heavenly Maidens:**
I see the world’s foolish people,
Creating their own walking corpses’ calamities.
Their hearts are not upright in serving the master,
How can they ascend to heaven’s halls?
This life bears heavy illness,
It is the retribution of past lives.
They whip and torment the suffering people,
Heaven thus bestows misfortune.
Today, for ten thousand kinds of illness,
Erect fasts and present oral petitions.
Reverently bow to all the true saints,
Devoutly repent to the ten directions.

**The Hymn of the Nine Heavenly Maidens:**
The Most High Lords of the ten directions,
Compassionately cherish all people.
They bestow the qi of the Middle Prime,
Yet none recognize the immortals and perfected.
Those who receive the registers yet commit evil,
With thievery ever in their hearts—
Thus they submit petitions and memorials,
To transcend this deluded fate.
With reverent hearts, they bow to the exalted saints,
Beseeching pardon for the source of their sins.

**The Hymn of the Ten Heavenly Perfected:**
I see all the foolish,
Whose hearts know not their own selves.
In poverty, they commit the ten evils,
Seeing goodness as if unheard.
Coveting petty wealth,
They incur great transgressions.
The source of sins accumulates day and night,
With guilt piled high—what repentance can be spoken?
Thus they suffer myriad illnesses,
Afflictions entwining their whole lives.
Today, they present oral petitions,
Memorials ascending to the gates of heaven.
Each bows with reverence,
As the immortals descend with great mercy.

**The Hymn of the Queen Mother of the West:**
The world’s customs are tangled,
Self-entangled in their own snares.
The Three Caverns’ teachings spread,
Yet fools do not heed them.
Seeing the Dharma, they do not cultivate,
Creating evil causes and conditions.
Greed harms the present,
Ensnared by the ten evils.
The three paths and eight difficulties,
The five destinies and ghostly realms—
Today, they establish blessings,
That seven ancestors may ascend to heaven.
The living endure long,
Turning toward the ten heavens.
Jade maidens descend,
Bestowing grace upon you.
Disciples bow thrice,
Receiving a thousand springs of fortune.

**Three Hymns of the Jade Maidens’ Journey Through the Three Heavens**

Far beyond the three realms,
There lies the Terrace of the Immortals’ Palace.
Countless perfected beings,
Riding dragons and phoenixes, arrive.
The Three Caverns transform the foolish,
Divine incantations dispel great calamities.
The Five Emperors summon demon kings,
Binding evil and restraining ghostly bones.
Should any dare to test this,
Heavenly soldiers will slay their ghostly forms.
Jade maidens chant to the ten directions,
Ghosts die, and people live anew.
All gods hear the wondrous Dharma,
Seven ancestors ascend to the heavenly court.
All attain liberation,
Together roaming the Purple Phoenix City.

Those who uphold the Dao and meet the immortals,
Keep their hearts upright.
Contemplating goodness, they ride dragons in flight,
While the faithless fall into darkest night.
For ten thousand kalpas, they dwell in gloom,
Gone forever, never to be reborn.
If you revere the passage through the three calamities,
Receive the wondrous scriptures from your master.
The Great Dao is most profound,
Revere your master as the sun and moon,
Filial piety moves the heavenly spirits.
Those who disbelieve the Three Caverns’ scriptures,
For ten thousand kalpas tread upon blades and frost.
Seven ancestors enter the dark realm,
Endless night, how vast and boundless!
Alas, the pain is unbearable—
Body perishes, descendants die.
Speak no slander, and mouths remain blameless;
Steal nothing, and ascend to heaven’s halls.
Serve your master to join the ranks of immortals,
Beholding the Most High Lord.
Disciples bow thrice,
Everlasting fortune and prosperity.

The Dao declares: In all fasts, rituals, and scripture recitations, in setting up altars, chanting incantations, presenting memorials, burning incense, and visualizing spirits, meditate upon the perfected—
Supplicating the Most High.
The mysterious, profound, and abyssal,
The samadhi divine incantations,
The treasure trove of great scriptures,
The numinous texts of the Upper Prime,
The Void and Empty Cavern,
The Three Heavens’ Perfected,
The Exalted Jade Emperor,
The Perfected of the Mysterious Center,
The Boundless Great Dao,
The responsive and perceptive of the ten directions—
The Heavenly Worthy, the Most High Lord Lao, the Heavenly Emperor,
The Lord of Life who commands the myriad Daoist saints,
The twenty-four venerable worthies,
The divine soldiers of heaven and earth,
The thirty-six perfected,
The immortals of the Five Emperors,
Those already perfected and those yet to be,
All lords of the mysterious and profound,
Every heavenly being—
Universally descend,
Witnessing and affirming our sincere devotion.
With united hearts and combined strength,
Encircle the homes of the fast’s patrons,
A thousand times, a hundredfold,
Bows drawn, arrows nocked,
Guarding and securing the four directions.
For every *zhang*, a general;
For every *chi*, a soldier.
Search within a hundred *li* of the patrons’ dwellings,
In every inch and span,
Seizing the five pestilential plagues and malevolent ghosts,
Slaying them upon capture.
Pity and pardon the disciples’ households,
Ensuring peace in all four seasons,
Dissolving ten thousand misfortunes like melting ice.
Official disputes and slanderous tongues shall never trouble them,
No floods or droughts shall arise,
Livestock shall flourish,
Graves and homes shall prosper,
Families shall thrive in health.
All intentions and endeavors,
Shall meet with success.
Ghosts and demons shall flee afar,
Evil spirits shall hide in flight.
Should any ghost or malefactor refuse to depart,
We dispatch the thirty-six heavenly immortals and divine soldiers,
To descend, seize, and bind them,
Slaying them one by one,
Allowing none to escape.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the Most High’s oral decree commands.

Further, in accordance with the *Nüqing Veritable Writ* and the statutes of the divine ordinances:
The Dao declares: From this day forward, in all lands under heaven, should any suffer from plagues year after year, it is the demon kings—Wumingjiu and their legions—who bring calamities, roaming the world to afflict the people, accompanying the wandering souls of seven generations of ancestors to spread pestilence and slaughter the populace. If any of virtuous heart, moved to preserve and protect, invite masters of the Three Caverns to establish ritual altars, recite scriptures, chant incantations, present memorials according to the Dharma, and hold fasts and offerings, praying to the Five Emperors and the immortals, their merit shall be boundless. They shall dispel plagues and bestow blessings, their merit unmatched. The wandering souls of seven generations shall ascend to the azure heavens, the nine lineages of ancestors shall be liberated in the Vermilion Mound. They shall transcend the three realms, attaining freedom in the six voids. The people shall enjoy peace and prosperity, the old and young shall live in tranquility. Their lifespans shall be extended, and they shall attain immortality and transcend the world. Fields shall yield double harvests, silkworms shall spin eightfold threads. Graves and homes shall be harmonious, livestock shall multiply. Public and private affairs shall be serene, disasters and pestilence shall vanish. The lord and king of the realm shall surpass Yao and Shun in virtue. The golden branches shall flourish, the jade leaves shall remain evergreen. The world shall know great peace, weapons shall be stilled. Governors and magistrates shall rule with the Dao, bringing peace to the people. No calamities shall arise, no rebellions shall occur. The four serpents shall withdraw their venom, the six thieves shall cease their depredations. We now transmit this scripture to dissolve your disasters and avert your sufferings—why not receive it with reverence? Those who receive it devoutly shall gain boundless blessings. But those who deceive their masters, betray the Dao, disobey the scriptures’ words, commit the five rebellious acts, are unfilial, kill the innocent, exploit the orphaned and poor, or harm the good and virtuous—such sins shall pile high as mountains and seas. Whether in past lives or present, for men and women, old and young, high and low, from the age of seven onward, none shall escape these grievous sins.

Now, therefore, we burn incense to make universal repentance, beseeching that all sins be swept away and no punishments be meted out. From this moment after the turning of the scriptures, you ghostly multitudes, together with the demon kings and their legions, and all spirits and specters, shall follow the directives of this true scripture. Should any fierce or overbearing ghostly brigands defy our edict, the Ten Heavenly Divine Generals shall be dispatched to cut them down at once, leaving no descendants.

*Recite urgently as per the* **Taishang’s Oral Command to Slay Ghosts and Pacify the People.**

**The Fourteenth Scroll of the** *Taishang Dongyuan Divine Incantations Sutra* **concludes.**

**The Fifteenth Scroll of the** *Taishang Dongyuan Divine Incantations Sutra*
**The Step of Lu: The Release from Torment**

The Dao speaks: We cannot bear to witness you, the people of the world, so shallow in fortune and virtue. From the moment you emerged from the womb into this world, from the age of seven when you learned to speak, every gesture, every word, every thought has been tainted by the five poisons, while the six thieves vie for dominance. Never have you shown kindness; only evil arises, and you delight in killing. Thus, the Three Corpses record your deeds, and the Seven Ghosts inscribe your names. On every *jiazi* and *gengshen* day, they report to the Heavenly Courts, where your sins accumulate to three thousand. The celestial ledgers issue decrees to the Central Dipper’s bureau, commanding the star officials of your fate to seize your three hun and seven po souls and consign them to the Earth Prison of Mount Tai. From there, your case falls into the Register of Life and Death, and your grave offenses are transferred to Fengdu, plunging you into the Twenty-Four Hells. Even if your sins are not compounded, you shall remain in the Eighteen Hells of Mount Tai, lashed day and night, tormented without cease. Once your confessions are fixed and your records made clear, the hell wardens raise their forks, and the clerks drag you forward. The Great King Yama rages, for your crimes admit no pardon. Each is measured by its statute, and you must repay your karmic debts. Some shall be reborn in the heavenly realms, some in the earthly, some among humans, some as ghosts, some as beasts. Some shall live, some fall ill; some shall die, some linger in death’s threshold. Some shall be sated to death, some starved; some scorched, some frozen; some drowned, some burned; some crushed by earth, maimed by wood, or slain by metal blades. Some shall perish from snakebites, tiger maulings, or the jaws of dragons and turtles; some from the goring of oxen, the trampling of horses, or the bites of dogs. Some shall die by blades, cudgels, or warfare; some by lightning, hail, or tempest. Some, though not yet dead, shall suffer every manner of foul disease: the five-colored swellings of *qi*, emaciation, madness, epilepsy, scabies, leprosy, ulcers, sores, scars, consumption, malaria, blindness, deafness, muteness, stuttering, throat closures, nasal obstructions, vertigo, hunchbacks, protruding chests, twisted limbs, swollen bellies, heart pain, vomiting, and retching. These myriad afflictions, too numerous to name, are the retribution for your past sins, which you have failed to recognize.

We, now entrusted with the salvation of the people, cannot bear to see you endure such suffering and perpetual calamity. Thus, we specially dispatch the Radiant Net Realized One to carry this scripture through the world, delivering all beings from the five sufferings, dissolving disasters, averting misfortunes, rescuing the imperiled, healing the sick, and eradicating the roots of all woes. Should any among the people—whether commoners or officials—suffer from these afflictions, or be entangled in lawsuits and imprisoned for years, or face droughts, floods, locusts, warfare, or epidemics that no physician can cure, let them invite a high-ranking master of the Three Caverns to purify and establish a sacred altar. Let them turn the scriptures, recite the incantations, submit memorials, set up fasts, and perform rites to thank the Five Emperors. Let the immortals pace the void, chanting praises and circling the altar. By the spontaneous power of the Most High, the assembly of the Venerable One shall gather. The merit of the heavenly soldiers is boundless; all sins shall disperse, demonic legions perish, epidemics vanish, households prosper, families thrive, states and courts know peace, droughts and floods cease, fields and silkworms yield double, and livestock flourish. We now chant for you to gather poisons and withdraw pestilence—listen with reverence.

The Daoist assembly intones:
**The Venerable Lord of the Eastern Azure,** named the Numinous Goumang,
The Brahmin maidens wander the vast sky, brushing the Jade Capital afar.
The Great Vehicle unites the Three Heavens; its hosts command the demon legions.
The eight tones resound through the ten lands; nine dragons bear the cloud chariot.
Establish the fast and achieve great merit—through the long night, light shall dawn.
The drum of the true Dao resounds; all demons shatter their essence.
The demon kings bow in submission, and only then are they spared punishment.
Virtuous spirits guard the gates; the mighty warriors marshal the ten thousand spirits.
The Dao’s *qi* flows widely; kin and family all know peace.
Plagues and poisons vanish; the people all attain long life.
Together they uphold the supreme Dao, journeying to the Purple Phoenix City.

**The Flame Emperor of the Southern Realm,** named Yama of the Eight Directions,
His flying chariot rides the cloud carriage; the Ten Perfected wander the Three Heavens.
Jade maidens sing in the clouds; golden light overflows the cinnabar mounds.
Today the Dharma wheel turns; the Brahmanic tones shake the nine peaks.
The Heavenly Emperor commands the demon soldiers; the winds rise, then naturally cease.
The three luminaries shine brilliantly; all demons sink into the nine depths.
Should any dare test this power, the mighty warriors shall strike off their heads.
The sons of the Heavenly Emperor—what ghost would dare linger?
Thus, the defiant shall be boiled in cauldrons; their bodies cooked.
Thousands upon thousands shall be beheaded; not one shall be spared.
Establish the fast to gather demonic essence; *wangliang* spirits shall be seized at once.
The majesty of the Great Dao is weighty; the divine wind sweeps away evil.
Plague ghosts vanish utterly; the people know no disaster or sorrow.

**The Divine Ruler of the Western Harvest,** named the Mighty Juni,
The three luminaries hang in the vast void, shining brightly in the four directions.
The eight tones and thirty-two transformations—how could the hundred demons not be crushed?
Today we establish the field of merit; the divine incantations shatter the demonic hordes.
The lamps’ light reaches far; the long night brightens at last.
The winds still, the rains cease; demons are slain, and evil bound.

Whoever dares to defy shall be bound and sent to the nethermost hell.
Golden blades slash in all directions; iron staves strike in wild fury.
The Way’s procession eradicates a hundred evils; burning incense dispels a thousand calamities.
The Daoist’s heart is pure in intent; through accumulated goodness, even the dead are revived.
All demons fear true rectitude and dare not disobey, cowering in hiding.
Those who honor their masters and revere the Great Dao find the Dao’s *qi* naturally drawn to them.
The foolish and deluded fail to learn, while the wise ever abide in its shelter.
They spare neither wealth nor body, prizing instead the reverence that soars through empty space.

In the northern realm of Youtai, the Divine Ruler is named Xuanming.
The four seasons’ gates stand vast; the five *qi* shine resplendent.
All filth and evil are swept away; heaven and earth become pristine.
The Most High’s majesty is stern; malevolent demons perish without rebirth.
Whoever dares to defy shall be seized and delivered to the Celestial Soldiers.
Thousands upon thousands shall be beheaded; tens of thousands utterly destroyed in form.
Yama severs demonic specters; the Northern Emperor annihilates demonic essence.
The divine wind sweeps away misfortune; no evil may linger.
The Most Sage’s benevolence flows forth, and all things flourish universally.
Should any defy this decree, the divine soldiers shall sever them limb from limb.

The Central Deity of Wuji, the Yellow Emperor, governs all affairs.
The Three Qin rule the eight directions; the Celestial Array radiates heavenly brilliance.
Divine light blazes forth, suddenly dispelling the darkest night.
The Perfect Dao’s grace is universal; all beings return to its shelter.
Today we establish the myriad fasts; no evil dares to draw near.
The winds still, no branch stirs; blessings and virtue tower high.
Plague demons must flee far; billions upon billions are slain without remnant.
When the people suffer illness and distress, they come to invoke the divine incantations and fasts.
The afflicted recover; plague demons are crushed of themselves.
The Devas seize demonic specters; the Perfected Ones pursue evil and wrong.
The Most High’s golden edict commands: "Begone swiftly, delay not!"

In the northeast, the son of Gen, his spirit governs the yin seasons.
He upholds the Most High’s teachings, distinguishing good from evil.
Deceit cannot assail the true; transgressors merit execution.
The Most Sage protects the people; those who harm them incur heavenly punishment.
The Cavern Abyss is governed with clarity and solemnity; the Three Mysteries’ law is stern.
Divine incantations destroy demonic hordes; all perverse spirits are annihilated.
Eliminate evil, and evil ceases; slay demons, and demons are extinguished.
Divine soldiers cover the earth; the numinous wind sweeps forth across the land.
The myriad spirits gather from the ten directions; the thousand disasters of the nine yin realms are stilled.
Public and private affairs know no hindrance; the living and the dead alike find liberation.

In the southeast, the domain of Xun, the earth’s gates spread their nets.
The nets span the heavens; no demon may pass through.
The Five Peaks are at peace; the Four Seas do not surge.
No evil dares stir; the decree restrains all demons.
Should any demon dare to rebel, it shall be slain and delivered to Dharā.
Its head shall be shattered into hundreds of pieces; its form utterly consumed.
We rescue the people from suffering; how dare calamity and distress persist?
The Three Officials proclaim the edict, as in the *Scripture of Lady Green*.
In the southwest, the mother of Kun, divine incantations gather demonic essence.
Heaven and earth’s spirits are restrained; pestilence dares not advance.
Should any refuse to comply, the spirits shall sever your form.
Today we establish the great fast, slaying demons to govern life.
The Three Luminaries flow as one in radiance; the Nine Dark Realms are universally illumined.
Brightness pervades the ten directions; no demon may conceal its form.
Thus, for those whose illness persists, they shall be seized and delivered to the Seven Stars.
The divine wind sweeps away iniquity; evil naturally subsides.
The Most Venerable Lord’s luminous edict commands the slaughter of all demonic hosts.

In the northwest, the father of Qian, his spirit penetrates the light of heaven.
The Sage Emperor pities the common people; how could the hundred demons harm them?
Thus, the celestial nets are cast, spread throughout the ten directions.
Divine soldiers capture plague demons, allowing none to hide.
Each is slain in turn and cast into boiling cauldrons.
All are utterly destroyed, none may escape.
Today we establish merit; blessings flow to dispel misfortune.
The ill recover; the healthy enjoy enduring well-being.
Dwellings and households are all purified; demonic *qi* vanishes entirely.
Heavenly spirits gather in protection; the entire household enjoys eternal good fortune.

The Emperors of the Ten Heavens above issue forth from the Great Brahma Gate.
They nurture the people of Jambudvīpa, prolonging the kalpa’s existence.
How dare the myriad demons, spreading poison, slay the people?
Death and suffering lie strewn about; their grievances reach the heavens above.
The Most High dispatches the great army, hurling fire to gather the hundred plagues.
The Three and Five sever demonic paths; the Seven Stars block the demon gates.
Seized and bound, they are delivered to the celestial prison; only then are the people preserved.

The earth spirits below, their nets span the nine regions.
They pacify the Four Seas and secure the Five Peaks.
They restrain and subdue demonic ghosts, preventing them from spreading their hundred poisons.
The Most Sage protects the people, thus issuing this luminous and majestic decree.
Should any defy it, they shall be captured and delivered to the celestial prison.
Iron hooks shall pierce the demons’ eyes; golden blades sever their hands and feet.
Divine incantations slay malevolent demons; the myriad evils are annihilated to the last.
The people bear the Dao’s grace, no longer knowing sorrow or weeping.
They escape the inauspicious year, soon to witness an age of peace and harmony.
We bow to the Perfected Ones of the ten directions, forever free from calamity and poison.

The Dao declares: In this world, the faithful followers within the Middle Kingdom uphold the Dao’s teachings.
Now the Ten Heavenly Emperor Lords solemnly proclaim the Cavern Abyss of the Three Mysteries.
With numinous sounds and divine hymns, they perform fasts and establish jiao rites.
You must recite and chant, delighting the spirits and destroying demons—merit without bound.
Disasters are dispelled, blessings sought; virtue and fortune descend at once.
Now I shall expound; you should listen attentively.

In the Eastern Nine Radiance Heaven, the Qingling Palace of the Zhen Palace:
Jade maidens strike golden bells; demon kings beat the dharma drums.
The Emperor Lord issues his decree; nine dragons race through clouds and rain.
Banners and standards descend from empty space; the Ten Perfected Ones perform their wondrous dance.
They deliver the souls of the long night, able to heal the suffering of living beings.
Celestial Soldiers brandish their precious blades; Mighty Warriors part the mists.
They scour and seize demonic ghosts; the Flying Celestials pacify the roads.
The Three Caverns now radiate light, illuminating every household that performs the fast.

In the Southern Palace of Three Qi, the Chongli Hall blazes with the Great Sun.
Flowers scatter across the ten heavens; the jade chariot gleams with ninefold brilliance.
Crimson phoenixes bear the jade seal; fire dragons draw the precious banner.

The Mystic Maiden sings of long life; the Azure Youth burns descending incense.
Myriad upon myriad array celestial soldiers; thousands upon thousands slay demon kings.
The Great Emperor descends the celestial talisman, sweeping away all inauspicious omens.
Extinguishing the ghosts of the Six Caverns, each is cast into boiling汤.
The true Dharma has now been proclaimed; blessings overflow the provinces.

In the Western Palace of Seven Qi, the Dui Palace flies its golden blades.
The jade chariot soars lightly; immortal staves array the empty sky.
Cranes dance in lofty spirals; precious pendants chime with delicate sounds.
Within stand the Ten Thousand Eternities’ spirits, expounding the merits of the Three Caverns.
They deliver those lost in the dark paths, ascending into the vastness of the Great Void.
Golden soldiers by the thousands and tens of thousands; no demon may encounter them.
The true teaching flourishes in the nation’s halls; demon-slaying leaves no trace behind.
Now by the grace of the Great Dao, may the six dragons be universally blessed.

In the Northern Palace of Five Qi, the Dark Warrior of the Kan Palace, deep and profound.
Water essence forms its palaces; immortal courts remain ever spring-like.
Black waves stretch boundlessly deep; Fengdu stands peerlessly high.
The Emperor Lord recites the Cavern Sutra; both hidden and manifest realms hear it.
Demonic ghosts assume no proper form; shattered bones and remnant souls are condemned.
The Heavens of Luo possess fierce beasts, whose breath darkens the Four Seas.
Flying bells and fire wheels purify and pacify heaven and earth.
Through the power of those who perform the fast, all enter the gate of myriad blessings.

The Central Deity of Wu and Ji, the Five Lands enthroned in honor.
Crimson gates tower into the great void; precious halls conceal Kunlun.
The Twelve Scriptures of Long Life, spoken from the golden mouth on jade slips.
With reverent force they array the clouds, a hundredfold encircling the fast’s gate.
Heavenly Soldiers shatter black poisons; Mighty Warriors slay the Yellow Pestilence.
The Emperor Lord’s demon-slaying talisman sweeps away the myriad heretical hordes.
Immortal youths strike the jade bells, washing and delivering the souls of the long night.
Incense lamps shine brightly; karmic retribution is diligently bestowed.
Blessings and grace abound.

In the Northeast, the Pure Brahman Heaven, the Gen Palace deep and clear.
Jade maidens scatter precious incense; the Perfected Sovereign expounds the Cavern Sutra.
Flutes play the music of simurghs and phoenixes; winds harmonize with cloud-borne melodies.
They deliver the nine sunken souls, all ascending to the Purple Cloud City.
A thousand leagues turn the sword wheels; ten thousand leagues array celestial soldiers.
All demonic ghosts that bring harm today cannot conceal their forms.
The thunder dragons all obey the decree, condemning and slaying by the hands of Heavenly Soldiers.
Fortune rises as misfortune perishes; a thousand years of peace and tranquility are preserved.

In the Southeast, the Brahman Treasure Palace, the Xun realm where azure clouds gather.
Divine soldiers but chant the mantra, and the Three Realms’ demons are overthrown.
Merits now towering, the azure sea knows no waves.
Jade maidens sing the empty cavern hymn; Azure Youths step the void song.
Good deeds are now established; the immortal path lightly treads the cloud net.
Banners and canopies intersperse flying flowers; divine soldiers multiply with each step.
Supreme Saints descend from empty space; the fast’s blessings rise high and towering.
The Three Officials and Twelve Bureaus grandly proclaim the Most High’s statutes.

In the Southwest, the Brahman Qi City, the Kun Palace of the Great Mystic Rosy Clouds.
Ninefold light congeals in radiance; the Ten Caverns’ cloud chariots ascend.
The Void Sovereign discourses on the secret sutras; assembled immortals scatter heavenly flowers.
Golden dragons fly with crimson flames; iron-faced ones seize the malevolent.
Bright lamps illumine the Nine Springs; immortal chants nurture the seeds of virtue.
*Wangliang* and *chimei* demons, each is consigned to the golden fork.
The Three Caverns now prevail; the Ten Thousand Perfected follow the Ten Flowers.
Lamps are lit without bound; merits complete the pure and tranquil home.

In the Northwest, called the Gate of Heaven, the Qian Palace where purple clouds run deep.
Exquisite music plays resoundingly; precious halls are fragrant and profound.
The Three Heavens offer no other path but to illumine the pure and empty heart.
The fast’s merits and sutra’s power can dispel the sounds of sorrow and suffering.
Those who cultivate ascend to heaven’s halls; calamities spare them cold and heat.
The Great Dao magnifies the Three Caverns; immortals chant in due order.
Dare any demonic forces act wantonly, their recklessness betraying their hearts?
They guard the fast’s precincts, flying immortals in the Treasure Flower Grove.

Above, in the Boundless Realm, the Thirty-Two Pure Heavens.
Within dwell the long-lived, countless immortals without end.
The Void Sovereign expounds the true sutras; immortal chants spiral through empty space.
Multitudes of dragons drive in profusion; the Five Emperors’ chariots soar lightly.
The Most High issues his decree; the Three Realms condemn demonic heresies.
Purifying the Five Turbidities, they wish to escape the searing fires of suffering.
Delivering the souls of the nether darkness, they uphold the sacred words of their masters.
Those who perform the fast establish merit, generation after generation receiving honor and ascent.

Below, the Twelve Perfected Ones of the Four Seas, boundless and vast.
Those who perform the fast and observe the precepts command the demons, decreeing the expulsion of heretical evils.
Incense wafts azure smoke; lamps array red lotus flowers.
Jade maidens’ songs never end; blessings fill countless households.
The Sun Valley determines the Cold Pool; the Five Cloud Chariots deliver.
Mystic clarity matches the Three Lights; let not mists and rains be distant.
Today, worshipping the Ten Directions, celestial soldiers encircle a hundredfold.
Compassion’s supreme power follows wishes to feast in the Golden Flower.

The Dao speaks: I now specially dispatch the Great Lineage Dharma Master
to universally proclaim the Disaster-Dispelling Step-Void for your households afflicted by illness, hardship, and suffering.
Now, the thirty-six Heavenly Demon Kings all submit in devotion.
From this day forward, you shall no longer bring calamity and harm to the world’s people.
Having heard the true words of the Great Dao, all shall reverently uphold them.
Each bows their head and listens to the ode:

The Great Dao emerges from the formless,
Mystic clarity illumines all beings.
Heavenly beings transform the foolish and lost;
Immortals transcend the cloud journey.
If one can rescue from the Eight Perils,
This Dao grants long life.
The ultimate principle is so still,
The formless so profoundly obscure.
The Most High sits on the Mystic Terrace;
Jade maidens chant the Great Clarity.
The Perfected remain without action,
Yet you have attained Dao’s completion.
All heavens pay homage to the Most High;
The Three and Five naturally follow.
Flying immortals roam the Three Realms;
Perfected Ones chant amidst the clouds.
Saints utter no sound,
Who can know this heart?
The True and Upright Great Unity transforms,
Without sign, one ascends to heaven.
Lions roar in the great wilderness;
Phoenixes chant in harmony with the seasons.
Immortals come to bow their heads,
For you alone know the mystery.
The Three and Five shine in timely splendor;
Mystic clarity responds to things’ changes.
The formless does not name itself,
Vast and boundless, it enters the infinite.
If one can grasp this principle,
What prevents becoming immortal?
The formless has no constant name,
Only the heart’s resolve endures in form.

The Heavenly Venerable emerges from the dark and profound,
And the Dao is born within this very realm.
The wise who study the Luminous Teachings
May ascend to the court of the Most High.

Heavenly beings hold crimson blossoms,
Jade maidens wave jade mushrooms.
Divine beings gather to attend,
Flying immortals establish the imperial foundation.
The Primordial Ultimate’s many mysterious disciples
Are beyond the thoughts of this world.
Immortals live for ten thousand kalpas,
A thousand years like a single spring.
Countless ages are but an evening,
How could worldly names suffice for discussion?
If one possesses the bones of immortals,
Only then does this heart respond.

The Three Caverns flow to the ten directions,
The Luminous Teachings must be propagated by men.
Loyalty and faith uphold the scriptures and precepts,
Just as the Five Peaks are sacred.
Without the bones to soar aloft,
How could one ascend and fly?
Fix the heart beyond the Three Realms,
Let thoughts drift to the Jade Capital.
Perfected Ones chant in the void,
Jade maidens glide through the emptiness.
Today, we pay homage to the Heavenly Venerable,
Bowing our heads to the Jade Emperor.

---

At the time of purification, three hymns:
The Most High is profoundly mysterious,
The supreme principle leaves no trace.
Wondrous enlightenment is sung in the void,
Immortals chant amidst the emptiness.
If not a scholar of the Yellow Forest,
Who could propagate this merit?
Ascending through the clouds in reverence,
The distant heavenly beings appear.
Mouths recite the true secret formulas,
Eight dragons ascend to the Purple Court.
If not a guest of the highest realms,
How could one embody this scripture?
The supreme principle transcends distant shores,
Where there is existence, there is no unraveling.
The Mystic Artisan illumines the Three Luminaries,
Perfected Ones receive the model and standard.
Immortals bow to the flowing cinnabar,
None fail to prostrate in reverence.

---

Establishing the Great Purification Rite for three nights:
Wondrous are the Three Cavern Scriptures,
Divinely guarded, welcomed by nine dragons.
Establishing the rite dispels anxious hearts,
Allowing one to wander the Purple Phoenix City.
Meritorious resolve accumulates over ten thousand kalpas,
How dare demons disobey?
Clear and resonant, the eight tones resound,
The capital of the Most High in the ten directions.
The Three Caverns are best studied with wholehearted devotion,
To guide and transform, delivering sentient beings.
When the scripture is expounded,
Three bows are made while listening to the teachings.
Beyond the distant Three Realms,
Vast and boundless, profoundly obscure.
Now we establish the great purification rite,
Lighting lamps to illuminate the mysterious stars.
Suddenly, a young phoenix exhales,
Summoning the divine to muster demonic troops.

The Dao speaks: "I reside above the Three Heavens,
Unable to bear seeing the multitudes of your world bring calamity upon themselves.
Sickness, death, and ruin are rampant,
All of your own making.
From the age of seven,
The six thieves and ten evils arise in competition.
Body and mind are constantly recorded by the Three Corpses for their transgressions,
Reported to the celestial bureaus to determine the length of your lives,
Before they are ordered to pursue and seize you.
Thus, the celestial bureaus issue decrees,
And demon kings spread plagues and diseases.
All because of the sins committed by your body, heart, mouth, and hands.
Now, for the sake of you and all beings,
I broadly proclaim repentance.
Let each demon king and ghostly lord
Hear these scriptural words,
Naturally generating shame and remorse,
Withdrawing their poisons and diseases.

You, the people of this world,
Listen with a tranquil heart
As I recount the origins of your sins."

The Dao speaks: "Now I tell you, sentient beings,
From the age of seven,
You have incurred the retribution of scolding wind and cursing rain.
You have incurred the retribution of disrespecting Heaven and Earth.
Or disrespecting the sun, moon, and stars.
Or cursing and reviling the gods of Heaven and Earth.
Or exposing your form to the Three Luminaries.
Or resenting and cursing ghosts and spirits.
Or invoking and summoning taboo names of underworld deities.
Or failing to revere the precepts, defiling and disdaining the wondrous.
Or disrespecting parents and teachers.
Or facing the Three Luminaries to urinate or defecate.
Or disrespecting scriptures and teachings, leaking secret texts.
Or slandering the loyal, good, and wise.
Or using youth to bully elders, lacking harmony and obedience.
Or using light scales and small measures when giving to others.
Or using heavy scales and large measures when taking for oneself.
Or abandoning the Dao to embrace heterodoxy.
Or acting unlawfully.
Or encouraging others to do evil, forsaking their good roots.
Or disrespecting the teachings, sabotaging others’ success.
Or persistently acting with malice, concealing good and promoting evil.
Or acting as a false master, lacking spiritual efficacy, deceitfully speaking as a god, ruining others’ hearts and affairs.
Or violating graves and disturbing tombs, startling the spirits.
Or offending household gods, defiling wells and hearths.
Or casting filth into water and fire.
Or defiling and disdaining the earth and soil.
Or polluting gold, silver, copper, and iron.
Or borrowing without repayment, speaking falsely with the heart.
Or mocking others for doing good, desiring them to do evil.
Or resenting others’ good deeds, delighting in unlawfulness.
Or seeing others cultivate merit and establish virtue, begrudging and refusing to bestow.
Or praying for blessings and making vows without reverence.
Or buying and selling Daoist and Buddhist scriptures, images, and sacred objects.
Or cursing the innocent, implicating ordinary people.
Or bullying and scheming to seize others’ property.
Or drinking wine and eating meat, pretending drunkenness to invoke gods and ghosts.
Or indulging in lust and desire, disregarding kinship.
Or conducting purification rites and offering rituals without following the proper procedures.
Or failing to rescue in times of urgency, refusing to assist in danger, desiring others’ downfall.
Or making vows to cultivate and construct merit, yet failing to complete them.
Or receiving treatment from masters when ill, yet not understanding the texts and petitions.
Or relying on alcohol to act wildly, offending elders and superiors, destroying everything.
Or seeing others’ wives and women, harboring lustful thoughts.
Or keeping purification vows yet breaking precepts, arrogantly disdaining the immortals.
Or killing living beings, trampling insects and ants.
Or being greedy, never knowing contentment.
Or giving free rein to jealousy, beating and scolding subordinates, refusing to provide clothing.
Or maliciously altering contracts, seizing others’ fields.
Or when drunk, or in times of urgency, making solemn vows, then breaking them with deceitful hearts."

Or harboring scheming intentions, all manner of wicked and malevolent offenses.
Or enjoying abundant clothing and food, with all desires fulfilled, yet failing to feel shame for heaven’s gifts.
Such offenses are too numerous to recount in full.
Now, in the midst of this recitation, confessing past transgressions and making vows, may all sins be swept away and mercy granted at once.
May sins sink into the nine depths of earth, and blessings arise from the ten directions.
In life after life, may one always encounter the Great Dao, faithfully receive and uphold it.

*The Fifteenth Scroll of the Supreme Cavernous Divine Incantations Sutra* concludes.

*The Sixteenth Scroll of the Supreme Cavernous Divine Incantations Sutra*
*The Chapter on Commanding Ghosts*

The Dao speaks: In the ten directions of the world, among the common people—men and women—if afflicted by ghosts and spirits, falling ill or dying;
Or suffering from madness, running wildly, speaking alone in delirium;
Or struck by cholera, vomiting and diarrhea, with unceasing muscle spasms;
Or plagued by epidemic fevers, jaundice, toxic heat diseases, swelling, and distension;
Or harmed by fire, water, bandits, or theft, losing wealth and livestock, facing slander and lawsuits, unjust imprisonment, attacks by birds and beasts, chickens and dogs, bloodshed and strange omens, miscarriages, deaths of men and women, unfulfilled vows, all manner of misfortune, restless graves and homes, and depletion of livelihood—
For all such afflictions and hardships, the impoverished and unlucky should seek a wise master, receive my precepts and registers, revere and honor them, and refrain from all evil.
On days of calamity, bathe, don proper attire, burn incense, pay homage to the sutras, sit upright with a calm mind, compose the spirit and quiet the thoughts, hold incense, and knock the teeth thirty-six times.
Recite the incantation:
*Crowned with the Vermilion Sparrow, treading the Dark Warrior beneath the feet,
Supported by the Azure Dragon on the left, seated upon the White Tiger on the right,
With the Verdant Essence Sword and halberds before me, and the Golden Hammer and Iron Axe behind,
Heavenly Ding warriors guard my front and rear.
A hundred Yellow Slaves—all malevolent ghosts and thieves—flee a thousand miles away.
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!*

The Dao speaks: In the world, there are countless ghosts that harm the people; I now know all your names.
The Red-Headed Ghost King of Slaughter, standing two *zhang* tall, commands thirty-six trillion slaughter ghosts, each wielding a red staff, roaming the world to claim lives.
There are also the Three Heavenly Great Demons, the Nine Heavenly Great Demons, the Thirty-Six Heavenly Great Demons, the Ten Directions’ Slaughter Ghosts, the Ghost-Commanding Great Kings, and thirty-eight myriad beings.
Further, the Eastern Divine Spirit, the Western Divine Spirit, the Southern Divine Spirit, and the Northern Divine Spirit, each leading three hundred million attendants, afflict men and women, depleting their resources.
I know all your names—flee a thousand miles away!
If you do not depart, I will dispatch the Eight Divisions of Enforcing Soldiers to strike you down.
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!

The Dao speaks: Great Demon Kings Xia Yin, Wu Yan Chi, Bo Hong Gong, and others, along with the Thirty-Nine Myriad Great Expulsion Generals, twelve myriad great soldiers, four hundred thousand Red Bow Great Troops, nineteen thousand Regional Strongmen, forty-nine myriad Life-Commanding Officers, and eight hundred ten thousand Heavenly Slaughter Marquis Great Soldiers—
All shall heed my command, gather the thousand spirits and myriad demons for all good men and women, drive them beyond the borders, and spare the innocent.
I further summon the thirty-six Heavenly Great Kings with seven myriad soldiers, the ninety myriad great soldiers of the Nine Heavens, eighty myriad Heavenly Spirits who never depart, thirty myriad Heavenly Ding warriors, four hundred thousand Incense-Transmitting Jade Maidens, four hundred thousand Incense-Attending Golden Chapters, thirty-six Brahma Kings, and nine thousand myriad Righteous Soldiers.
Upon hearing this sutra, you must come to protect the person [named], causing ghosts and demons to retreat and all illnesses to be cured.
I further summon four hundred thousand Harmonious Might Warriors, thirty-six myriad Hundred-Tongued Official Soldiers, and others.
Wherever this sutra is recited and incantations are proclaimed, you must reconcile the person’s family and relatives, ensuring internal and external harmony, peace for kin, and stability for the household.
Guard the person, expel all external ghosts and demonic spirits, and drive them away.
Those who protect diligently shall be rewarded according to the statutes; those who defy me shall incur the punishment of the Three Officials.
Beware, beware!
Knock the teeth three times, swallow saliva three times.

The Dao speaks: If devout men and women, rulers, officials, commoners, monks, minor immortals, officials of all ranks, mountain sages, courageous scholars, the noble and the lowly—upon hearing this sutra—can believe and accept it,
Know that such a person has, for countless kalpas, been an immortal, born from the heavens.
Though briefly in the world, they will soon ascend as immortals.
Some may achieve liberation through simulated death, or feign extinction, ascending to the heavens never to die again.
For this reason, I briefly expound this sutra.
Yet many in the world do not believe in the Dao; people’s hearts are wicked. Upon hearing this sutra, they scorn it, mock the divine incantations, disbelieve the sacred words, dismiss it as sorcery, disrespect the true sutra, deceive their masters, and belittle the Dao, refusing to believe.
Such people come from the Three Evil Realms, harboring malice and venom, their dark sins unresolved, their karmic obstacles heavy—this is why they are so.
In this life, they suffer afflictions: greed, ignorance, and delusion bind them like silkworms in a cocoon, with no hope of escape.
Or they contract severe illnesses, their bodies ravaged by jaundice and epidemics, haunted by plague ghosts that never leave their side, their livelihoods failing, their endeavors thwarted. Even if they attain high office, they soon fall from grace.
Or they face mutilation, swiftly reduced to lowly status; temporary wealth and nobility give way to poverty. If struck by grave illness, their families perish without cause.
Or their bodies fester with malignant sores, leprosy, oozing pus and blood, or they suffer from scabies, syphilitic sores, edema, *qi* diseases, carbuncles, silkworm-like ulcers, and boils—plague diseases spread by ghosts, infecting neighbors.
If they seek shamans, their suffering worsens; even with good medicine, they cannot be cured. Their lives end, leaving lingering misfortune—this is the heavenly punishment for scorning this sutra.

Such persons shall again be cast into the Avīci Hell, confined within its dark prisons and barred cells, for kalpas uncounted without reprieve. Only after this shall they emerge, reborn as birds and beasts, the six kinds of livestock—despised and abhorred by humankind, their names unwelcome to the ear. They shall feed on filth and foulness, even mingled with excrement. Their desires shall never be sated; they shall bear heavy burdens in toil and suffering, lashed by whips and cudgels. Once they lose the human form, ten thousand kalpas shall pass before they regain it. Such is the retribution for mocking this sutra.

Now I look upon the beings of the lower realms, and see their suffering and joy, their lifespans long or short, their stations noble or base, their deeds unequal. Thus do I pity all those tormented by suffering, as a mother pities her infant child. I exhort the foolish and ignorant to revere and believe, that all may be liberated and ascend to the heavens, spared the afflictions of the womb, ever possessing bodies pure and free. They shall wander with me, and I proclaim this verse:

*The samādhi spreads far and wide;*
*Those with karmic affinity may hear it.*
*The wise at once believe and receive;*
*For kalpas they shall be noble ones.*
*Though briefly born in the world of men,*
*Soon they shall ascend as immortals.*
*To deliver all beings, I come to this cause.*

I dispatch the devas and humans, the true immortals of countless kalpas, to teach and transform the benighted. Yet the wicked refuse to believe, and further mock this sutra, declaring its teachings devoid of spiritual efficacy. They show no reverence or love, and in this life they suffer retribution: afflicted by disease, plagued by pestilence ghosts and demon kings who come to destroy their households, their kin and wives and children all perish, their deaths still insufficient. Their souls descend into hell, where for ten thousand kalpas there is no release, cast into the darkness of *qi*. Imprisoned in heavy fetters, they endure torment most grievous. Through the long night of darkness, they emerge at last as birds and beasts, feeding on foulness, or reborn as livestock. Scorned by humankind, they bear heavy loads beneath the whip. Such is the punishment for those who slight this sutra.

Yet those who believe and receive it shall gain blessings and ascend to heaven. Those with the bones of immortals shall uphold the *Samādhi Sutra*. You who cultivate the Middle Way shall behold the True Lord.

When the Most High had spoken this verse, the Great Demon Kings of the Nine Heavens, the thirty-six Heavenly Demon Kings, the celestial maidens, the devas, Brahmā kings, demon kings, and their retinues, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s hymn, rejoiced in their hearts. As one, they rose, prostrated themselves, and bowed twice, saying: “We, the Great Brahmā and Demon Kings, together with our followers, shall ever guard and protect, traversing the world. For those who uphold this sutra, we shall ensure freedom from disease, capturing and slaying the pestilence ghosts, malevolent spirits, and demonic plagues that bring calamity, that their illnesses may swiftly be cured. May all their wishes be fulfilled, their legal troubles resolved, their endeavors successful. If any evil demons, perverse spirits, or wicked ghosts disobey the Most High’s command, we shall seize and rend them into ten thousand pieces, grinding them to dust, and show no mercy. We, the Demon Kings, now swear together: we shall not commit evil, but pray to transform our demonic forms, ever walking the immortal path, drawing near to the Great Sage.”

At that time, the Perfected Ones—Weiming, Luotong, Zhishi, Zhang, and Junminzi—and the assembled devas, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s wondrous verse, rejoiced greatly. Each prostrated themselves thrice, believing, receiving, and vowing to practice it.

*The Sixteenth Scroll of the* Most High Cavernous Divine Incantations Sutra *concludes.*
*The Seventeenth Scroll of the* Most High Cavernous Divine Incantations Sutra *begins.*

**Chapter on Summoning the Celestial Deities and Dragon Spirits to Pacify Tombs and Dwellings**

At that time, the Most High Dao Lord, prior to the Radiant Dawn of the Great Beginning, accompanied the assembly of celestial deities, immortals, and the ten supreme Divine Kings of the Great Sages. Together they proceeded to the ruins of Yang Valley beneath the Long Sang Grove, circumambulating thrice to the left in ritual procession. With one heart, they bowed in reverence and addressed the Primordial Heavenly Worthy:

“Your servant observes that when the parents or kin of ordinary people pass away, they are interred upon the hills, tombs erected to secure their rest for ten thousand years, in hope of safeguarding descendants and ensuring prosperity for their children. Yet those who remain at home suffer misfortune year after year, enduring constant hardship, annual calamities, and the dissipation of wealth and grain. Misfortunes befall them without cause, entangling them in official lawsuits and imprisonment for years. Their livestock fails to multiply, their fields and silkworms lose vitality, their fortunes falter, and their plans go awry.

“By virtue of past karma, they now enjoy blessings in this life and, on this day, have been granted the sight of the Most High and Supreme Worthy. I humbly beseech You to dispel my ignorance and grant Your compassionate mercy. Should You deign to instruct me, even the decayed bones of the departed shall be revived, and they shall receive Your boundless grace—a debt impossible to repay for the gift of life.”

Thereupon, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy snapped His fingers and furrowed His brow, addressing the Most High Dao Lord:

“What you have described regarding the causes of misfortune is indeed a profound means to relieve suffering. To deliver those sunk in delusion and guide them to the shore of fortune, you may now be seated.”

With utmost reverence, the Dao Lord gazed upon the sacred countenance, his heart earnest and intent, listening with unwavering focus and sincere devotion.

The Heavenly Worthy then asked the Most High Dao Lord:

“Have you observed those who enjoy abundance and warmth, as well as those who suffer hunger and cold?”

The Dao Lord replied:

“I have seen them often, yet I do not fully understand the root of their conditions. I humbly beseech Your sacred grace to bestow Your guidance.”

The Heavenly Worthy said:

“Those who receive such good fortune may owe it to the blessings they cultivated in past lives, now ripening in this one. Or they may inherit the residual virtue of their ancestors, which extends to their descendants. If, in addition to enjoying such abundance, they aid the poor and relieve the suffering, restore ancient sacred sites and immortal dwellings, and diligently build and maintain them, they shall reap blessings in this very life, not merely in the hereafter.

“As for those who endure hunger, cold, and poverty, their suffering may stem from past lives in which they plundered and harmed the virtuous. Or they may have stolen materials meant for construction, failed to rescue those in peril, or refused to assist those in distress. Perhaps they exploited many laborers, hoarded grain in granaries, amassed wealth in their households, or relied upon their riches in silver and gold. They may have complained of their dwellings being too cramped or their halls too low, disregarding the dangers of harming life or the signs of declining fortune and severed destiny. Acting recklessly, they violated the Two Black Stars and Five Yellow Stars, inviting the doom of dwindling households and failed enterprises. Or, when burying their kin, they feared only the ominous cries of women and the killing of children, neglecting to choose auspicious years and months for the benefit of the deceased when constructing the tomb. Such actions invoke the Five Ghosts and Three Calamities of the dead, bringing misfortune upon the living and causing their households to suffer violence. They may associate with wicked companions, bully the weak, offend their elders, curse their fathers, or deceive their mothers, leading to injuries from wood and stone, harm from snakes and tigers, or death by lightning, fire, plague, warfare, or imprisonment. Year after year, they face lawsuits, lose wealth without cause, fail in their endeavors, and struggle to achieve their goals. Their fields and silkworms languish, their households fall into discord, their livestock fails to thrive, and they wander in perpetual hardship, year after year of misfortune, with no path to peace.

“Those of high practice who comprehend the scriptures, along with the Daoist priests, shall follow the natural codes of the *Numinous Treasure*. They may conduct rites day and night, offering incense, ascending the altar, and submitting petitions. Thrice daily, they shall perform the ritual circumambulation and recite the scriptures, summoning the celestial deities, earthly spirits, dragon kings, and sacred assemblies to absolve past transgressions and future errors, repenting for former sins and seeking forgiveness for deep offenses. They shall pray for the descent of boundless grace to deliver them.

“The altar shall stand two *zhang* and four *cun* in height, exceeding one *zhang* and two *chi* in width. It shall be adorned with twenty-four stalks of *zuan*, encircled thrice to the left by a cord. The Gate of Heaven and the Door of Earth shall be opened, along with the Human Gate and the Ghost Gate. Within the altar, arrange eleven incense altars or five incense tables for the directions. Adorn the ritual space with banners and canopies.

“With utmost reverence, they shall invoke the Nameless and Natural Great Dao, the Jade Purity Primordial Heavenly Worthy, the Highest Purity Jade Dawn Dao Lord, the Supreme Purity Mysterious Origin Venerable Lord, the Most High Great One of the Empty Cavern Heavenly Worthy, the Ten Directions’ Boundless Great Dao and the Five Elder Emperor Lords of the Great Beginning, the Three Primordial Venerable Saints, the Sovereigns of the Sun and Moon, the Five Planetary Sages, the Seven Primordial Perfected Lords, the Divine Perfected of the Five Celestial Granaries, and the officials of the Three Terraces.

“With solemn respect, they shall state the purpose of their prayer, purifying body and mind. Then they shall unfurl the scriptures and recite the names and titles of the dragon spirits.

“They shall invoke:
The Azure Emperor Dragon King who Guards Tombs and Pacifies Dwellings in the East,
The Vermilion Emperor Dragon King who Guards Tombs and Pacifies Dwellings in the South,
The White Emperor Dragon King who Guards Tombs and Pacifies Dwellings in the West,
The Black Emperor Dragon King who Guards Tombs and Pacifies Dwellings in the North,
The Yellow Emperor Dragon King who Guards Tombs and Pacifies Dwellings in the Center.

The Dragon King of the Eastern Treasury,
The Dragon King of the Southern Treasury,
The Dragon King of the Western Treasury,
The Dragon King of the Northern Treasury,
The Dragon King of the Central Treasury,
The Dragon King of Auspicious Cultivation in the East,
The Dragon King of Abundant Goodness in the South,
The Dragon King of Sweet Thoughts in the West,
The Dragon King of Flowing Waves in the North,
The Dragon King of the Black Dragon in the Center.

The Celestial Deity Dragon King,
The Earthly Spirit Dragon King,
The Dragon King of the Nation,
The Dragon King of the Prefecture,
The Dragon King of the Deep Forest,
The Dragon King of Blossoming Flowers,
The Dragon King of Auspicious Joy,
The Dragon King of Thoughtful Celebration,
The Dragon King of Palaces,
The Dragon King of Halls,
The Dragon King of Houses,
The Dragon King of Chambers,
The Dragon King of Kitchens and Hearths,
The Dragon King of Estates and Fields,
The Dragon King of Silkworms and Mulberries,
The Dragon King of Silk and Cotton,
The Dragon King of Fine Silk,
The Dragon King of Brocade and Fine Fabrics—”

The Dragon King of Fine Silks and Gauzes,
The Dragon King of Gold and Silver,
The Dragon King of Pearls and Jade,
The Dragon King of Copper and Iron,
The Dragon King of Granaries and Storehouses,
The Dragon King of the Eight Grains,
The Dragon King of the Son of Heaven,
The Dragon King of the Feudal Lords,
The Dragon King of the Commandery Lords,
The Dragon King of the County Magistrates,
The Dragon King of the Household Heads,
The Dragon King of Descendants,
The Dragon King of Hills and Mountains,
The Dragon King of Tombs and Dwellings,
The Dragon King of Yin Abodes,
The Dragon King of Yang Abodes,
The Dragon King of National Protection,
The Dragon King of Prefecture Pacification,
The Dragon King of Household Safeguarding,
The Dragon King of Ghost-Driving,
The Dragon King of Ghost-Slaying,
The Dragon King of the Six Livestock,
The Dragon King of Wealth and Money,
The Dragon King of Wealth-Attraction,
The Dragon King of Clothing and Headgear,
The Dragon King of Benevolence and Righteousness,
The Dragon King of Loyalty and Filial Piety,
The Dragon King of Rain and Dew,
The Dragon King of Springs and Marshes.

The Primordial Heavenly Worthy proclaimed that these myriad celestial dragon kings, each with ninety thousand hosts, if there be faithful and devout male and female disciples who, having endured years of misfortune in their households, invite accomplished and enlightened Daoist masters to establish a ritual arena at home—whether by arranging an altar and setting up a register, submitting memorials at the hours of *zi* and *wu*, or considering the scale of the people’s prayers—may resolve disasters and transcend calamities solely through the recitation of scriptures, submitting petitions at the three periods, or performing the Dao at the six hours. Upon the conclusion of the fast and the dispersal of the altar, a grand *jiao* offering to summon the dragons should be held, ensuring the protection and stability of the household, the nation, the king, and the common folk. All shall attain peace, free from disasters, with misfortunes dissolved, blessings and protection universally bestowed, bandits and thieves vanishing without trace, and the divine dragons shielding and dispelling calamities, swiftly banishing them a myriad miles beyond the borders. The people shall rejoice in their livelihoods, and a single planting shall yield ninefold harvests.

By the edict of the Most High, the myriad celestial dragon kings and the divine soldiers and warriors of the ten directions shall each receive their commands and descend to guard the nation, the prefectures, the ancestral tombs, and the households. At this time, the sovereigns, ministers, and officials of the nation and prefectures, along with the common people, shall wholeheartedly embrace the Dao, each vowing to receive the *Marvelous Scripture of the Northern Dipper’s Divine Footsteps*, allowing the Dharma to spread and flourish. The celestial dragon deities, the great sage divine kings, the warriors, the perfected immortals, and the divine soldiers shall all come to safeguard them. The faithful male and female disciples who uphold the scriptural Dharma shall each be blessed with longevity, perpetually occupying positions of emolument. The lands shall enjoy eternal peace, the people shall thrive in prosperity, the eight grains shall ripen abundantly, and the world shall be at great peace. The Three Luminaries shall shine with true radiance, ever adhering to the proper measures of time; the Five Movements shall not err, and the Four Seasons shall follow their course. The Three Calamities shall be forever eradicated, and the scourge of war shall vanish without trace.

Hasten, hasten, in accordance with the Most High’s edict, as the divine dragon’s great decree to pacify the people!

The Primordial Heavenly Worthy further addressed the people of the Lower Realm: From this day forward, if there be any nation or prefecture in turmoil, its people in distress, the Three Calamities arising in competition, the Five Poisons spreading unchecked, bandits and thieves encroaching upon the people, villages and hamlets reduced to ashes, the people losing their livelihoods, prefectures and commanderies laid to waste, the populace starving and enslaved, kin and kindred estranged, and flesh and blood sundered—these are the works of demonic soldiers and rampant disasters, bringing bitter suffering to humanity. If there be a sovereign, prefectural lord, or regional governor who can lead the multitudes—whether ten households or five—uniting their hearts and strength to procure incense and oil, establish a ritual arena, and sincerely invite accomplished Daoist masters well-versed in the scriptures and precepts to recite the *Sacred Canon of Dragon-Summoning* and the *Northern Dipper’s Abyssal Secret Texts*, with unified devotion and purified intent, together venerating the true image of the Primordial Heavenly Worthy, the august forms of the Five Venerable Sovereigns, and the true visages of all the immortals and sages, presenting their supplications with utmost sincerity—then I shall dispatch the summoned hosts of sacred perfected dragon deities to descend upon the ritual arena, heeding the people’s wishes. They shall deploy their soldiers to capture and subdue the malevolent demons causing harm, extinguishing the Five Poisons and the Three Calamities. They shall bestow vast grace and great blessings, protecting and sheltering the devoted common folk, who shall forever receive the profound favor of the Dao, perpetually bathing in its compassion. Their plans shall unfold as desired, their endeavors shall succeed, their undertakings shall all come to fruition, their families shall flourish, and their gates shall prosper with noble lineages.

After peace is restored, they shall devote themselves even more sincerely to revering the Three Luminaries and honoring all the numinous deities, naturally and eternally enjoying tranquility and prosperity.

Hasten, hasten, in accordance with the Most High’s edict to deliver the people from disaster and invoke blessings!

Thus concludes the seventeenth scroll of the *Most High Abyssal Divine Incantations Scripture*.
The eighteenth scroll of the *Most High Abyssal Divine Incantations Scripture*:
**Determining the Fortunes and Misfortunes within the Six Jia Cycles and Invoking Blessings**

The Dao proclaimed: In the *Longhan* era of the Primordial Heavenly Worthy, together with the Five Venerable Sovereigns, the Two Palaces of Yin and Yang, the Five Perfected Stars of the Upper Realms, the Seven Perfected Lords of the Primal Origins, and the officials of the Twenty-Eight Constellations, they roamed the Three Heavens, determining the fortunes and misfortunes of the mortal realm. Later, in the first year of the *Shanghuang* era, the year of *jiawu*, they descended upon the Central Lands of *Zhendan*, observing the various nations of this world. Blessings and auspices were rare, pestilence and miasmas raged fiercely, the people suffered widespread displacement, and the lands were afflicted by alternating floods and droughts, causing the Five Grains to fail in their ripening.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy sighed in lamentation, moved by the suffering of the multitudes. Thereupon, he manifested his divine power, revealing the might of the Dao, his majestic radiance universally illuminating and inspecting the lands and nations. He summoned the celestial immortals and sages, the myriad celestial dragon kings, the jade maidens and immortal youths of the dragon palaces—seven thousand two hundred in number—as well as the spirits and deities governing the mountains, rivers, pools, and caves within their domains, all assembling at the sacred gathering to gaze upon his august countenance and listen to the proclamation of the true Dharma. Then, winds howled and thunder roared, sweet rains poured down in torrents, the sagely grace flowed like mist, washing away all inauspiciousness, and the lands rejoiced in peace and prosperity.

At that time, among the assembly, there was a lofty Daoist master named *Mingluo*, who stepped forward from the crowd, prostrated himself, and paid homage, saying: "By virtue of past blessings, your servant has been privileged to attend upon your august presence. Through the great and lesser *yangjiu* calamities, I have been bathed in your grace, yet I remain ignorant. I humbly inquire: within the six *jia* cycles, from whence do the annual disasters arise? I implore your compassionate illumination and the bestowal of your boundless grace, that this withered wood may encounter the warmth of spring, and the dried fish may meet the life-giving spring rains."

Then the Heavenly Worthy addressed him, saying: "This principle is profound and distant; you should return to your place, and I shall reveal it to you. From the very inception of heaven and earth, I established the celestial *jiazi*, the terrestrial *jiazi*, and the human *jiazi*. The human *jiazi* is marked by the succession of the four seasons, the progression of yang through the pitch-pipes, and the movement of yin through the phases. Thus are divided the Upper, Middle, and Lower Yuan, each Yuan governing sixty years. Now I shall expound the prosperity, scarcity, fortune, and misfortune of each year within a Yuan. You should transcribe this as I speak, that it may be shown to later generations and the years of disaster and blessing be made manifest.

When one encounters the first yang, let them adjust their conduct with sincerity and early supplicate for divine protection.

Thus is the ode recited:

**Jiazi Year:** In autumn, the tillers bear bitter sorrow.
The grain sprouts fail to ripen, calamity harms the fields.
But mark the time after autumn’s onset—
High fields cannot be preserved.
Toiling through winter and spring,
Fathers and sons flee their homes.
Brothers become strangers on the road,
Wives and children scrape by alone.
All the people suffer hardship,
The folk scatter a thousand *li* away.

**Yichou Year:** In spring, pestilence harms the myriad people.
At summer’s beginning, plague arises,
