Striking especially the people of Chu and Lu.
Households all struggle to feed themselves,
While in Wu, families scatter.
The people flee beyond a thousand *li*,
The six livestock all meet with disaster.
High fields may still be planted,
But lowlands suffer blighted sprouts.
The plague is as severe as the year before—
None may remain to guard their homes.

**Bingyin Year:** At the start, fierce beasts roam in packs.
The four seas all surge in waves,
From the wilds to the hills and mounds.
High fields are fit for planting,
Along the ridges and mountain slopes.
But mark the fourth and fifth months—
Fish throng the courtyards.

**Dingmao Year:** Do not follow the fleeting winds.
Early spring lacks heavy rain,
But mid-autumn brings great floods.
Low fields suffer endless calamity,
While the mountainsides are fit for labor.
Though the year yields a meager harvest,
The granaries cannot but remain empty.

**Wuchen Year:** Wrapped in calamity, locusts all arise in swarms.
The people suffer plague,
Women grieve over life and death.
Disaster strikes in mid-autumn,
Rice emerges from the mountainsides.
Lowlands surely cannot be reaped—
They are bound to be swept by floods.

**Jisi Year:** At the outset, fish play before the steps.
In the lakes, dragons emerge,
Boats traverse the thoroughfares.
Level roads are submerged,
All rice and millet are swept away.
If one seeks dry ground,
They must early build lofty dwellings.

**Gengwu Year:** At the start, both flood and drought appear.
Boats sail upon the roads,
Horses are led through the lakes.
Summer brings a hundred days of drought,
Autumn suffers three, six, and nine days of deluge.
The grain surely grows in high fields,
Harvested early at winter’s onset.
Late reaping must meet with disaster,
And warfare will soon arise.

**Xinwei Year:** Plant near the mountains’ edge.
Early spring brings great floods,
Summer must surely be parched.
Wu will suffer no misfortune,
But Jing and Chu are bound by calamity.
Though early summer sees slight drought,
Autumn springs overflow their sources.
Plague cannot but arise,
Affecting every household.

**Renshen Year:** High fields are hard to preserve.
Chariots roll through the canals,
Wu’s lands are no longer seen.
Granaries are meager and cramped,
Households lack even a *sheng* or *dou*.
The northern lands suffer successive calamities,
All nine regions endure them together.
Plague also breaks out in Deng and Lai,
And along the shores of the Wu River.

**Guiyou Year:** Neither high nor low fields are to be pitied.
Early spring brings drought,
Summer’s onset brings ceaseless floods.
Late autumn’s winds and fires rage,
The rice and millet are not abundant.
But mark the lands of Qi and Lu—
There lies the year of famine.

**Jiaxu Year:** At spring’s outset, pests bring calamity.
Summer’s heat meets drought,
Autumn and winter are swept by floods.
High fields planted in vain—
They must surely see only weeds.
To know the pools of disaster,
Look to Yan, Wei, and Shandong.

**Yihai Year:** At the start, flood and drought fill the channels.
Calamity arises from this,
Great demons dwell within the cities.
From afar, it corresponds to the ninth and fifth,
The year of gains and losses is not yet begun.
Where the grain sprouts are planted,
Both high and low may yet be settled.

**Bingzi Year:** Passing, the fields lie beyond the rivers.
The toiling people suffer hardship,
The sprouts are harmed in great numbers.
Plague rats gather in troops,
Ten or more share a single nest.
Piously entreat the gods’ protection,
To safeguard the harvest of the coming season.

**Dingchou Year:** The farmers cannot be at ease.
Though they plant in early spring,
At autumn’s onset, it becomes a sea.
Oxen and horses suffer harm,
Jingzhao is most alarmed.
To know where the sprouts flourish,
The rice emerges from last year’s fields.

**Wuyin Year:** The mountaintops are fit for fields.
Roads become river channels,
Starving people die by the wayside.
Fish and turtles run with hares,
Lotus is planted on high banks.
But mark the end of early summer—
Boats race before the courtyards.

**Jimao Year:** In high fields, the sprouts fare well.
Though early spring lacks water,
Summer and autumn merge with the vast rivers.
Chu and Lu suffer these calamities,
While Wu and Yue receive grace.
That year brings abundant harvests,
Planting should all be done early.

**Gengchen Year:** The people of Yan and Wei rise up.
Livestock fare likewise,
The sprouts are devoured by pests.
The mountainsides are fit for labor,
The people of Wu rejoice in their toil.
Lowlands suffer flooding,
But mid and high fields are most bountiful.

**Xinsi Year:** At the eaves’ end, fish play in the gutters.
Fish swim through the streets and lanes,
The rice sprouts flourish on the hills.
Planting should press forward,
Labor should not lag behind.
Lowlands hold disaster,
But mid and high fields are most abundant.

**Renwu Year:** In spring, flood and drought are not in harmony.
Where it is dry, a thousand *li* are troubled,
Where it is low, fish sport in play.
Not only is there famine,
But also the frequent fear of war.
Plague and miasma arise year after year,
Hunger and hardship are also manifold.

**Guiwei Year:** Five households share a single well.
Spring and summer meet with miasma,
Autumn brings floods once more.
But mark the lands of Wu and Chu,
And also those in Shandong.
To the west, famine arises—
The farmers should but labor on.

**Jiashen Year:** Gathering, the fears are not long in coming.
Chariots roll through flooded lakes,
Horses gallop at the Three Rivers’ mouth.
Those who move their homes surely do not return—
This is the fault of calamity.
Rice emerges along the Five Lakes’ shores,
Planting the mountainsides is of no use.

**You Year:** In shifting, spring drought must surely come."

Three households share a single well,
Disasters link from Wu’s grand meet.
Where livelihoods take root,
All yearn for the Five Lakes’ shore.
No need to till the mountain slopes—
High ground lies barren as waste.

**Bingxu Year:** Autumn brings dried-up wells and springs.
Though summer’s start has water,
Afterward the earth burns dry.
This year, cloud-dragons rise,
Rice sprouts by the Five Lakes’ edge.
Mid-high fields tilled in vain—
Disaster surely clings.

**Dinghai Year:** In Wu’s lands, life settles well.
High and low see harvests spread,
Yet famine strikes Hong and Lu.
Sicheng faces dire straits,
Yan and Chu lie most desolate.
Though the year yields a meager crop,
Spring’s start brings flood’s ruin.

**Wuzi Year:** Farmers till the slopes with care.
Late summer brings plague of pests,
Autumn’s harm runs deep.
Drought and flood chase in turn,
Vermin and rats spare none.
Low fields need no sowing—
High ground bears scant grain.

**Jichou Year:** Calamity spreads across the land.
Pestilence and jaundice strike Zheng’s soil,
Farmers turn boats to steeds.
Livestock all meet misfortune,
Planting clings to mid-high wilds.
Ghosts walk with every sickness,
Those afflicted find no ease.

**Gengyin Year:** High ground calls for labor’s toil.
Though light drought may come,
Water matches last year’s flow.
Low land yields a modest crop,
Mid-high fields stand most abundant.
Wild beasts roam in herds,
High and low roads lie open.

**Xinmao Year:** Early sowing need not be much.
Autumn floods wreak havoc,
Mountains’ edges turn to waves.
Early sown, then drought returns—
Late planting fares no better.
But mark the autumn’s end,
Fish sport upon the roads.

**Renchen Year:** Crops perish to pestilence.
All people suffer alike,
Livestock fares no differently.
Low rice needs no tilling—
Plant the mountains’ waist instead.
Early work yields poor harvest,
Late sowing brings no surety.

**Gui_si Year:** High and low hold no sure measure.
Mid-fields meet misfortune,
Millet and wheat retreat to hills.
This year brings disaster’s wound,
Low ground often meets with flood.
Old stores are consumed,
New provisions lack in full.

**Jiawu Year:** Drought and flood prove hard to flee.
Chariots roll through lake beds,
Boats nestle in mountain homes.
Low fields though tilled and sown,
Winter’s stores will surely fail.
To build a household’s stead,
Till the mountains’ edge instead.

**Yiwei Year:** Fields lie at the Three Rivers’ mouth.
Wu’s land feeds its people,
Yet Jingzhao bears disaster’s weight.
Not only scorching blight—
Ominous ills vie to strike.
Drifting on the wind’s waves,
Death’s hour draws ever near.

**Bingshen Year:** High and low cannot yet shift.
Five Lakes fit for thorns alone,
Coming and going share the same.
If you see disaster’s place,
A peck of rice costs a thousand coins.
To know where peace may dwell,
Jiangnan stands most pitiable.

**Dingyou Year:** High and low till in vain.
Three households share a single well,
Lake beds grow brambles thick.
Jiangdong and its neighboring lands,
Qi and Lu all seek their food.
Western Long and Chu face woe,
The southeast knows no rest.

**Wuxu Year:** Jiangnan’s rice stands full and tall.
Yan and Wei face famine’s grip,
Three years leave homes hollow.
Men are dragged by war’s chains,
Some return to weep at doors.
Wives and children torn apart,
Each pursues the other’s trace.

**Jihai Year:** Jiangnan stands most pitiable.
No need to mark high or low—
Bounty fills the hills and streams.
Disaster strikes the western lands,
Famine mirrors last year’s plight.
Borderlands stir with unrest,
After comes deeper sorrow’s sting.

**Gengzi Year:** Households find no settled life.
Crops suffer widespread harm,
Kin turn to plunder kin.
No surplus fills the mouth,
Wives and children sleep alone.
Though Jiangnan reaps its fill,
Afterward comes wailing’s cry.
Disaster’s turn must come—
Everywhere, only empty homes.

**Xinchou Year:** Disaster’s coming proves no lie.
Wu and Yue burn for a thousand li,
Summer’s start bears the brunt.
But mark the autumn’s onset—
Locusts swarm in every place.
The starving die in foreign lands,
Livestock meets disaster’s fate.

**Renyin Year:** Fierce beasts gather in packs to raid.
Planting clings to mountain slopes,
Courtyards lack even a path’s width.
Rice sprouts in high fields’ midst,
Disaster strikes Wei and Qin.
Boats sail upon the land,
High walls drown in surging waves.

**Guimao Year:** Jin and Wei meet disaster’s blow.
Drought spans three autumns,
Nearly two years’ toll it takes.
Fields lack water’s gift,
High and low lose all surety.
People vie in clamor,
Strife grips the walled cities’ heart.

**Jiachen Year:** Pestilence spreads everywhere.
This year brims with calamity,
Three Rivers’ mouth suffers most.
Millet and wheat fare best,
Spring and summer till the slopes.
Though Jiangnan sees a meager crop,
Bandits’ raids bring no escape.

**Yisi Year:** From the earth, flood-dragons rise.
This year brings famine’s reign,
Boats sail upon the land.
Suzhou and Huzhou drown in waves,
Wu’s lands reap their harvest whole.
Rice sprouts in high fields,
The path ahead holds profit’s sway.

**Bingwu Year:** Flood and drought hold no fixed map.
Sudden deluge then swift drought,
If dry, wells and springs run dry.
Fish turn to hares and deer,
Chickens and dogs become as fish.
Rice sprouts in low fields’ midst,
High ground needs no hoe’s touch.

**Dingwei Year:** Plant the mountains’ waist instead.
Low ground needs no tilling—
The fallen starve to death.
Not only flood’s disaster,
But also war’s uprising strikes.
Wu’s land stands as a peaceful realm,
Yet hardship grips Yan, Qi, and Chu.

**Wushen Year:** Jiangnan’s folk alone survive.
High and low all reap their fill,
Plagues of pests self-destruct.
This year, the eight grains thrive,
People and livestock all rejoice.
Officials climb the ranks,
All roads lie open wide.

**Jiyou Year:** Farmers need but till their fields.
Pestilence comes in small measure,
Plagues too prove easy to heal.
Mountain slopes fit for planting,
A peck of rice costs three coins.
Low ground suffers slight flood’s harm,
Mid-high fields stand most pitiable.

**Gengxu Year:** People need not fret in autumn.
Though Jiangnan sees light drought,
No need to seek beyond its bounds.
Granaries all stand full,
Rice and grain bring autumn’s beauty.
Farmers all rejoice,
The four seas share the breeze.

**Xinhai Year:** Disaster and plague strike where they fall.

**Renzi Year:** Rebellion and cliques harm the peaceful state,
Disaster erupts at Cangling’s mouth.
The celestial divisions face dire calamity,
The time aligns with Longyou’s plight.
Jiangnan sees meager harvests,
Wu’s hills and mounds fare ill.

**Renzi Year (continued):** Grain lies uneaten by men.
Jiangnan remains fit for dwelling,
Yet eastern roads know no end to levies.
Sicheng reverts to the imperial way,
Post roads overgrow with brambles.
All lands lie in frantic waste,
Only Wu’s realm suits planting.

**Guichou Year:** The people are fated to suffer disaster.
Plagues arise in Pengying,
Qi and Lu crumble under misfortune.
Jaundice and pestilence vie to strike,
Households stand shuttered, unopened.
Hardship lingers in these lands,
As mulberry fields turn once more.

**Jiayin Year:** Jiangdong suffices to fill the mouth.
Granaries stand empty everywhere,
Households flee their native villages.
Again, pestilence breaks out,
Encountering hardship, none escape.
Lowlands must suffer flood’s harm,
Mid-high fields yield nothing.

**Yimao Year:** The four seas lie open in traffic.
Where no calamity falls, all ripens,
Farmers reap the beauty of their labor.
Millet and wheat lead the harvest,
Shandong benefits most.
This year brings abundant fortune,
Yet winds rage fiercely within the year.
Plant early,
High ground merits no toil.
Mid-low fields till best,
High ground sprouts but weeds.

**Bingchen Year:** Millet sprouts along dry roads.
Peace reigns in Haochu,
Qi and Jin bear ruin’s weight.
Again, floods bring disaster,
Deer and rabbits mingle with fish.
Here, the people lack food,
Granaries lie utterly bare.

**Dingsi Year:** Wu’s lands abound in prosperity.
Granaries brim full,
Vast and boundless, the people roam.
If but a sage-ruler appears,
Promotions need not be sought.
High and low all ripen,
Farmers forget their cares.

**Wuwu Year:** Each household holds three mouths.
Misfortune strikes in autumn’s midst,
Few return, many lament.
High and low all reap their fill,
Famine’s end draws near.
This year is one of plenty,
The people secure their own.

**Jiwei Year:** Livestock face disaster’s trial.
Five horses barter for one ox,
Foretelling the year’s end.
Grain stores may be sought in dispersal,
Fields yield a thin harvest.
Though this hardship comes,
No bitter sorrow need arise.

**Gengshen Year:** Rice sprouts from high fields.
Mid-summer brings great floods,
Lowlands suffer insects’ torment.
Boast not of lush seedlings,
For Haochu fares the same.
Lowlands labor in planting,
Mid-high fields prove most pitiable.

**Xinyou Year:** Mid-fields may yet be tended.
Drought harms high sources,
Great floods drown lake regions.
Early rice falls to wind’s ruin,
Wu’s gates suffer most.
High and low find no peace,
Only mid-level fields hold promise.

**Renzu Year:** High and low differ utterly.
Spring and summer face drought,
Jiangnan’s boats cannot pass.
Autumn and winter must know drought,
Lowlands suit labor well.
High fields plant in vain,
Ending but in weeds.
To know where disaster strikes,
Look to Yang, Chu, and Jiangdong.

**Guihai Year:** Wu’s divisions sit untroubled.
Mid-fields offer surest refuge,
Lowlands need not be sought.
After the year, the Azure Dragon lies hidden,
Mid-level fields too may be sought.
Though autumn and winter know drought,
Still, a full harvest comes.

At this time, the Heavenly Worthy concluded his hymn of disaster and fortune. The Radiant Perfected Lord Ming Luo and the assembled immortals, each adjusting their dignified attire, advanced together to bow in reverence: "We, by virtue of past karmic blessings, have been granted the fortune to encounter the Compassionate Worthy, who has proclaimed the cycles of fortune through kalpas, revealed the revolving numbers of disaster, opened the pearl-like eyes of understanding, and chiseled through the caves of ignorance, that those of the coming kalpa may prepare for inauspicious years. We cannot contain our joy and gratitude for the boundless grace of creation."

The Heavenly Worthy addressed the assembled immortals: "What I have just recited does not yet exhaust the origin. There remain two *jia* years in the cycle, still distant, which cannot be revealed all at once lest my celestial design be prematurely disclosed. Now, I shall impart to you a wondrous method, to be transmitted to those of faithful and righteous disposition. Take care that the vulgar and foolish do not learn of it. This secret method foretells a year’s abundance or famine, safety or peril, and the rise and fall of the five grains. You must carve it into your bones and remember it well, keeping it within your hearts alone. Do not reveal it to the reckless, the faithless, or the base."

Then he intoned:
*"On New Year’s Day and the advent of spring,*
*First meet the Tiger or Hare.*
*If delayed to the third or fourth watch,*
*Pass not the fifth day.*
*Should this term be met,*
*Grain will be cheap, the people free from suffering.*
*If it falls within the seventh, eighth, ninth, or tenth,*
*Rice will be dear, the year lean, and rain scarce."*

The Heavenly Worthy spoke to the assembled immortals: "I compose this hymn to be passed down eternally to my disciples, that they may foresee inauspicious years and lean seasons, and prepare by storing grain. Should disaster’s portion descend, then deploy my rites of exorcism and prayer. Choose a solitary peak or sheer cliff, or a place between water and mountain; failing that, an ancient sacred site or altar, or even a public courtyard or orchid-strewn wilds—anywhere pure and unsullied, far from filth and defilement. There, in accordance with the strict codes of the Three Caverns, establish an altar and set up the ritual implements.

If acting for the king, the chief minister, the prefect, or the magistrate, then array a three-tiered sacred altar, open twenty-four gates, and set out twenty-four incense feasts. With wholehearted devotion, invoke the Three Pure Dao, the Five Venerable Lords of the Great Beginning, the officials of the Three Primes, the immortals and divine officers of the forty-six grotto-heavens, and the spirits of famous mountains, great rivers, abysses, and marshes. Hold a fast for three days to disperse the altar, and conduct a grand offering, adjusting its scale to the abundance or scarcity of resources. Recite the scriptures for summoning dragons, and present memorials on yellow silk. Alternatively, compose a memorial in devotion to the Dao, spoken aloud with utmost sincerity. Do not treat the rites with negligence.

The vulgar and base, however, first slight the true sages of the heavens, and second, scorn officials and the common people. They mobilize the masses in vain, squander resources, and thus their prayers go unanswered, while incurring grave karmic retribution. Those who practice my teachings must proceed with awe and caution."

Then the Radiant Perfected Lord Ming Luo and the assembled immortals, having received the Heavenly Worthy’s guidance on abundance and famine, disaster and fortune, and his instruction in the rites of exorcism and prayer, each adjusted their robes and crowns and bowed in reverent prostration.

The various Perfected Lords and High Ministers each mounted their phoenix carriages and dragon chariots, attending the Heavenly Worthy as they ascended back to the Jade Realm, where they were received with welcoming rites. The divine spirits and the assembly who had heard the Dharma all returned to their original stations.

*Thus concludes Scroll Eighteen of the* Supreme Cavernous Abyss Divine Incantations Sutra.
*Scroll Nineteen of the* Supreme Cavernous Abyss Divine Incantations Sutra: *The Decree to the Heavenly Demons*

The Primordial Heavenly Worthy, in the Land of Great Blessing’s Palace of Eternal Joy, sat upon a throne woven of seven-jeweled treasures alongside the Boundless Great Sage, the Flying Heavenly Divine Kings. As he expounded the *Great Expulsion Sutra of the Cavernous Abyss Divine Incantations*, he summoned the Ten Directions’ Kings of the Samadhi Divine Incantations and the Flying Transcendent Perfected Great Spirits of the Mysterious and Wondrous Heavens to gather before his seat.

The Heavenly Worthy addressed the Supreme Dao Lord, saying: "Have you heard that along the ten borders of the Land of Great Blessing in the Palace of Eternal Joy, demonic ghosts recklessly arise, harming the men and women of the multitude, so that the sound of sorrow and suffering is ever present?"

The Dao Lord replied: "This realm has been the World of Ultimate Bliss for seven billion five hundred million kalpas, and there has been no sound of lamentation. Since the era of Dragon Han, however, the men and women of the people have all been born with fierce and murderous natures, offering lewd prayers to the various demonic spirits, vainly seeking to sustain their lives. Since that time of awakening, for seven billion five hundred million kalpas, the people have suffered poverty and hardship, their forms withering with age and illness. Whether man or woman, all share the same intent, flattering and beseeching evil ghosts. The residual *qi* of the Six Heavens, bearing the nine-fold ugliness of the Wood Essence’s demonic illusions, enters their hearts, giving rise to violent rebellion. They kill the innocent without cause, and the power of evil spirits grows ever stronger."

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy commanded the Five Venerable Celestial Emperors to summon the Ten Great Demons of Heaven, the Lords of the Three Realms, and the Great Soldiers of the Supreme Perfected Divine Armies—countless myriads—to capture all the ghosts who had slipped from the registers of the world. He asked: "Which of them harm the people, causing the lands to know no great peace, the people to bear many debts, and life and death to hold no tranquility?"

The Perfected Kings of the Three Heavens, along with the Three Heavens’ Great Soldiers of the Ten Directions’ Divine Perfected, roamed the borders of the lands. For all people, they healed illness, aided the upright *qi* of Heaven, slew and extinguished evil essences, and rescued the lives of the multitude, all through the power of the Dao, preserving their heavenly destinies.

"From this day forward, if there are Daoist priests who submit to the Three Caverns, receive and uphold this sutra, and carry its Dharma to travel the world, healing the sick so that they may recover and know no premature death—should any ghost refuse to depart or dare to act wickedly against such a Daoist priest in the course of healing, I shall dispatch the Great Demon Kings of the Nine Heavens with their armies to bind and capture them, exterminating their factions and cutting off their influence in other lands."

The Dao declared: "Within the Three Realms, from this day forward, in the perverse and doomed lands of the latter kalpas, where yin *qi* and turbid evil arise, change will swiftly come. Simplicity and purity having been lost, frivolity and competition will flourish. In the Four Heavens and Eight Directions below, those who style themselves as Demon Kings of the Divine will emerge, naming themselves the Heavenly Spirits of a turbid and evil age, spreading throughout the lower realms. Within the Four Heavens, the mountain and forest stone essences will possess living people, men and women alike imitating and learning from one another, calling themselves Heavenly Kings. Together with the residual *qi* ghosts of the Six Heavens and the ghosts who have slipped from the world’s registers, they will form factions, branching and dispersing, adopting names in accordance with the times, bringing calamity to the myriad people. They will cause people to pray and supplicate, flattering and beseeching for protection, turning their backs on the Dao to believe in evil, offering food and seeking blessings. These ghosts will grow ever more powerful, gnawing at people’s essence and *qi*, consuming their blood and vessels, cutting short their years. Unaware, people will allow them to enter their bodies, causing them to despise life and love death. Such ghosts, in numbers beyond count, will bewitch men and women alike.

Wherever a Daoist priest travels to heal such afflictions, I shall dispatch the Great Spirits of the Ten Directions and the Envoys of the Five Peaks—three hundred thousand in number—to assist the Daoist in healing illness. From this day forward, in the years of *jiashen* and *renchen*, great armies will arise in the world, and plague demons will kill people, nine out of every ten. The world will be vast and desolate, the people distressed and suffering, their rulers indifferent. Thirty kinds of illness will afflict the world, beyond all cure. If there are Daoist priests who submit to the *Three Caverns Divine Incantations Sutra*, I shall send down the Great Divine Soldiers of Heaven to assist them in healing illness. They shall invoke the Great Kings of the Samadhi Divine Incantations to lead a host of one hundred thousand red-armored soldiers and golden-armored warriors. They shall also summon the Generals of the Nine Heavens’ Punitive Campaigns—four hundred thousand strong. And the Green-Armored Soldiers—four hundred thousand. And the Red-Armored Soldiers—four hundred thousand. And the White-Armored Soldiers—four hundred thousand. And the *Qi*-Armored Soldiers—four hundred thousand. And the Yellow-Armored Soldiers—four hundred thousand. And the Great Soldiers of Prohibitions and Slaughter—four hundred thousand. And the Great Officers of the Azure Heaven—four hundred eighty thousand. And the Great Officers of the Red Heaven—four hundred eighty thousand. And the Great Officers of the White Heaven—four hundred eighty thousand. And the Great Officers of the Black Heaven—four hundred eighty thousand. And the Great Officers of the Yellow Heaven—four hundred eighty thousand. Each shall lead armies of countless myriads, wielding the triple-armored implements for slaying ghosts to assist the Daoist in healing illness. Should any ghost dare to act with malicious poison, or any evil person direct their malevolent intent toward this Daoist, they shall be slain one by one, leaving no trace of harm to people or ghosts, thereby manifesting the divine efficacy of the Great Dao."

The Dao declared: "If a Daoist priest dwells in hidden mountain valleys or among the people, they should wholeheartedly rescue those in peril and dire distress, reciting the sutras and performing the Daoist rites thrice daily. After reciting the sutras and performing the rites for one to three days, they shall face north in the central courtyard and present the *Precious Chapter of the Great Expulsion* once. They shall also wear the Registers of the Great Talismans of the Nine Heavens, inscribed on silk, and don the divine talismans. Thus, the sick shall swiftly recover, and no harm shall come to people or ghosts—all shall be resolved clearly and completely. These ghostly spirits shall each gather pestilence and seize poisons for the Daoist, aiding them in healing the sick."

The Dao declared: "From this day forward, if any Daoist priest practices the *Scripture of the Divine Incantations of the Three Caverns* but does not wear the *Great Expulsion Scripture*, the hundred demons shall not submit, the spirits shall not aid them, and their healing of the sick shall not succeed. From this day forward, if any Daoist priest wholeheartedly embraces the Dao, their aspiration fixed upon the Three Caverns, and receives this *Great Expulsion Scripture of the Three Heavens* along with the Four Great Talismans of Pacification, they shall subdue all manner of ghosts. Wherever such a Daoist priest may go in the world, the ten thousand ghosts shall pay homage. Should any dare to cause harm, when the Daoist priest recites the scriptures and performs the rites, they shall command the people to refrain from clamor and foul speech. Then, the ninety myriad great soldiers of the Nine Heavens shall shield the Daoist priest, assisting in the healing of the sick, and none shall dare to transgress.

The Dao declared: "From this day forward, if any Daoist priest recites the scriptures for a single night and expounds the great Dharma of the Three Caverns and the great *Expulsion Scripture*, demonic harms shall be stirred, malevolent spirits shall lose their essence, the thunder of the Dharma shall resound, heavenly soldiers shall array themselves, fire shall flow for ten thousand miles, fire bells and shooting stars shall rush forth, the Nine Uglies shall be slain, demonic spirits shall be beheaded, pestilence shall be swept away, and the sick shall recover from their afflictions. People and ghosts shall suffer no harm—you and all your myriad kinds shall be banished. Swiftly, swiftly, as in the *Great Expulsion* decrees!"

The True Kings of the Three Heavens addressed the people, men and women alike: "If any can wholeheartedly embrace the Dao, delighting in the Three Caverns, and receive and uphold this scripture, enshrining it in their home, then on the day of the Great Expulsion, when ghostly soldiers might wrongfully slaughter, and the calamity of the great kalpa draws near, neither people nor ghosts shall be able to distinguish themselves from one another. From this day forward, if any Daoist priest is single-minded, bearing the sun and moon upon their head, carrying the stars upon their shoulders, revering and delighting in the True Dao, and aiding the rectification of Heaven’s *qi*, they may present forty feet of white silk, a pair of golden rings, five feet of five-colored silk, and precious incense of descending truth. At a pure and numinous abode, in the mountains or marshes, they shall establish an altar and offer a grand jiao to the Five Emperors. With the Three Samadhi Divine Incantations, the Great Expulsion Talismans, the red and black *qi*, and the Four Great Talismans of Pacification, they shall seal the springs so that they dry up, seal the mountains so that they crumble, seal the rivers so that they run dry, seal fire so that it is extinguished, seal spirits so that they perish, and seal ghosts so that they are destroyed. The prohibitions of the Three Heavens shall subdue all hidden things.

From this day forward, wherever a Daoist priest holds these Great Expulsion divine incantations and talismans, I shall assist them in healing the sick, capturing all ghosts who have escaped the registers, and delivering them to the prisons of the Three Heavens to be punished. Thus shall the divine efficacy of the Great Dao be made manifest. When healing the sick, the Daoist priest shall recite this scripture and perform the rites, revealing their practice at the six periods of the day. They shall inscribe the divine talismans and great registers upon red and black silk. These shall be given to the sick to wear for pacification, all in accordance with the scriptural regulations. When healing the sick, the Daoist priest must act with a single mind, rescuing those in dire peril, and must not demand recompense or harbor greed. Heaven shall diminish their Dao-power—what immortality could they attain?

This talisman commands the demonic soldiers and horses of the Five Emperors, along with the ninety myriad heavenly soldiers of the Three Caverns, to guard and protect it. If a Daoist priest does not receive this talisman, the hundred ghosts and thousand demons shall not fear them. But if they wear this talisman, the ten thousand demons shall pay homage, all ghosts shall praise its virtue, and the assembled multitudes shall bow their heads, each requesting to uphold it.

The Dao declared: "The great kalpa is nigh, and the Three Calamities—blades, pestilence, water, and fire—draw near. Before the *ren-chen* year, waters shall surge ten thousand fathoms, ghostly soldiers shall slaughter people, and pestilence shall abound, sparing not a single region. I now lead the numinous consorts of the various heavens, the divine perfected of the ten directions, and the officials of the Three Realms to descend into the world and save all beings from illness. If any embrace the Dao and delight in the scriptures of the Three Caverns, receiving and upholding the divine incantations, the Three Samadhi, and the great talismans of expulsion, they shall dwell within the Nine Palaces, behind the Three Dragons, and be appointed as heavenly officials. In the Jade Registers, they shall be spared the Three Calamities and Nine Perils. Swiftly, swiftly, as in the *Great Expulsion* decrees!"

The Dao declared: "Within the Three Realms, there are many gods and demons. The demon kings possess abundant poisons and slaughter living beings, heedless of Heaven’s majesty. From this day forward, I command the vanguard Lu’s prohibition soldiers, numbering in the billions and myriads. There are also the Five Ding Envoys, ninety myriad strong. There are the prohibition soldiers of the Three Heavens, thirty myriad strong. And there are the Red Ding Clerical Soldiers, forty-nine myriad strong. Together, they shall descend to heal all illnesses of humankind."

If Daoist priests submit to the Three Caverns, perform the Dao, recite scriptures to save others, they must first establish a quiet chamber, paint the true portraits of the Five Thearchs and the supreme true visages of the Three Caverns, and erect a Three Caverns ritual arena. Therein, they shall broadly dispel misfortune and invoke blessings for the world, eliminating calamities and averting disasters. Should men or women bring incense to the ritual arena, beseeching treatment for illness, the priests shall, according to their wealth or poverty, prepare vegetarian feasts and offer prayers, invoking the gods of the Five Thearchs and bestowing upon them talismanic charms to wear. For those whose illnesses are cured, I shall banish you, myriad demonic spirits, in ranks of thousands. Swiftly, swiftly, as in the *Great Expulsion* decrees!

The celestial maidens of the Three Heavens and the multicolored maidens of the ten directions, along with the divine consorts of the heavens, each bearing the Ten Absolute Spirit Banners for summoning demons, jade staffs, and jeweled canopies, and riding upon dragon-phoenix carriages, shall descend for all living beings to disseminate the true *qi* of the Three Heavens. Thus, the people of the world shall all awaken to remorse, revere our Three Treasures, and turn toward the Great Dao. Passing beyond the *jiashen* year, they shall be recorded in the Jade Registers and spared the Three Calamities and Nine Perils. You, plague demons, shall cease your poisonous rampage and no longer kill; all beings shall attain safety, free from harm. From this day forward, if any Daoist priest arouses a heart of great compassion, cherishes all without distinction, and single-mindedly practices the Three Caverns to save others, I shall assist the priest in healing the sick. Wherever this scripture is recited, all ghosts and spirits shall flee in terror. Swiftly, swiftly, as in the *Great Expulsion* decrees!

The Dao declared: "From this day forward, if any Daoist priest in the world upholds this scripture, turns toward the Seven Perfected, wears and serves the divine talismans, and saves all beings afflicted with illness, they shall be given talismans to wear and memorials to present, offering prayers to the gods of the Five Thearchs, so that their illnesses may be cured and they may pass beyond the Three Calamities and Nine Perils. If any Daoist priest renounces worldly burdens, single-mindedly devotes themselves to the Dharma, and resolves to practice the Three Caverns to heal the sick, reducing their own clothing and food, relinquishing wealth and silk, and distributing alms to the poor to aid all beings, then the gods of Heaven and Earth shall establish their merit, and they shall immediately perceive the true Dao. The lords of the Three Heavens shall assist the Daoist priest in practicing the Dao, and all ghosts and spirits shall tremble in fear. They shall no longer come to kill the people; I dispatch the demon kings of the *Great Expulsion* to execute them in succession. Swiftly, swiftly, as in the decrees!"

The Dao speaks: From this day forward, if any Daoist priest, ruler, emperor, regional lord, or magistrate believes in the scriptures, upholds Our Three Caverns, and receives the wondrous qi, they shall enable others to ascend as immortals. Those who cultivate and uphold the Way among the upper immortals shall grow feathered wings and soar freely. Those among the middle immortals shall conceal themselves at will. Those among the lower immortals shall command ghosts and spirits. At that time, when the perfected of the Three Caverns ascend as immortals, their fame shall spread afar, and the thirsting multitudes of the ten directions shall gaze in reverence. Beneath the Four Heavens, all men and women shall burn incense, bow their heads, and lift their thoughts to Heaven, yearning for the Great Dao to descend upon the world. With compassionate radiance universally bestowed, ruler and minister shall employ the Dao, mutually supporting one another, bringing great peace to the realm and everlasting prosperity to their reigns.

The Dao speaks: From this day forward, in the years of *jiǎ-shēn* and *rén-chén*, plague demons numbering nine hundred thousand shall descend and spread across the world, inflicting ten thousand kinds of illness, maladies beyond cure. If there are Daoist priests who uphold the Three Caverns, recite the scriptures, and practice the Dao, employing the qi of the Three and Five to ward off evil, they shall bind these demons, banish them to distant lands, and pacify the spirits of household elders, community altars, and sacred turtles, ensuring all remain unharmed. When illness strikes, if a Daoist priest of the Three Caverns recites the scriptures, practices the Dao, burns incense, lights lamps, hangs silken banners and canopies, scatters flowers, and chants praises in the six periods, then on the day the rites conclude, they shall perform offerings and supplications to the Five Emperors. The Five Marchmounts, Four Rivers, Nine Water Lords, Twelve Stream Sources, cavernous grottoes, dragon kings, and all officials of the heavens, the Three Realms, their divine retinues, down to the Six Paths, Four Births, and the dark underworld—all shall momentarily feel remorse and be banished to distant lands.

The Dao speaks: From this day forward, if any Daoist priest submits to the Three Caverns and travels to a land where the sick reside to heal them, they shall summon the Celestial Prohibited Soldiers of the Three Heavens, the Chief Scribes, the Perfected Divine Lords of the Ten Directions, the Twelve Karma Officers, the Nine Heavens’ Demon-Seizing Envoys, the Ghost-Capturing Officers, the Treachery-Seizing Officers, the Great Demon-Expelling Kings, the Crimson Capital Envoys, and the Heavenly Might Warriors, leading their retinues of four hundred eighty thousand to descend and assist this Daoist priest in healing the sick.

The Dao speaks: Upon hearing the recitation of this scripture nearing its end, all these perfected immortals—heavenly men and women, divine consorts, and immortal youths—shall bow their heads in reverence, believing, receiving, and upholding it.

The *Divine Talisman for Beheading Ghosts in the Prisons of Hell* shall be written in black ink, placed in a crimson pouch, and worn upon the head.
The *Talisman for Dispelling All Myriad Evils* shall be written in black ink on white silk and worn upon the head.

The Dao speaks: Daoist priests shall inscribe divine talismans and cast them into springs to suppress and seal the hundred demons of the world, regardless of their size. When reciting the scriptures and practicing the Dao, they shall present the *Precious Chapter of the Great Expulsion and Execution* and orally summon the officers and soldiers.

This talisman shall be written in vermilion.

The nineteenth scroll of the *Supreme Pervasive Divine Incantations Scripture* concludes here.
The twentieth scroll of the *Supreme Pervasive Divine Incantations Scripture* begins.

**Chapter on Dispelling Ghosts Through the Long Night**

The Dao speaks: Long ago, I traveled with Wen Shi and Red Pine Master, leading seventy thousand Brahma Kings, roaming the outskirts of the Five Ridges in the world. We saw those who had died by the blade—not merely one or two. The Most High, moved by compassion, dispatched transformed Daoist priests to ask them: *"What crimes have you committed to suffer such torment?"* Each answered: *"We endure this cruel agony, yet know not its cause. We only beseech the Great Compassion to bestow its decree upon the transformed ones."*

The Dao said: *"Hark! Do you not know? The great kalpa draws near, and the waters shall soon rise. All the people of the world shall become as mud. Such as you are not few. Why do you not cultivate the Dao and thus endure forever? You covet wealth and rank, fleeting as a moment, and so fail to attain transcendence through ten thousand kalpas. You see no good roots, and thus remain obscured by heaven and earth, bound to calamity as your fate. The world is impure, and the Five Thieves lead men astray, drawing them into evil destinies. They drain men’s spirit-qi and cast them into the abyss. One misstep, and regret comes too late."*

As the Most High spoke these words, thirty-nine thousand in the assembly, one hundred thousand heavenly maidens, two hundred thirty thousand transformed ones beneath the earth, and four hundred ninety thousand Daoist priests and demon kings—men and women alike—all rose in astonishment, seeking to receive this scripture. From this day forth, they vowed to uphold this Dharma, to teach and transform the foolish, that they might no longer crave official rank or royal station. Each swore: *"Today, we have heard the Celestial Worthy’s words and shall act upon them, daring not to disobey."* They removed their garments to receive the scripture.

The Dao speaks: In the world’s latter age, thirty-nine thousand people shall attain the rank of Upper Immortal, ascending upon the Most High’s nine dragons. Three hundred million heavenly beings shall traverse the lands, welcoming Daoist priests of immortal bone. In that era, great floods shall arise, and ghostly armies shall clash. Countless men and women shall perish. Now, I specially dispatch transformed ones to journey across the Four Seas, commanding all to prepare the scriptures and receive the *Precious Chapter of the Great Expulsion*, donning its protective signs. Among them, those with faith shall hear and rejoice, seeking the transformed ones to receive it. But those who disbelieve shall hear yet remain unmoved, drifting aimlessly into the nine rivers and three streams until all perish. Alas!

The Most High, riding upon five-colored clouds in the void, gazed down in great compassion, lamenting the foolishness of these beings. *"Alas, alas! How shall I save them?"* Then, mounting a dragon, He led the heavenly hosts, all the sage-kings, and a hundred million immortals of the Five Peaks into the midst of the great flood to rescue those of steadfast faith, granting them fearlessness. Great ravens bore them aloft to the Nine Heavens. The dragon-borne ascents spanned ten thousand leagues in breadth, some two thousand nine hundred leagues, others one thousand two hundred leagues. There were eighty million such ascents, each capable of carrying three hundred million people. Yet those who did not receive the scriptures, who heard not the Dharma, who kept no fasts, who knew not the Dharma-realm—none could board these ascents.

Though the transformed ones sought to rescue them as the great waters rose, the Beam Spirits and Controller Officials would slay them, seizing the sinners and casting them back into the waters. Yet the Most High, the Perfect Sage, could still save them, and the flying immortals—men and women—assisted in delivering the people. Countless great ravens arrived as one, bearing away those of virtuous conduct.

*"You Daoist priests, having now seen this* Great Expulsion Scripture *and heard the Most High, and beheld His form and image—you shall indeed encounter the dragon-borne ascents in future lives. The words of the sages are not empty!"*

The Dao speaks: These immortals and jade maidens were born before heaven and earth, enduring many kalpas. Now, they join Me in teaching and transforming the foolish. Only those with immortal bone may behold their forms. You, in turn, must each transmit this teaching to later generations—men and women alike—who, if they receive it together, shall not die untimely deaths. When the great flood comes, they shall not be among the drowned.

The great assembly, hearing the Celestial Worthy’s words, wept in sorrow and sought to receive and uphold them. Moved by compassion, the Most High commanded the transformed ones to enter the mountains and erect an altar, where eighty million men and women from the multitude received the scripture. The demon kings and their followers, unable to attend, pledged their faith and came to the mountains to receive it.

The Dao speaks: *"You who receive this* Precious Scripture of the Great Expulsion *—its essentials shall make you immortals. Diligently transform and deliver others, passing it on to the foolish. The foolish, with their inverted views, are pitiable indeed. In the coming age, the great flood shall engulf them. The sages see the foolish living heedlessly, like men observing worms in a privy—unaware of when they might emerge. You Daoist priests who fail to transform them shall remain forever mired in birth and death."*

The great assembly—immortals of the Five Peaks, all four divisions, heavenly beings, men and women—all sighed in unison: *"Excellent! We too shall uphold this!"*

The Dao speaks: Beyond the Northern Sea lies the land of the Yilin Kingdom, comprising forty-eight thousand households. They do not believe in the Dao or its laws, killing living beings for their own use. Their land is in turmoil, and the people rebel, slaughtering three hundred each day. The Most High, seeing the great flood approaching and the foolish unaware, committing sins that cast them into evil destinies—when would they ever escape?—entered the Dark Mountain and observed all beings drifting aimlessly. Whither were they bound? Then, He released the light from within His body, illuminating the ten directions. He dispatched transformed ones from the ten directions to fly through the void to the land of Yilin.

The kings, seeing them, were greatly alarmed: *"These beings ride the empty air—what are they? Are they not demonic spirits?"* They immediately sent thirty thousand men to shoot arrows upward. Yet the arrows turned back and struck their own people dead—who then revived.

The officials could not kill them and reported to the king. Enraged, the king dispatched thirty thousand soldiers to slay them, yet still they could not be killed. The flying immortals descended, filling the entire kingdom. The land overflowed with them, transforming in an instant into women, children, and elders—countless millions of forms. The king, seized with terror, prostrated himself before the flying immortals and said: *"We are sinners, unaware that a great sage had descended. From this day forth, we take the immortals as our masters. We humbly beg your acceptance."*

The immortals replied: *"We are not worthy to be your masters. We too have our own original master, known as the Heavenly Worthy. If you truly possess such devotion, we shall take you to report to Him."* They then led the king and his retinue to the transformed ones of the Most High. At once, the king and all within the kingdom vanished, leaving the land eerily empty.

The king and his ministers declared: *"These immortals are great sages. We must transform our hearts and serve them."* The transformed ones, perceiving their sincerity, converted all the people of the kingdom, each receiving the Dao, along with talismans, scriptures, and covenants, and they performed the rites of purification. From that time, beyond the Northern Sea, the Dao flourished.

The king and his minister Ma Xuan asked: *"How ought one who receives these scriptures honor their master?"* The transformed ones replied: *"One who receives these scriptures must revere their master as the sun and moon, and honor the scriptures as pearls and jade. Never slight the scriptures, never belittle the master. The master is like heaven, the scriptures like the sun—heaven cannot be destroyed, the sun cannot be touched. Ascension to immortality and deliverance from the world depend entirely upon the master. Without a master, one cannot obtain these scriptures; without the scriptures, one cannot ascend to immortality.*

*You who serve a master must never harbor resentment, nor speak their name in vain even after a single night. The Dao does not tolerate dual loyalties—reverence must come from the heart without deceit. If you disobey, your head shall shatter into seven pieces."*

The Dao spoke: When the great flood comes, in the Middle Kingdom there shall be the immortals Tang Ping, Yu Guang, and Ma Qi, leading eighty thousand heavenly beings. These immortals shall ride iron boats to receive Daoists who possess the scriptures—you must await them. When these immortals arrive, above them will be five-colored clouds, a circular canopy stretching three million *li*. Within it, one hundred thousand jade maidens shall shine with radiant red and white light, shimmering brilliantly—this is the coming of the immortals. You must await them.

A Daoist of the Eastern Grove asked: *"We do not know which scriptures one must receive to behold the immortals and escape the Three Calamities."*

The Most High replied: *"The* Upper Clarity Numinous Treasure Samādhi of Infinite Wonders *will suffice. Yet if a Daoist does not receive the* Great Expulsion Scripture*, they shall not cross the three great rivers nor escape the calamities of the kalpa. Why is this? The* Great Expulsion Scripture *is the foremost among scriptures, the king of the thirty-six divisions of scriptures—none surpass it. It is the grand regulator of all scriptures; to receive it is to complete the scriptures. Daoist men and women, unless their former lives bore the bones of immortality, may not receive this scripture. It shares the same womb as the* Infinite Wonders Scripture*—in practice and application, it is identical to the methods of the* Infinite Wonders.* If one seeks immortal ascension, one must study the* Infinite Treasure Scripture*. A Daoist who does not receive the* Infinite Great Expulsion Scripture *is no Daoist at all."*

Among the eighty-four thousand present, all heard the Most High’s words. Each bowed thrice and sought to receive it, vowing to uphold it. The disciples, from this day forth, shall carry this scripture to transform all people under heaven. Those who fully receive it shall be transformed in every way.

The Dao spoke: *"Humans possess three hun-souls and seven po-souls. At death, they scatter and are driven into the Five Shades. Thus, the dead may meet fortune or misfortune. Those who die in the third month of spring are slain by the emissaries of the Great Yang, ruled by the Lord of the Nine Yi. Ninety myriad great spirits select them, their might like boiling broth. The stars above shall dim, and their fate shall be severed. If one performs rituals and enters samādhi, refining the corpse ten times, the seven po-souls shall attain non-action. They shall avoid the Five Sufferings, ascend to the Mud Pill Palace, and abide by the Primordial Method. Protected by heavenly beings, their good and evil shall be distinguished. If, after death, someone recites this scripture for them, eight hundred million great spirits shall deliver their departed souls, restoring them to rebirth in heaven. If reborn among humans, they shall become lords and elders, their clothing and sustenance naturally provided, sparing them from suffering. Wherever this ritual is performed, eight hundred million heavenly beings and jade maidens shall descend to witness it. The merit of the Daoist shall bring blessings to the living and ascension to the dead—all through the power of the commemorative ritual."*

The Dao spoke: *"Those who die in the third month of summer are slain by the Great Yin Controller of Destiny of the Vast Forest, ruled by the Lord of the Eight Man. Eighty myriad spirits select them, and the stars above shall dim, their fate forever severed. From this day forth, if someone dies and this scripture is recited for them, the departed shall not be displaced. If they cannot ascend to heaven or be reborn among humans, I shall dispatch the Radiant Immortal Great Yu, Immortal Qian Zhi, and Immortal Fang Sheng, each leading thirty-nine thousand heavenly soldiers and one hundred thousand mighty warriors, to smite the demon kings, selection officials, and the ten refining spirits, preventing them from ascending. They shall remain as lowly ghosts, forever barred from immortality. This is the decree from the golden mouth of the Most High—once issued, there shall be no pardon. As the Most High commands, so shall it be. If you, lesser demon kings, heed this edict, you may yet ascend. If you enforce it without deviation, but fail to carry out the decree, ninety myriad great spirits wielding crimson staves shall bludgeon the evil ghosts to death. The officials of the Five Paths and the selection spirits of the ten directions must act in their own interest, ensuring the dead are not reported above. If word reaches the heavens, you shall be the first to face judgment—the golden mouth of the Most High shall show no mercy. All shall follow the words of the Most High Perfected. Those who disobey shall see the heads of demon kings and ghost kings shattered into sixteen pieces."*

The Dao spoke: *"Those who die in the third month of autumn are slain by the Six Harms—great epidemics, water, fire, and misfortunes—ruled by the Lord of the Six Rong. Sixty billion selection spirits shall judge them, their names self-generated. The stars above shall dim, and their fate shall be forever severed. From this day forth, those who die and have this scripture recited for them shall have their spirits refined by the officials of the Five Paths. Those who cannot ascend to heaven are guilty of double-tongued slander, wicked speech, harming or killing others, the Five Inverse Acts, unfilial conduct, deceiving their masters, cursing their fathers, or striking their elders. Whether brother, sister, aunt, uncle, or any kin—all shall enter hell for ninety-one kalpas and never ascend to heaven. The heavenly officials shall not tolerate them. Even if this scripture is recited for them, it shall be of no benefit. Their sin is equal to that of slanderers. Daoists must cultivate goodness, transform others, receive the Three Caverns, revere the scriptures, and practice the Dao. If the dead have this scripture recited for them, the spirits shall issue the decree, and the departed shall ascend directly to heaven. From the years *guiwei* and *xinsi* onward, Daoists who transform and deliver others may escape the great flood of the *jiashen* calamity."*

The Dao spoke: *"Those who die in the third month of winter are slain by the emissaries of the Luminous Decree for failing to practice the Dao, mocking those who do good, and ridiculing the common folk. They are not human in their three hun-souls and seven po-souls, ruled by the Lord of the Five Di. Fifty myriad selection officials shall distinguish their good and evil, and the stars above shall dim, their fate forever severed. From this day forth, the dead shall have their spirits refined. The Lord of Spirit Refinement commands eight hundred million spirits to ensure the departed ascend to heaven, where heavenly maidens shall welcome them. Though they may not attain flying immortality, they shall be reborn as humans."*

"Through ten refinements, the corpse is quickened; from the ten directions, guests arrive. The world selects together—none may descend to rebirth. Should they fall into the Three Wretched Realms, the fault lies with the demon kings. The Registrar of Mount Tai, the Lords of the Five Paths, and the immortal officials of the sacred mountains—if they fail to attend with care and cause the departed to suffer trials, you shall be the first to bear punishment. The Supreme August One’s oral decree is never empty.

When Daoists transform others, fortune and misfortune depend on the fast; the gods of the fast shall guard their bodies.

The Dao speaks: Those who die in penal servitude are governed by the Civil Scribes. Those who die of cold or heat are governed by the Luminous Kings. Those who die from falling from cliffs or trees are governed by the Fiery Ram Lords. Those who die by blade or weapon are governed by the Sacrificial Officers. Those who die by hanging are governed by the Lady of Creeping Vines. Those who drown are governed by the Dark Lady. Those who die in fire are governed by the Heavenly Aides. Those who die in forests are governed by King He. Those who die of starvation are governed by Meng Ying. Those who die of swellings are governed by Ji Ying. Those who die from needles are governed by the Dragon Kings. Those who die in dreams are governed by Lin Xuan. Those who die of suffocation are governed by Scribe Liu. Those who die of grievous injustice are governed by Zuo Ren. Those who die in madness are governed by Ding Gou. Those who die by self-stabbing are governed by Commander Zhu. Those who drown themselves are governed by Hu Chun. Those who die of chronic illness are governed by Qiao Qiu.

From this day forth, if one falls under the jurisdiction of these eighteen death-officials, simply transfer this text to the governing officers. When others recite the scriptures, the gods within the scriptures shall themselves distinguish and cause the living to ascend, while the dead shall be reborn among humans.

From the *renwu* and *xinsi* years onward, fortune and misfortune shall all depend on the recitation of this scripture.

The Dao speaks: All living beings belong to the lunar lodges—Horn, Neck, Root, Heart, Tail, Winnowing Basket, Dipper, Ox, Woman, Emptiness, Danger, House, Wall, Straddler, Harvester, Stomach, Pleiades, Net, Turtle Beak, Well, Ghost, Willow, Star, Spread, Wings, and Chariot. If a star has a name, it naturally has a retinue of ten thousand myriad attendants, pacing the roads and paths.

The Supreme August One, pitying sentient beings, has revealed all the great demon kings. From this day forth, if any household performs great merit by reciting this scripture, swiftly distinguish the departed, causing them to be reborn in heaven, where clothing and food arise spontaneously. If they remain in the Three Wretched Realms, rescue them and lead them out. If their stars have not crossed, cause them to cross. If their stars have not dimmed, cause them to dim. Should they still fail to ascend or remain severed from fate, the great demon kings shall first suffer an aeon of punishment. The Lords of the Five Paths and the Registrar of Mount Tai shall all incur guilt. Their offenses shall surely be met with penalties, and they shall not ascend as immortals.

The Dao speaks: For those who have died within twenty-one days, whether ten, five, or a hundred years have passed, merit may still be pursued on their behalf. Simply perform the ten refinements of goodness for the departed, practicing the two, five, seven, and nine virtues to establish merit and redress transgressions. If the deceased lacked a register, bestow one upon them. The *Heavenly Yellow Writ of the Mysterious* is this great scripture; to receive this single contract is to encompass all without exception.

If the living lack a great register, they may also receive the Ten Generals and reverently wear the *Heavenly Yellow Writ* contract, thereby gaining access to the Three Caverns. Bestow it upon those who come, regardless of high or low status. Why is this so?"

The Dao is like the sea—how could the sea reject filth and foulness? The great Dharma knows no bounds, and the great person makes no distinctions. When Daoists transform others, take care not to envy one another. Those who envy will have their allotted years seized by the gods and immortals.

The Dao’s methods are myriad; only the wise expand their thoughts upon them.

The Dao speaks: From this moment, in this place of refining the spirit, I command ninety million heavenly soldiers, eighty thousand warriors of the ten directions, one hundred twenty thousand immortal officials, and three thousand six hundred jade maidens—each wielding a crimson halberd—to strike down all evil ghosts under heaven, to slay those who speak wicked words, and to drive away corrupt officials and thieves. As for all those in white robes who scheme against Daoists, who seek to monopolize or encroach, who deceive these Dharma masters—each shall have their living souls seized and be executed without mercy.

When Daoists diligently transform others, the Great Demon King, the Lords of Ghosts, all governing spirits, and the gods who select officials shall pursue the documents on behalf of the deceased. If the departed are confined in the Three Bureaus, condemned to places of suffering, they shall all be reported and released, allowing them to ascend to heaven. Should they fail to remove the deceased from the Three Paths, the officers and soldiers shall be held accountable.

From this jiǎxū year onward, among the people of the world who hear the teachings of the Three Caverns, many men and women Daoists will encounter this text—all are those who have descended from heaven. Yet the foolish of the world shall not hear of it.

The Dao speaks: This *Scripture of Refining the Spirit* is the foremost among scriptures. How is this known? Within this scripture, a single character of the spirit encompasses thirty-six thousand spirits. When people perform purification rites, the spirits hear them. Forty-nine thousand spirits oversee the rites, along with eight thousand Jade Maidens of the Great Beginning and one hundred twenty thousand immortals of Mount Tai, who come to select the deceased. The deceased ascend, and the living gain blessings.

From this day forward, Daoists who uphold this Dharma, receive the essentials of the Three Caverns, and teach others to receive them shall themselves enter the ranks of immortals. From the rényǔ year onward, kings, great ministers, regional lords, and officials of two thousand *shi* who receive this scripture—all have bones destined for immortality from past lives. Immortals come to transform them, thus allowing these people to generate faith on their own and encounter great Dharma masters. How fortunate are these men and women! They shall surely ascend as immortals and never fall into the abyss.

The Dao speaks: If, after a person’s death, the living perform merit on their behalf, the deceased shall regain human form. Once human form is restored, they may ascend to heaven. After ascending to heaven, they shall return to the human realm, where clothing and food come naturally. If they dwell in the world, they shall become teachers of humanity. If they become Daoists and study the Dao, kings shall revere them as masters, and they shall not remain ordinary people. If they become kings, regional lords, officials of two thousand *shi*, or magistrates, their hearts shall constantly dwell on goodness, exhorting others to practice the Dao and personally upholding the Dharma. They shall honor the scriptures of the Three Caverns, revere their masters, and respect the gods, ever steadfast as the sun and moon. Such people shall attain great nobility in this life, passing it down through generations without end.

The upright appearance of you disciples in this life is also covered by the great Dao. Wealth and nobility, poverty and lowliness—all are decreed by the Dao. Even ugliness is but the qi of the Dao. Simply believe in the Dao with a single heart, for the Dao does not speak falsely.

Upon hearing this Dharma, the countless jade maidens in attendance rejoiced greatly, each performing the three bows and transforming to receive and uphold it on behalf of others.

The Dao speaks: When people study the Dao, the qi of the Dao runs deep. Though they may not perceive it directly, they should trust the scriptural texts, for the scriptures reveal the Dao. Without scriptures, how could the people of the world know the Dao? The scriptures are the eyes of humanity. Eyes can see far, distinguishing blue from white, good from evil, great from small. Without eyes, nothing is known—so too are the scriptures.

In studying the Dao, Daoists must first cultivate faith, for only with faith do they gain scriptures. Next, they must serve their masters, for masters guide people. The sages are profoundly distant, hidden and unseen; only masters can be followed. Only those with a predestined affinity for the Dao encounter masters, and thus come to know the Way.

When performing purification rites and practicing the Dao, recall your master in every detail. The gods, immortals, and jade maidens shall naturally assist your virtuous heart. The method of purification rites involves practicing the Dao in three periods over one day and two nights.

The Dao speaks: Long ago, there was a kingdom plagued by tigers and leopards that devoured people on the roads. At that time, a Daoist of the Three Caverns, an official of men and women, entered the mountains to gather herbs. On the way back, they encountered a traveler and asked if there were tigers on the road. The traveler, knowing tigers were present, deceived the Daoist, saying there were none. The Daoists proceeded, and the tiger transformed into a deer, showing no fear or malice toward them. The Daoists, hearing there were no tigers, rejoiced and hastened on their way. The gods protected them, knowing the traveler had deceived the Daoists. With a righteous heart, heaven naturally shielded and guarded them. Thus, the method of Daoists lies solely in establishing faith. Those who maintain faith shall naturally be supported.

There was Jiao Mai of the Southern Sea, who led eighty people into the mountains to seek immortality. They dwelled there for seven years, and each day a hundred thousand evil ghosts descended to test them. The Daoists and their assembly remained fearless, saying, “We uphold the contract of the Supreme and Boundless. How could you petty ghosts frighten us?” With unwavering faith, the ghosts departed of their own accord. The Daoists were transformed by heavenly maidens and later all ascended as immortals. Thus, Daoists need only maintain faith in their hearts.

This occurred during the reign of Empress Huì of the Western Jìn, when the Sima clan crossed the Yangtze to the south. In the jiǎzǐ year, the Six Barbarians invaded China. With no ruler in the Central Kingdom, the Sima clan moved to the land of Wú, establishing an emperor on the left bank of the Yangtze. Later, the brothers of the Golden Blade ruled as kings, bringing great joy to the realm. The people thrived, and the Four Barbarians were at peace. By the xīnsì year, the lesser Six Barbarians stirred unrest, which continued through the rényǔ and guǐwèi years, growing ever more chaotic.

In the jiǎshēn year, disaster struck—a flood rising forty *zhang*. Where no water came, great armies would instead descend, with barbarian raiders pressing southward yet causing no harm. The Nine Provinces remained untroubled.

As the era of the True Lord of the Golden Blade drew to its close, the emperor relocated his court to the land of Cháng’ān, though the earth itself rejected its people. When the time came to depart, the native-born fled first, while sojourners followed after—such was the natural course of heavenly *qi*, not the will of men.

Within the Daoist gates of the Mysterious Portal, the sovereign revered and upheld the teachings, and the Daoist arts flourished. Even the Six Barbarians submitted. With the advent of the Middle Prime, a radiant king governed, and none harbored the malice of war or blade. The displaced people gradually returned to the central capital, and the realm knew peace, gathering in perfect harmony.

These events, from the *Yǒngjiā* era of the Western Jìn to the early years of the Sòng, have now come to pass.

The Dao speaks: In the *rényǔ* and *xīnsì* years, some saw Daoists enter the mountains, cutting off grain to fast, seeking the Dao of immortality. Others saw Daoists spurn worldly glory, enduring hardship in pursuit of their masters, seeking the Dao of immortality. Still others saw Daoists forsake worldly ties, single-mindedly reciting scriptures, seeking the Dao of immortality. Some saw Daoists remain unwed, seeking the Dao of immortality. Others saw Daoists devote themselves to austerities, enduring toil and suffering, seeking the Dao of immortality. Some saw Daoists abstain from food, offering sustenance to their masters, seeking the Dao of immortality. Others saw Daoists spare no expense, commissioning vast numbers of scriptures and images, seeking the Dao of immortality. Some saw Daoists receive numerous registers and covenants, seeking the Dao of immortality. Others saw Daoists abandon their wives and refuse service to kings, seeking the Dao of immortality. Some saw Daoists daily exhorting others, seeking the Dao of immortality. Others saw Daoists constructing many oratories for purification, seeking the Dao of immortality. Some saw Daoists serve their masters without negligence, seeking the Dao of immortality. Still others saw Daoists refrain from deliberate action, seeking the Dao of immortality.

The Dao speaks: When people practice the Dao and serve their masters, some lounge or slouch before them, show no reverence upon seeing them, and deceive their masters and fellow disciples—ten such claims hold not a single truth. Such people waste your efforts, and both heaven and men will punish them, cutting short their allotted years. Serving a master should be like a minister before the Son of Heaven—how could one dare arrogance or disrespect? Even if a master appears ordinary, they are lords of spirits and gods. If you honor them, divine beings will draw near to you. If you disrespect your master, they will not await your reverence. Yet masters are protected by immortal guardian spirits, and when these spirits grow angry, they punish men. Thus, you Daoists must exercise the utmost caution.

The Dao speaks: From this time until the *xīnsì* year, red people will appear. These red people stand three *chǐ* and seven *cùn* tall, numbering three hundred million. They dwell in the waters of the Eastern Sea, and among them are Daoists who study the Way. In the Southern Sea, eight hundred thousand people stand nine *chǐ* tall, and they too will come to China to receive the Dao—though some of the time may not recognize them.

The water-dwellers reside on Crooked Mountain in the sea, with both men and women living beneath the waves. They occasionally emerge onto the Nine Bends Mountain, and many of their Daoist practitioners are exceedingly fair, unmatched anywhere in the world. Their king has three hundred consorts, all of whom receive the Daoist arts, transformed by the immortal Celestial Women of Heaven. The Three Caverns’ great scriptures have spread to the Western Sea, where people stand seventeen *chǐ* tall. They too observe the ways of husband and wife, yet their practice of the Dao differs from that of the people of China.

Wáng Fāngpíng and Mágū visit them daily to instruct the people. In this land, too, there are water-dwellers, standing sixteen *chǐ* tall, with many women and few men. Their king stands twenty-nine *chǐ* tall, with three thousand consorts, each bearing thirty-six princely sons. They do not eat the five grains, and celestial beings descend to the waters to craft palaces of gold, jade, and the seven treasures. Their bodies are clad in garments of gold, jade, and the seven treasures. Even if people of China were to encounter them, they would not recognize them. When they travel, they ride the wind and command the rain, possessing the natural *qi* of the Dao.

These water-dwellers live beneath the waters, though the waters flow above them. The great beasts of the sea are beyond the knowledge of worldly men, and there are also colossal horses and oxen as large as horses, with countless varieties—ten thousand kinds, not to be compared to a single thing. There is nothing like them in the world.

The Dao speaks: Among the people of the world, there are thirty-six kinds. Ninety thousand *lǐ* beyond the Eastern Sea lies the Red Moon-Branch Mountain, towering nine hundred million *zhàng* high. At its summit dwell beings with three heads sharing a single body, serpentine in form. They do not eat the five grains but feed on humans, insects, deer, birds, and beasts. Their bodies can fly.

Three hundred thousand *lǐ* beyond the Southern Sea stands Bamboo Mountain, rising seven hundred thousand *zhàng* high. Within it lives a one-horned person, six *zhàng* and seven *chǐ* tall, who eats insects, birds, grasses, and trees. Their speech is unintelligible.

Seventy thousand *lǐ* beyond the Western Sea, people stand five *chǐ* tall and consume stones, sand, and water. Their language is incomprehensible.

Fifty thousand *lǐ* beyond the Northern Sea lies another mountain, two hundred *zhàng* high. Atop it dwell people with one body and three faces, nine *chǐ* tall. They cannot eat grain but subsist on grasses and seeds. They know nothing of human affairs yet possess the *qi* of yin and yang, husband and wife. Their offspring resemble humans, yet they run as swiftly as flying birds, and tigers and wolves fear them.

The Dao speaks: These water-dwellers live for three thousand years before dying, while the wild people of the mountains live for three hundred years. They know nothing of the Dao and lack rites and propriety. Only the people of China understand rites and propriety.

China spans fourteen thousand *lǐ* from east to west and north to south, and its people know the law and study the great Dao. Celestial beings naturally come and go among them. No other lands possess this. The ten directions contain boundless realms—these are the wondrous lands, not the lesser ones. Only the sagely dwell there, and unless one is a Perfected Immortal of the Primordial Truth, none may journey to those places.

The Perfected Immortal of the Primordial Truth said: "What land is this, and how many *lǐ* does it span? It is second only to China."

The Celestial Worthy addressed the Most High, saying: "This is Chang’an of China. From the eastern shores to the outskirts beyond Wu and Chu in the south, from Qubing in the west to the deserts in the north—all these are encompassed within the name of China. Yet among the people of today who practice rites and the Dao, only those of the Central Plains, Wu and Chu, Shu and Han, Jianye, and Luoyang truly do so. Men and women who believe in the law find their finest exemplars in the regions of Jingchu, Jiangxia, and Nanyang’s Zhou lands. In the western lands of Congling and Liangzhou, and in the northern commanderies of Xuantu, few study the path of immortality."

The Dao states: "Among all the palaces under heaven, Duyang Palace is supreme, with Mount Wudang ranking second. China contains ninety myriad myriad palaces, each with seventy myriad lesser palaces, and within them dwell thirty million people. Among the forty-nine mountains, the foremost is Mount Duyang. It stretches twelve hundred *lǐ* from east to west, its slopes broad and level, a place of repose where the sun’s valleys lie two hundred *lǐ* deep. In ancient times, a Dharma Master journeyed there to propagate the Dao and its teachings, and the Three Caverns spread forth. Within a decade, those who responded—such as Feixian, Ji Chao, Du Xuanzhi, Xing Tongfa, Li Majin, Zhang Nu, and Liu Shizi—all ascended as masters. Zhongshan holds the dwellings of ancients, now called Xiangchuan. The younger son of King Hui of Zhou attained immortality, and his palace remains there. Many among its people have achieved transcendence, and later generations of Daoists who encounter this Dharma Master’s Three Caverns scriptures shall all attain flight as immortals. The men and women of this land in later ages will also produce many Daoists who meet sagely beings. Why is this so? The ancient immortal Dong Xuanke dwelled there, having long attained the Dao. He would appear to teach the people, and those who believed in the Dao were instructed by these immortals."

The Dao states: "In later ages, three thousand Daoists will come from the sea, their brows like a hundred phoenixes. Their palaces and halls lie in the northern mountains of the Western Regions—this was the dwelling of Fuxi’s younger brother. Fuxi originally resided on Mount Qiuchi, also in the Ox Mountain of the Western Regions. Mount Nüwa is another abode of ancient sages, located in Xiangchuan, where thirty thousand immortals dwelled during the Zhou era."

The Dao states: "Among the mountains—Yuntai, Minxuan, Mianzhu, Chishi, Longhe, and Ningshu—ancient immortals dwell in Shu, within the city of Chengdu. In the *renwu* and *xinsi* years, the Three Caverns are supreme on Fenyang Mountain, Bamin Mountain, and the Five Upper Mountains. In Baxi’s Mount Zitong, many ancient immortals reside in its forests and grottoes. Later generations of Daoists, in every lineage, are all transformations of the Jade Immortal of the Mysterious Woman, daily guided by the Dharma Masters who travel there. Traversing the ten directions, they emerge from Mount Fu, Mount Ba, and Mount Jianping, where seven hundred thousand immortals conceal themselves."

The Dao states: "In households that uphold the Dao, on the days of the Three Assemblies, one must not fail to visit one’s master. Whenever attending the Three Assemblies, each must present a *shi* of celestial tribute—no shortfall of even a *sheng* is permitted. If the granary officials investigate and find fault, misfortune will befall the household: livestock will die suddenly, undertakings will fail, and pestilence will spread across the land. When attending the Three Assemblies, offering three *liang* of incense is the customary practice. Whenever inviting a master, proper ritual propriety must be observed—nothing may be done in vain. In cases of grave illness, exceptions are made, but one must honor the master as a father, without negligence. Even if one departs for a single night, one must bow to the master; where the master stays, one stays."

"Daoists who sit at the desk to administer their duties hold no distinction of rank. When seated together for inquiry, no future misfortune remains, for the assembled spirits are not resentful. If one has received many scriptures but holds a minor position, the one with more scriptures is deemed greater. To administer major affairs without scriptural foundation is but a minor governance."

The Dao states: "Households that receive the Dao and uphold its laws must reverently offer celestial tribute, annually delivering it to the administration themselves. They must attend to this diligently, lest the master be displeased. The celestial beings will punish you, and even a single *dou* shortfall will not suffice. If the master reports to the celestial courts, the household head will suffer calamity and retribution for failing to honor the master.
