The foolishness of worldly people leads them to resent the master instead, though the master bears no fault. Every report made above will bring misfortune upon your Daoist community. The same applies to receiving the Dao and its scriptures—one must not act falsely, for even if one cannot fulfill every requirement, one must not be insincere. Many worldly people are impoverished yet unwilling to exert themselves, hoping only for empty gains. When they hear that masters impose many regulations and legal codes, none can comply, and thus they deceive both themselves and others. Daoists who aspire to the Daoist gate must rouse themselves, seek trustworthy offerings, and prepare them with a sincere heart. Only then may the master absolve them—nothing is impossible."

The Dao states: "From this time forward, the celestial yellow writs and contracts, along with the scriptures, shall be supreme. Those who no longer receive them will now attain the Yellow, Red, and Purple Palaces of this world. Those who refuse will be examined by the *qi* near them. Why is this so? The spread of the Three Caverns allows those afflicted by sudden illness to summon a Three Caverns Daoist for treatment. Bowing, burning incense, and invoking the incense fire will naturally disperse all troubles—no memorial is needed, for the celestial courts will comply. In the *renwu* and *xinsi* years, one must not refuse memorials for others. If one composes memorials for worldly people, the household head will be punished by death, and the master will also bear guilt. For each memorial composed, gather the living person’s words according to the matter at hand. Whether three masters, eight masters, five masters, or one master, face east in the upper chamber, present the memorial, pace the void, chant and recite, and then cease. The ghostly soldiers will naturally disperse and rest. Offerings of cakes, fruits, and fine foods must accompany the memorial. From now on, after presenting a memorial, bow twice upon completing the rites."

The Dao states: "When one receives registers, talismans, or contracts, from the rank of general upward, all must be provided for. One must present pledges and tokens according to the law—no leniency is permitted."

The Yellow Writ of Heaven is to be consumed by eight persons. When conducting rites at the Capital of Scriptures, twelve practitioners are required, each partaking of this as the constant norm. Worldly people, unaware, often perform rites to no avail. When Daoists perform blessings, the sun and moon oversee them—fasting and lecturing take precedence, with reverence for the master held in the heart. Should one act improperly even for a day, showing disrespect to the master, the master’s neglect will not endure past the first day of the month. On the fifteenth day, when paying homage to the scriptures, one must bow to the ten directions and also to the master. To take even one false step incurs thirty-six trials per step, with each sin consigning one to the Inexhaustible Hell, from which escape is impossible, and ascension to the Dao forever forfeit.

The Dao states: "From now on, in the years *xinsi* and *renwu*, the Three Caverns shall spread and disseminate throughout the world. The people of the world shall no longer submit memorials. Many men and women will uphold the scriptures and enter the mountains, with women often receiving the teachings—transformed by heavenly maidens. After the passing of *jiashen*, the Dao’s *qi* will flourish, the Six Barbarians will submit in faith, and all immortals will share the same dharma as one family. From the year *renwu* onward, Daoists shall don the three ritual garments: the cap, brown robe, skirt, mantle, staff, and sandals. They shall eat once daily, fasting past noon, abstaining from all meat and wine, and never tasting them. They shall instruct the laity, ensuring no transgressions of the law. Men and women may transmit the teachings, with the wise serving as masters. They shall not raise livestock, for the proper cultivation of life pertains to the self alone. The study of scriptures is their vocation. Those who enter the mountains shall observe monthly fasts, subsisting on vegetables alone. When ten, thirty, or a hundred enter the mountains together, they shall cultivate fields extensively, plant gardens, grow the five vegetables, and construct dwellings on all sides, along with fasting halls and pavilions. No one, two, or three shall dwell alone. Ghosts and spirits deceive the solitary—scriptural dharma cannot be practiced in isolation. In fasting halls with many people, three fasts shall be held monthly, and incense offered thrice daily to bow to the ten directions. Thus do the gods draw near to humanity. If one or two dwell alone in the mountains without establishing rites or building fasting halls, they are no different from beasts or deer in the wild. What distinction is there? One must follow an enlightened master, one rich in skills and scriptural knowledge, for the ascent of even one is auspicious—how much more so for many. Thus, fewer than ten should not reside together, let alone two or five. Such people do not submit to the mountain spirits; the mountain spirits deceive them, and they shall know no fortune."

The Dao states: "When one receives the Yellow Writ and scriptures, they endure long. If one does not follow the master’s transmission, trials will come daily. Illness will afflict them, silkworms and fields will wither, households will suffer misfortune, lifespans will not reach their term, and they will die prematurely. Moreover, one cannot return the master’s talismans and contracts, for the spirits have already entered the body’s organs, causing illness. If one follows the dharma and is transmitted by three masters, no harm shall befall. For Daoists, the mastery of scriptures is paramount—the foundation of ascension to immortality. Thus, among all masters, the scripture master is supreme. Immortals and jade maidens all revere the scripture master. Talismans and contracts are foremost. A Daoist who does not receive all talismans and contracts is no Daoist. One who does not uphold the Three Caverns is no Daoist. To receive only the inner and outer Yellow, Red, and Purple Registers is to be but a minor Daoist. One must receive the *Five Thousand Character Scripture*, the upper talismans, and all related matters to attain the rank of upper immortal."

The Dao states: "When Daoists enter the mountains, they shall honor their masters as they would in the world. If a master dies, they shall visit the grave, bury them with rites, and dress them with proper garments and sashes. They shall weep for seven days and then hold a fast. The fast shall be observed once every seven days for three weeks, then cease. If a disciple dies, the master shall likewise attend to them according to the dharma, without slaughtering animals for offerings—seasonal cakes and fruits suffice. For later generations of Daoists, follow the scriptures in all matters. Those who do not shall become heavenly beings, never to die. All other possessions may be given away."

The Dao states: "In later ages, those who master the Three Caverns and encounter this *Scripture of Flying Immortals* shall behold the image of the Most High Lord. Those unable to enter the mountains may instead dwell in distant forests or hills, far from worldly people—ten or five *li* apart. They shall plant abundant vegetable gardens, orchards, and fields. Monthly fasts shall be observed without fail, converting and instructing the foolish to uphold the Three Treasures. Masters, regardless of rank, are honored as noble. Formerly, Luo He, at ninety-eight years, bowed thrice daily to his sixteen-year-old master, attending him with reverence and never showing disrespect. Worldly people, seeing this, sighed: ‘This old man, his temples graying, bows to this young boy!’ Yet the heavenly beings and jade maidens said: ‘This is the elder’s master from a past life. Though young, his wisdom runs deep.’"

The Dao states: "The bond between master and disciple is a profound connection from past lives, akin to that of father and son. All are drawn together from former existences, having sworn oaths across kalpas—this intimacy is not merely of the present. Those bound by evil karma are likewise entangled. If rulers, great ministers, governors, or officials of two thousand bushels now study immortality with these Daoists, it is due to good karma from past lives. Without such deep connections, they could not become masters, disciples, or spiritual kin. Today’s wisdom, love of scriptures, and devotion to study all stem from long practice in past lives. The master-disciple bond is the same, forged over countless ages. They swore to be master and friend, and upon encountering this scripture, now receive it. Those who receive it wisely do so because they studied it in past lives. Though unaware of worldly affairs, they are called wise—this is clear, for their devotion has endured long."

The Dao states: "In later ages, epidemics and ghostly soldiers will multiply, slaying people."

The Daoist may instruct people to observe fasts on the eight seasonal days, with an entire village participating together—doing abundant good. These are: the days of *Lichun*, *Chunfen*, *Lixia*, *Xiazhi*, *Liqiu*, *Qiufen*, *Lidong*, and *Dongzhi*, as well as the fifteenth day of the first, seventh, and tenth months—these are the great fast days. On these days, the Daoist conducts the fast according to the grand ritual. For those studying the Dao of immortality, reciting scriptures and performing the Daoist rites for three days and three nights brings boundless merit. In the Daoist method, unless they are master and disciple, the elder is called "elder brother" and the younger "younger brother"; they may not be addressed as □ or servant. Ghosts kill people—Daoists must be cautious of this.

Those who wish to observe the eight seasonal fasts should choose a place by wild waters, on an island or islet, a pure and secluded site—this is the first offering to the *Xun* direction. The Dao states: "From the *Renwu* year onward, memorials were submitted again, but the worldly *huangshu* contracts and decrees were no longer received; what the Heavenly Maidens received came without gate or barrier. From now until the *Guiwei* year, after *Jiashen* has passed, the *huangshu* contracts and decrees will no longer be consulted; only this world’s *huangshu* will remain. Those who formally receive the worldly *huangshu* will not ascend as immortals. If men or women have not previously held immortal registers, they may receive the *huangshu* contracts and decrees of the heavens by obtaining at least ten divine youths and one general. If three masters or even one master initiates them, they too become great Daoists and may receive the scriptures and contracts. The people of the world, unaware of the approaching great flood, refuse to accept the Dao—when the time of great disaster comes, they will suddenly perish. Alas, what can be done? If they cannot receive many texts, receiving the *Five Thousand Character Scripture* or the *Scripture of Transforming the Barbarians* is also good."

The Dao states: "From now until the *Renwu* and *Xinsi* years, there will be many women Daoists who receive the Three Caverns. Those entering the mountains will also be mostly female Daoists, while men will be few. The Mysterious Woman often descends, transforming into a young girl to receive disciples in the world. After *Jiashen*, all men and women aged thirteen and above will receive the ten generals, divine youths, and the heavenly *huangshu* contracts and decrees. Why? Because the world will increasingly believe in the Dao."

Magu, Du Lanxiang, An Qisheng, and Tang Gongfang—all these transformed beings—have each received Daoist teachings, with every school possessing them. Scriptures are supreme, and rituals and lectures abound day and night. In the lands east of the Yangtze, Wu and Chu, as well as in the Shu commanderies of Han and Qin, many practice the Dao.

The Dao states: "As the Three Caverns emerge into the world, immortals descend daily. Daoist men and women must diligently study scriptures and contracts, receive many talismans and registers, wholeheartedly believe in goodness, contemplate their masters’ virtues, and make offerings to Daoists. Daoists know no rank—when summoned to dispel misfortune, incense and fire must not be neglected even for a single day. Daoists have their own officers and soldiers for protection, and these must not be disobeyed even for a moment. The officers and soldiers report human transgressions, and heavenly envoys punish those who defy them. At night, the officers within one’s body depart and execute judgment upon the person, causing illness. Prolonged affliction weakens the body. All manner of inauspicious dreams are the work of these officers.

Once, a female official was summoned to dispel misfortune. She deceived the petitioner, saying, 'Today, the officers within me are in conflict; I cannot perform the rite or dispel your misfortune.' For this deception, two months later, the female official began to hemorrhage and suffered for three years without recovery. A diviner declared, 'You bear a great sin; the heavenly courts are punishing you.' The female official reflected and realized this must be the consequence of her deception. She invited Daoists to perform rituals and repented for a month before recovering.

The Dao states: 'From now on, admonish future generations: when you receive the Dao, husband and wife must do so together; neither may receive alone. When receiving the *Yellow Writs*, the Three Masters must transmit them, and the Dao must confer the *Yellow Contracts*. Those who fail this will suffer bodily punishment and will not regain human form in future lives—how much less attain immortality? Deceiving others is also forbidden. Those who follow the Dao but neglect incense and fire will surely face punishment, which will extend to their descendants.'

Once, two neighboring households both received the *Great Contracts of the Yellow Writs* for inner and outer realms. One household had the Three Masters transmit the teachings, practiced the Dao daily, and had Daoists dispel misfortune. Every matter proceeded favorably, never against their wishes. Husband and wife ascended as immortals, protected by heavenly beings. The other household, though they received the teachings, did not undergo transmission by the Three Masters. They copied texts themselves and ceased practicing the Dao. They did not live out their allotted years, and within two years, their entire clan was destroyed—heavenly beings executed them. Those who receive the Dao must follow every word of the scriptures.

The Dao states: 'People of the world are often foolish. When husband and wife together follow the Dao, jealousy disrupts their practice, preventing them from cultivating the Way. The qi of the Dao and its officers and soldiers grow angry. After death, they enter the *Fire Cart* and *Eight Winds* hells, where they die and are reborn three times a day for seventy thousand kalpas, never regaining human form. Even if they are reborn as humans, they will have human shape but lack human nature—deaf, mute, covered in sores, convulsing, hideous in appearance, their bodies foul and odorous. Others shun them. Daoists, with compassionate hearts, transform people to avoid such corruption. Daoists wear hempen robes and eat plain food, transcribe scriptures, study diligently, and serve their masters. Teach future generations—male and female Daoists—reflect deeply on this.'

The Dao states: 'The Dao’s teachings are hard to encounter; few do so. Those who encounter them in later ages must revere and uphold them, sparing no wealth. Daoists, as teachers to others, should not greedily take people’s property. Daoists who wish to wear talismans and aspire to immortality must not be stingy. They should forsake wives and children, and not covet livestock or horses. In the past, there were those who gave away wives and children or sold them to receive scriptures—more than one such person. From ancient times to now, only one or two have truly believed in the Dao.'

The Dao states: 'The *Great Scriptures of the Three Caverns* are the highest of scriptures, yet they do not surpass the *Scripture of Flying Immortals*. Why? The *Scripture of Flying Immortals* was expounded by the Supreme of the Ten Directions’ Great Dao and all immortals and jade maidens who roam and transform the world. It is guarded by countless divine beings, soldiers, and horses. Those who receive it are protected by immortals, and nothing is inauspicious. In the *Xinsi* and *Renwu* years to come, this scripture will spread throughout the world. People will lecture and recite it more than other scriptures. Daoists, through fasting and abstinence, will widely transmit this scripture, for it enables one to become a flying immortal. The Three Caverns allow for many paths—corpse-liberation immortals and earthbound immortals—but this scripture has only flying immortals. This scripture, in twenty scrolls, is revered by heavenly beings, jade maidens, and immortals of the ten directions.'

The Dao states: 'From now until the *Renwu* and *Xinsi* years, Daoists must urgently convert the world to receive the Dao. Great disasters are imminent; heaven will release epidemic qi, and pestilence will spread, killing many wicked people. Those who perform meritorious deeds will be spared by ghostly soldiers. When the time of the water disaster arrives in those years, Daoists should urge people to build shelters, receive and uphold the true scriptures of the Three Caverns. With the scriptures and contracts upon them, the officers and divine warriors will naturally ward off evil. The waters will come soon, in the *Jiashen* year. If not then, there will be disasters of blades and warfare, and the people will be in turmoil. After the *Jiashen* year, the great flood will sweep everything away. At that time, heaven and earth will be renewed—this world will be no more.

The Dao states: 'The world is full of wicked people, so the Three Caverns are not widely disseminated. Sentient beings are pitiable, flowing with the mud, and ghostly soldiers execute them. Alas, what can be done? For three days and nights, the Supreme and Wen Shi remained in the Mysterious Capital, contemplating how to deliver sentient beings from life and death. They entered the Golden Casket and retrieved the *Supreme Scripture of the Great Void* and the *Scripture of Flying Immortals* in twenty scrolls, entrusting them to the Grand Dharma Master to transmit to the people of the world.'"

The Dao states: From this *Renwu* and *Xinsi* year onward, Daoist priests will frequently encounter these *Scriptures of Flying Immortals* and *Scriptures of the Great Void*. Shen Zhi of Shangdang, surnamed Chuwen, shall obtain these scriptures and ascend as an immortal of the highest rank. Among women, two hundred sixty thousand shall receive these scriptures and enter the mountains.

The Dao states: From this time forth, if one encounters such a master who imparts these scriptures, the flying immortals of the ten directions, the immortals of the Five Sacred Peaks, the Jade Maidens, the Boundless Venerable Ones, and all the Mysterious Women shall come together to protect those who receive the scriptures. Wherever this Dharma Master resides, the world shall be in great harmony, the five grains shall flourish, the people shall live in peace and joy, the emperor shall enjoy long life, and heavenly beings shall descend daily to instruct and assist the ruler in governing the realm.

The Dao states: Such are the merits of the Daoist priest. If the ruler, great ministers, regional lords, or officials of the two thousand *shi* ranks also uphold and receive these teachings, their positions shall be boundless, and heavenly beings shall naturally guard and protect them. Until the end of their days, they shall be kept from evil.

All those present who heard the Most High expound this scripture were overjoyed, each receiving the transformation. They bowed their heads in reverence, paid homage, and took refuge in the Three Treasures.

Here ends the twentieth scroll of the *Most High Scripture of the Abyssal Divine Incantations*.
